1001 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Swibaker v. Board of Trustees


No. 4-85-0009


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


140 Ill. App. 3d 550; 488 N.E.2d 1052; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 1744; 94 Ill. Dec. 805



January 21, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of McLean County; the Hon. James A. Knecht, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant firemen's pension fund sought review of an order from the Circuit Court of McLean County (Illinois), which granted a declaratory judgment to plaintiff fireman and permitted the fireman to convert his pension to one based on the salary of his last position.


OVERVIEW: The fireman, who had attained the rank of captain, began receiving disability benefits. After a 1982 amendment to the retirement provisions of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 108 1/2, para. 4-113 was enacted, the fireman filed an action seeking a declaratory judgment that he was permitted to a retirement pension based on the salary attached to his captain's rank at the time of his retirement. The trial court found that the fireman had not permanently retired from the fire department as of the legislative amendment's enactment date and that he was entitled to a retirement pension based on the salary attached to the rank of captain at the time of his permanent retirement. The firemen's pension fund sought review and argued that under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 108 1/2, para. 1-103.1 (1983), the amendment to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 108 1/2, para. 4-113 did not apply to the fireman. The court found that under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 108 1/2, para. 113(b) (Supp. 1984), the fireman was considered in service even though he was receiving disability benefits, that the 1982 amendment and a subsequent 1985 amendment were applicable to active service firefighters, and that the amendments applied to the fireman.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's declaratory judgment.

 

1002 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Illinois Municipal League v. Illinois State Labor Relations Bd.


No. 4-85-0179


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


140 Ill. App. 3d 592; 488 N.E.2d 1040; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 1748; 94 Ill. Dec. 793; 122 L.R.R.M. 3296



January 21, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Sangamon County; the Hon. Simon L. Friedman, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, association of municipalitie, sought review of an order of the Circuit Court of Sangamon County (Illinois), which dismissed plaintiff's complaint against defendant Illinois State Labor Board that requested declaratory and injunctive relief establishing the unconstitutionality of the Illinois Public Labor Relations Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 48, para. 1601 et seq. (1984), under state and federal law.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff, association of municipalities, brought an action against defendant Illinois State Labor Board requesting declaratory and injunctive relief establishing that the Illinois Public Labor Relations Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 48, para. 1601 et seq. (1984), violated the state and federal constitutions. Among other things, plaintiffs asserted that § 1603(g) of the Act improperly required the payment of money to unions by municipal employees, denying their freedom of association and depriving them of property without due process, and that § 1617(a) of the Act recognizing municipal employees' right to strike encouraged the employees to abandon the statutory and constitutional duties they owed to the public. The circuit court entered an order dismissing the action. On appeal, the court affirmed the order. The court held that plaintiff's claims concerning monetary payments by employees alleged only the possibility of a future controversy in which plaintiff and its members had no recognizable interest to support standing to bring suit. The court held that plaintiff's claims regarding potential injuries caused by striking employees were not ripe for adjudication.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the declaratory judgment action brought by plaintiff, association of municipalities, against defendant Illinois State Labor Board challenging the constitutionality of the Illinois Public Labor Relations Act. The court held that plaintiff lacked standing to assert claims of municipal employees and that claims regarding possible injuries caused by striking municipal employees were not ripe for adjudication.

 

1003 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Searle Pharmaceuticals, Inc. v. Department of Revenue


No. 84-2036


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth District


140 Ill. App. 3d 248; 488 N.E.2d 661; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 1862; 94 Ill. Dec. 662



January 16, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Earl Arkiss, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant parent-subsidiary taxpayers challenged the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which upheld an administrative decision that denied its claim for refund and upheld the constitutionality of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 2-203(e)(2)(E) (1983).


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers, which voluntarily filed a consolidated tax return under 26 U.S.C.S. § 1501 (1984), filed an amended Illinois tax return seeking a refund arising from carrying back a net operating loss. The state denied the refund, and the taxpayers sought review, challenging the constitutionality of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 2-203(e)(2)(E) (1983) as a denial of equal protection and uniformity of treatment. The trial court upheld the statute. On further appeal, the court affirmed, holding that in the case of a corporation which was a member of an affiliated group of corporations filing a consolidated income tax return for the taxable year for federal income tax purposes, taxable income was determined as if such corporation had filed a separate return for federal income tax purposes for the taxable year and each preceding taxable year for which it was a member of an affiliated group. The court noted that the granting of a deduction for net operating losses was a privilege created by statute as a matter of legislative grace.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court.

 

1004 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Boastick


No. 4-85-0241


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


140 Ill. App. 3d 78; 488 N.E.2d 326; 488 N.E.2d 672; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 1844; 94 Ill. Dec. 500



January 16, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Champaign County; the Hon. Harold L. Jensen, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, and vacated in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision of the Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois), which convicted him of aggravated criminal sexual assault, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38 para. 12-14(b)(1) (1984 Supp.), and aggravated criminal sexual abuse, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 12-16(c)(1) (1984 Supp.).


OVERVIEW: The trial court convicted defendant of aggravated criminal sexual assault, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38 para. 12-14(b)(1) (1984 Supp.), and aggravated criminal sexual abuse, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 12-16(c)(1) (1984 Supp.) upon his stepdaughter. On appeal, defendant claimed, inter alia, that the state failed to prove beyond a reasonable doubt one of the assault offenses and one of the abuse offenses. The court affirmed all convictions and all sentences except one sentence on one of the abuse convictions. The court held that if the evidence was sufficient to support any count charging a particular offense, the evidence supported a verdict convicting of that offense. The court found that the evidence supported the conviction of the offense of abuse, but it held that inadvertent error resulted in an inappropriate sentence on a count where the evidence failed. The appropriate remedy was to vacate the sentence imposed on that verdict and remand for resentencing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed all but one of defendant's convictions; it vacated the conviction for aggravated criminal sexual abuse that covered the period of July to November, 1984. The case was remanded for resentencing.

 

1005 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Swearingen


No. 4-85-0173


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


140 Ill. App. 3d 93; 488 N.E.2d 324; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 1846; 94 Ill. Dec. 498



January 13, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Macon County; the Hon. Donald W. Morthland, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision by the Circuit Court of Macon County (Illinois), which dismissed his pro se petition for post-conviction relief.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of rape, deviate sexual assault, and armed violence. On direct appeal, the appellate court affirmed defendant's convictions of rape and deviate sexual assault and reversed his armed violence conviction. Defendant filed an amended pro se petition for post-conviction relief. The trial court dismissed the petition pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 122-2.1 (1984 Supp.). Upon appeal, the court affirmed, holding that when defendant filed his amended petition, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, paras. 122-2.1(a), 122-4 (1984 Supp.) was in effect. This statute allowed the trial court to dismiss the petition without appointing counsel if the petition was frivolous or patently without merit. The court found that the two post-conviction petitions were separate petitions and, as such, subject to the applicable statutory provision which was in effect at the time each petition was filed. The court found the petition to have been frivolous or patently without merit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of defendant's petition for post-conviction relief.

 

1006 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Potter


Nos. 3-84-0786, 3-84-0787, 3-84-0788, 3-84-0789 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


140 Ill. App. 3d 693; 489 N.E.2d 334; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 1763; 95 Ill. Dec. 113



January 9, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Bureau County; the Hon. Richard R. Wilder, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff State of Illinois appealed the orders of the Circuit Court, Bureau County (Illinois), which granted the motions to suppress evidence by defendants on charges of theft by deception.


OVERVIEW: The police obtained information that defendants, who were used car dealers, were selling used cars with altered odometers. The State's attorney advised the police that there was insufficient evidence to obtain search warrants. The police then conducted administrative searches of the records of defendants of well over 24 hours each and obtained evidence against them but found no evidence of any stolen parts or cars. The trial court granted defendants' motions to suppress, and the State appealed. The court found that the purpose of the searches were criminal in nature and not administrative. The court also found that the statute, Ill. Veh. Code § 5-403, did not authorize administrative searches for altered odometers. The court also found that there was no good faith exception to administrative searches.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the orders of the trial court.

 

1007 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Ziegler


No. 3-85-0240


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


139 Ill. App. 3d 1088; 488 N.E.2d 310; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 1835; 94 Ill. Dec. 484



January 3, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Tazewell County; the Hon. Ivan L. Yontz, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court of Tazewell County (Illinois), which determined that a mail order business operated by defendants was a public nuisance as defined by section 3(b) of the Drug Paraphernalia Control Act (Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, para. 2103(b) (1983). The circuit court denied their motions challenging the constitutionality of the statute and the validity of a search of their premises.


OVERVIEW: Defendants reported a burglary at their premises. Upon arrival, the police observed drug paraphernalia. A search warrant was issued and numerous exhibits were seized. The State's Attorney obtained an injunction from the circuit court that declared defendants' enterprise a public nuisance as defined in section 3 of the Drug Paraphernalia Control Act and denied defendants' motions challenging the statute and the search. On appeal, the court modified, but affirmed the judgment. The court held that the standard employed in the statute was sufficiently specific to inform a reasonably prudent business person what conduct was proscribed and what was permitted. The circuit court was justified in its conclusion that the items being sold by defendants were, with a few exceptions, primarily associated with illegal drugs. Defendants' disclaimers that recited that the products were intended only for use with tobacco and legal smoking herbs were not persuasive. The State's Attorney provided evidence as to the illegal use of virtually every item in defendants' inventory, and to suggest that only legal uses were intended defied any reasonable probability.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that enjoined defendants' drug paraphernalia mail order business as a nuisance. Because cigarette rolling papers were not paraphernalia by statute, the court modified the judgment to eliminate this item.

 

1008 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Illinois Housing Dev. Authority v. La Salle Nat'l Bank


No. 84-0828


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


139 Ill. App. 3d 985; 487 N.E.2d 772; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 2917; 94 Ill. Dec. 15



December 31, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County; the Hon. Anthony M. Peccarelli, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a corporate trustee and a beneficiary, sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), which entered a judgment of foreclosure in favor of plaintiff Illinois Housing Development Authority (IHDA) and which held that the trustee, pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 12-125 (1983), had waived its redemption right in a mortgage between the trustee and IHDA.


OVERVIEW: A trust agreement, which waived the trustee's redemption right pursuant to § 12-125, was executed between the trustee and the beneficiary, and a mortgage was executed between the trustee and IHDA. Subsequently, IHDA filed a foreclosure action against the trustee and the beneficiary, and the trial court entered a foreclosure judgment, finding that the trustee was required to waive its redemption right. Thereafter, an appeal was filed, but because a stay was not obtained, the foreclosed property was sold to the company as trustee with the partnership as beneficiary. On appeal, IHDA claimed that in the absence of a stay, the appeal was moot under Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 305(i) because the property had been sold to a third party. However, after determining that a partnership was a nominee of its partners and was not protected as a stranger to a partner's litigation, the court held it could not dismiss the appeal as moot because it could not determine if IHDA was a partner. The court also held that because the mortgage did not contain a waiver and because the mortgage and the trust agreement were between different parties, the trustee had not waived its redemption right under the mortgage.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded.

 

1009 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Wilson


No. 83-0773


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


139 Ill. App. 3d 726; 487 N.E.2d 1015; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 2885; 94 Ill. Dec. 138



December 20, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. John J. Crowley, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of armed robbery and murder and sentenced him to 30 years of imprisonment. He appealed his convictions and his sentence on various grounds, including the refusal of the circuit court to ask on voir dire whether the prospective jurors understood that defendant was not required to testify in his own behalf.


OVERVIEW: Defense counsel tendered a list of questions for which he sought inclusion in the voir dire examination. One question concerned defendant's right not to testify. The circuit court refused the question, stating that the jurors would be instructed that defendant need not testify at trial. Defense counsel filed a motion for a mistrial, which the circuit court denied. The question was excluded. On appeal, the court noted that the Illinois Supreme Court stated that the understanding of the prospective jurors on the state's burden of proof, the presumption of innocence, and the defendant's right not to testify should have been covered in the course of interrogation on voir dire. The refusal to ask questions on the issues resulted in prejudicial error that required reversal of the judgment. The supreme court added that if a juror had a prejudice against the basic guarantees, an instruction given at the end of the trial would have little curative effect. On appeal, the court noted that the holding of the supreme court would be applied retrospectively. The court reversed the judgment of the circuit court and remanded the cause for a new trial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the circuit court, vacated the sentences of defendant, and remanded the cause for a new trial. The trial court committed reversible error in refusing to ask prospective jurors whether they understood that defendant was not required to testify in his own behalf and whether they would hold it against him or draw any negative inferences from his failure to do so.

 

1010 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


In re Marriage of Savas


Nos. 83-1245, 83-2859, 83-2928, 84-2501 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


139 Ill. App. 3d 68; 486 N.E.2d 1318; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 2795; 93 Ill. Dec. 483



December 6, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Michael S. Jordan, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, affirmed as modified in part and dismissed in part in 83 -- 1245; Judgment vacated in 83 -- 2859; Judgments reversed in 83 -- 2928 and 84 -- 2501.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner wife filed for dissolution of the marriage between her and respondent husband. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) entered a dissolution order and two judgments concerning attorney fees. The trial court also entered an order of protection for the wife and attorney fees and another order for prospective attorney fees for the defense of the appeal of the protective order. The husband appealed all of the orders.


OVERVIEW: The first and second petitions for dissolution of the marriage were dismissed for want of prosecution. However, the case was scheduled for trial and was tried without objection. The trial court entered an order for the dissolution of the marriage, a protective order, and attorney fees. On appeal, the court affirmed in part and reversed in part. The husband contended that the trial court lacked jurisdiction to adjudicate the dissolution and the trial court's subsequent orders. The court concluded that although the failure to vacate the dismissal formally and as directed could not be condoned, the revesting doctrine was appropriate and equitable. The husband contended that the trial court was without "authority" to award the wife prospective attorney fees to defend the appeal. The court held that the trial court had authority to award prospective fees because the orders that granted prospective fees for the appeal were both subsequent in time and collateral in nature to the judgments from which the appeal was taken. However, the record failed to sufficiently show the husband's financial ability to pay the fees. Therefore, the award for fees to defend the appeals was reversed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment for dissolution of marriage and award of the wife's attorney fees. The award of fees to the husband's former attorneys was reduced and affirmed as modified. The contention of erroneous dismissal of the husband's counter claim was dismissed. The court vacated the appeal of the protective order. The court reversed the award of prospective attorney fees to defend the pending appeal.

 

1011 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Mulhern v. Talk of the Town


No. 84-0274


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


138 Ill. App. 3d 829; 486 N.E.2d 383; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 2752; 93 Ill. Dec. 282



December 4, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County; the Hon. John J. Bowman, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a personal injury action, both parties sought review of an order by the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois) in favor of plaintiff injured party. The injured party's car collided with the car of a driver, who had consumed alcohol as a customer of the bar. The trial court remitted the verdict to the statutory Dramshop Act limit. The bar appealed the adverse judgment, and the injured party cross-appealed the statutory remittitur.


OVERVIEW: The injured party alleged that the bar operated a dramshop and served the driver alcoholic beverages which caused her intoxication. The complaint further alleged that the driver operated her car and struck the car in which the injured party was a passenger. The bar requested that the trial court prohibit the injured party from introducing or referring to blood alcohol test results of the driver taken at a hospital. The trial court concluded that the blood test certification requirements of the Illinois Vehicle Code were not applicable to the case because the driver was not arrested. The court concluded the trial court did not err in allowing admission of the test results. The court did not decide whether the driver's consent to the blood test was required where she was never arrested because the bar did not establish that the driver did not consent to the test. Because of the inadequacy of the record on the issue of consent, the bar waived its argument that the blood test results were inadmissible because the driver did not consent. The court also concluded that the statutory liability limitations imposed by the Dramshop Act were constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1012 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Morrison


No. 2-84-0623


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


138 Ill. App. 3d 595; 486 N.E.2d 345; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 2722; 93 Ill. Dec. 244



November 26, 1985, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied December 31, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County; the Hon. Robert J. French, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order by the Circuit Court of Winnebago County (Illinois), which convicted defendant under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, par. 11-20(a)(1) (1983) of obscenity regarding the sale of an allegedly obscene magazine. Defendant was sentenced to conditional discharge for a period of 12 months and assessed a fine. Defendant filed a timely notice of appeal.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant contended that the Illinois obscenity statute was unconstitutionally vague, indefinite, and uncertain, that one of the State's jury instructions incorrectly stated the law of obscenity, and that the prosecutor's remarks to the jury, in particular his repeated references to the jurors as members of the community of Illinois, misled the jury and prejudiced its deliberation. At defendant's trial a police detective testified that he entered an adult bookstore where defendant was behind the counter. The detective related that within the bookstore there were numerous magazines, all depicting sexually explicit activities on both the front and back covers. The court concluded that the obscenity statute was constitutional. The jury instruction informed the jurors that all three elements in the tripartite test for obscenity had to be present in the material under review for that material to be deemed "obscene." The court found that the prosecutor's remarks were not an attempt to influence the jurors into applying what they considered to be the community standard of the county to the materials in question and did not prejudice defendant's conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1013 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Pope


No. 2-84-1067


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


138 Ill. App. 3d 726; 486 N.E.2d 350; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 2739; 93 Ill. Dec. 249



November 26, 1985, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied December 31, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County; the Hon. Robert J. French, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, and reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment and sentence by the Circuit Court of Winnebago County (Illinois) that convicted defendant of three counts of obscenity under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 11-20(a)(1) (1983), based on the sale of allegedly obscene magazines at a book store and sentenced defendant to concurrent sentences on each of the counts as well as consecutive fines on each count.


OVERVIEW: The defendant claimed that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 11-20 (1983), was unconstitutionally vague, indefinite, uncertain, and overbroad; that the information was legally insufficient; the trial court abused its discretion by limiting defendant's voir dire examination; the trial court erred in admitting certain photographs into evidence; hat defendant was not proved guilty beyond a reasonable doubt; and the trial court abused its discretion in sentencing the defendant. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment convicting the defendant of obscenity, vacated the defendant's sentence, and remanded to the trial court for resentencing, holding that the prosecution proved sufficient evidence to show that the defendant knew he was selling obscene magazines, which violated the obscenity statute, which was not vague or overbroad. The court further held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in limiting the defendant's voir dire and allowing the photos into evidence. The court further held that the trial court failed to state the facts upon which the defendant was sentenced, rather than granted probation, which abused the trial court's discretion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that convicted the defendant of obscenity based on his sale of magazines, vacated the defendant's sentence that required him to serve time rather than probation, and remanded to the trial court for resentencing.

 

1014 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Boles Trucking, Inc. v. O'Connor


No. 4-85-0176


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


138 Ill. App. 3d 764; 486 N.E.2d 362; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 2744; 93 Ill. Dec. 261



November 26, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Sangamon County; the Hon. Richard E. Mann, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, intrastate truckers, appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court of Sangamon County (Illinois) in favor of defendants, members of the Illinois Commerce Commission, in the truckers' complaint challenging the civil penalty provision of §18-702 of the Illinois Motor Carrier of Property Law (Law), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 18-702 (1983), and seeking declaratory relief. The members cross-appealed a denial of their motion to dismiss.


OVERVIEW: The Illinois Commerce Commission issued citation orders to show cause why civil penalties should not be imposed against the intrastate truckers, pursuant to § 18-702, and the truckers sought declaratory relief by challenging that provision. The trial court denied the members' motion to dismiss and entered a judgment in favor of the members, presumably upholding the constitutionality of § 18-702. The court affirmed in part and reversed in part. The court held that: 1) the cross-appeal was dismissed because the denial of a motion to dismiss was unappealable; 2) the truckers alleged an actual controversy capable of a definitive determination of the rights of the parties because of the issued citation orders; 3) the civil penalty provision of § 18-702 was a valid delegation of authority for Law violations; 4) the commission's rule of practice regarding evidence was invalid to the extent that it conflicted with § 60 of the Public Utilities Act (PUA), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111 2/3, para. 64 (1983), which provided that commission proceedings were not governed by the technical rules of evidence, and 5) the attorney general was to prosecute the violations for the state.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part the trial court's judgment in favor of the members. The court declared that the commission was authorized to impose civil penalties under the Illinois Motor Carrier of Property Law; that such proceedings were governed by the PUA and a related commission rule was invalid to the extent that it conflicted with the PUA; and that the attorney general represented the state in the proceedings.

 

1015 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Seidel


No. 3-85-0191


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


138 Ill. App. 3d 616; 485 N.E.2d 1330; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 2725; 93 Ill. Dec. 120



November 22, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Whiteside County; the Hon. L. E. Ellison, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision of the Circuit Court of Whiteside County (Illinois), which convicted him of unlawful possession of cannabis with intent to deliver based on defendant's blind plea.


OVERVIEW: Defendant entered a blind plea of guilty to one count of unlawful possession of more than 500 grams of cannabis with intent to deliver. The trial court sentenced defendant to 7 years of imprisonment and the payment of a fine. The trial court denied defendant's motion to withdraw his guilty plea. On review, defendant argued that his guilty plea was improperly induced by the State's threats to prosecute his grandparents for his offense. The court found that there was nothing in the record to indicate that defendant's guilty plea was anything but voluntary. Furthermore, defendant's grandparents were also charged with the same crime and defendant's grandfather admitted that he was the only person who had a key to the room where the cannabis was found. The court found that the trial court properly exercised its discretion in denying defendant's motion to withdraw his guilty plea. The court also found that defendant was entitled to a $ 5.00 per day credit against his fine because his case was a bailable offense and he did not post bail. Therefore, the trial court's decision was modified regarding the fine and otherwise affirmed.


OUTCOME: The trial court's decision that convicted defendant of unlawful possession of cannabis with intent to deliver and assessed a fine was modified to show a $ 5.00 per day credit against the fine for the time he was in jail and in all other regards was affirmed.

 

1016 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Hazen v. County of Peoria


No. 3-85-0216


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


138 Ill. App. 3d 836; 485 N.E.2d 1325; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 2753; 93 Ill. Dec. 115



November 22, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Peoria County; the Hon. Robert E. Manning, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a county veterans assistance commission (VAC) and its superintendent, appealed an order of the Circuit Court of Peoria County (Illinois) denying them a writ of mandamus against defendant county board and granting defendant county an injunction compelling plaintiffs to comply with the rules and regulations of the Department of Public Aid. Defendants cross-appealed from orders requiring the county to pay plaintiffs' attorney fees.


OVERVIEW: The board directed the VAC to comply with rules and regulations of the Department so that the remainder of funds needed for relief of indigent veterans could be obtained from the State. The superintendent and the VAC filed a petition for mandamus and injunctions to compel the board to levy the full amount of funds requested by the VAC. On appeal, plaintiffs contended that the trial court erred in refusing to issue a writ of mandamus to compel the board to provide the funds under the Bogardus Act and that the injunction requiring the VAC to comply with the rules and regulations of the Department was improper. The court found that a writ of mandamus could not be used to review the sufficiency of the levy approved by the board because the board had determined that the needs of veterans in the county could better be met by utilizing State funds and that determination by the board was properly a discretionary judgment made by the officials elected to make such decisions. The trial court correctly ruled that the VAC had to comply with the regulations of the Department. The attorney for the VAC was not entitled to compensation from general county funds.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court in favor of defendants on the complaint and on the counterclaims and reversed the order requiring defendants to pay plaintiffs' attorney fees.

 

1017 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Baker

1018 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Independent Voters of Illinois v. Illinois Commerce Com.


No. 84-0892


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


139 Ill. App. 3d 957; 487 N.E.2d 963; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 2914; 94 Ill. Dec. 86



November 21, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County; the Hon. Paul W. Schnake, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to § 68 of the Public Utilities Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111 2/3, par. 72 (1983), appellant public interest group challenged an order of the Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois), which affirmed a decision of appellee Illinois Commerce Commission that telephone company customers were not entitled to reparations under § 72 of the Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. 1983, ch. 111 2/3, para. 76 (1983) for rates charged during a certain time period.


OVERVIEW: A voters' group brought a petition challenging the telephone company's rates. The circuit court affirmed the Commission's determination that the company's customers were not entitled to reparations pursuant to § 72 of Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. 1983, ch. 111 2/3, para. 76 (1983), for the rates charged between the time that the state supreme court determined that the rates were excessive and the Commission's recalculation. The court affirmed the order, finding that the statute provided for reparations as the exclusive remedy, and the equitable remedy of restitution was prohibited. No case law directly determined what effect a reviewing court's reversal of the Commission's order had on existing public utility rates, and the statutes did not specifically prescribe the effect on existing rates of a reviewing court's reversal of a Commission's order that set rates. The court held that the reversal and remand of the order of the Commission did not change the rate, but mandated the Commission to issue a new order. The rate in the reversed order remained in effect until the Commission acted on the mandate and issued a new order, and allowing an orderly transition from one rate to another.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order.

 

1019 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. McKay


No. 84-0700


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


138 Ill. App. 3d 446; 485 N.E.2d 1257; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 2703; 93 Ill. Dec. 47



November 20, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County; the Hon. Charles R. Norgle, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged an order of the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), which conducted a jury trial, found him guilty of residential burglary in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 19-3 (1983), and imposed sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of residential burglary. On appeal, the court affirmed, finding that (1) the officers' identification of defendant was not vague because they saw a picture of him at roll call, they saw him while driving beside defendant through a lighted intersection, they saw him when he fled on foot, and the officers were asked whether the man they saw was the man in the roll call photograph; (2) the victim's description was not inconsistent with her trial testimony or defendant's actual appearance because she described him as being clean-shaven but with stubble and she identified him when he had a few days' growth of beard; (3) the prosecutor's comment that defendant did not live in town and had no reason to be there was a proper comment on the facts presented in the record; and (4) although the second paragraph of Ill. Pattern Jury Instructions (Crim.) 2d No. 3.02 should have been given, defendant was not prejudiced, and the verdict did not result from error because defendant only argued misidentification and he offered no theory of innocence to explain the evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction.

 

1020 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Salas


No. 84-0663


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


138 Ill. App. 3d 48; 485 N.E.2d 596; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 2652; 92 Ill. Dec. 785



November 8, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County; the Hon. Fred A. Geiger, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, and reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged an order of the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois), which conducted a bench trial and found defendant guilty of indecent liberties with a child in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 11-4(a)(1) (1983), and entered a conviction on a jury verdict that found him guilty of rape and armed violence in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, paras. 11-1, 33A-2 (1983).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty of various sex offenses against a child. On review, the court reversed the rape and armed violence charges, finding that there was sufficient evidence that defendant was 17 years old or older in that he was the live-in boyfriend of the child's mother for two years and two months, the child was 11 years old, it was unlikely that her mother would have been living with a 16-year-old boy, defendant did not object to the investigator's conjecture that defendant was 32 years old, and the jury had an opportunity to observe him at trial. The circuit court erroneously denied defendant's motion in limine because § 115-10 of the Code of Criminal Procedure only permitted the admission into evidence of testimony that the child made a complaint, and not the details of the complaint. The admission of the details was not harmless, the State presented no corroborating evidence, and an instruction did not cure the error. Because complaints were not admissible under § 115-10 unless the child testified and was subject to cross-examination, the statute, as construed, was not unconstitutional, where the child did not claim to have forgotten the underlying incident.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of conviction of indecent liberties and the 15-year sentence of imprisonment imposed thereon, reversed the judgments of conviction of rape and armed violence, and remanded those charges for a new trial.

 

1021 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Boatright


No. 84-0937


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


137 Ill. App. 3d 888; 486 N.E.2d 926; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 2612; 93 Ill. Dec. 393



November 6, 1985, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 10, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Stephenson County; the Hon. Lawrence A. Smith, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order of the Circuit Court of Stephenson County (Illinois), which found him guilty but mentally ill of arson in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 20-1(a) (1983) and attempted arson in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 8-4(a) (1983) and the sentence imposed by the circuit court specifically the order of restitution.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty but mentally ill of arson and attempted arson after a bench trial. Defendant was sentenced to concurrent terms of probation and, as a condition of probation, was ordered to pay restitution and continue his treatment at a mental health center. Defendant contended that the circuit court erred by ordering him to pay restitution without first determining his ability to pay, and that the Illinois guilty-but-mentally-ill statute, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 6-2(c) (1983) violates the due process clause of the United States and Illinois constitutions. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that pursuant to § 5-6-3(b)(9) of the Unified Code of Corrections, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-6-3(b)(9) (1983) the court was not required to make any inquiry into a defendant's financial ability to pay restitution. Additionally, the Illinois guilty-but-mentally-ill statute was not unconstitutional as applied to non-incarcerated defendants because § 6-2(c) was rationally designed to accomplish the goal of reducing the number of persons who were erroneously found not guilty by reason of insanity and to characterize such defendants as in need of treatment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court.

 

1022 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Tait v. County of Sangamon


No. 4-85-0295


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


138 Ill. App. 3d 169; 485 N.E.2d 558; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 2668; 92 Ill. Dec. 747



November 5, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Sangamon County; the Hon. Raymond L. Terrell, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff criminal defendant sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court of Sangamon County (Illinois) which granted the motion to dismiss made by defendant, County of Sangamon, ruling that declaratory judgment was not appropriate in an action alleging that a portion of costs assessed against the criminal defendant and others were not authorized by statute.


OVERVIEW: After he and others were assessed costs in collateral criminal proceedings, the criminal defendant brought a declaratory judgment action on behalf of himself and all others similarly situated, alleging that a portion of the costs were not authorized by statute. The trial court granted the county's motion to dismiss ruling that the claim was not appropriate for declaratory relief. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment dismissing the criminal defendant's action. The court held that declaratory judgment was not appropriate because the criminal defendant was not seeking to learn the consequences of future action, but was attacking a prior judgment. He could have filed a motion to retax the costs in the criminal proceeding. The court further held that the action was barred as a collateral attack because the order to pay costs was part of the prior judgment and was subject to review on direct appeal. Even if the prior decision was erroneous, that would not render the judgment void.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court dismissing the criminal defendant's declaratory judgment action against the county, which alleged that a portion of the costs assessed in collateral criminal proceedings were not authorized by statute.

 

1023 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Moffitt


No. 2-84-0829


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


138 Ill. App. 3d 106; 485 N.E.2d 513; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 2659; 92 Ill. Dec. 702



November 4, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County; the Hon. Bernard E. Drew, Jr., Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and remanded in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois), which convicted him of and sentenced and fined him for unlawful possession of a controlled substance, unlawful use of weapons, and obstructing justice.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant asked the court to reverse his convictions and remand the case for a new trial at which all the fruits of his allegedly illegal arrest were suppressed from evidence. Alternatively, he asked for a reduction in his sentence or for the vacation of the sentencing orders and for the remanding of his cause for a new sentencing hearing. Additionally, he asked the court to correct the mittimus to provide that his sentence for unlawful use of weapons was for a term of 364 days or less. Upon review, the court held that the mittimus required correction. Since the stop of defendant's car was justified, it followed that the officer's examination of defendant's driver's license and license plates constituted usual and customary police procedure in such a situation. When it was discovered that the driver's license was not valid and that the license plates were also suspended, probable cause existed for defendant's arrest and the subsequent valid inventory search of the car. Defendant's sentence of one year for unlawful use of weapons was one day too long and that the mittimus issued required correction to reflect the term of 364 days.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions, but remanded the cause to the trial court with directions for preparation of an amended mittimus reflecting the proper sentence for unlawful use of weapons.

 

1024 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Wolf v. Hynes


No. 85-503


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


137 Ill. App. 3d 987; 485 N.E.2d 463; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 2629; 92 Ill. Dec. 652



October 31, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Earl Arkiss, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Orders affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayers appealed from the Circuit Court of Cook County's (Illinois) dismissal of their complaint and the denial of their motion to reconsider. The taxpayers had sought a declaration that an assessed valuation for certain real estate and the taxes thereon were grossly excessive, fraudulent, and void. The taxpayers had also sought to enjoin defendants, a county assessor and other officials, from collecting the taxes.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs exhausted administrative remedies but did not pay the tax under protest because they contended that the payment-under-protest procedure in § 194 of the Revenue Act of 1939, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 675 (1977) was inadequate and was violative of equal protection. On appeal, the court held that § 194 of the Act was an adequate remedy at law, and therefore, the taxpayers were not entitled to injunctive relief. Unlike the four-fold assessment increase in the instant case, the assessment in the case relied on by the taxpayers was 25 times the amount assessed for the previous year and was predicated upon nonexistent improvements. Further, the taxpayers had the means to pay the tax under protest. Equal protection was not violated because consideration of the financial ability to pursue the payment-under-protest remedy was reasonably related to the determination of the adequacy of that legal remedy. The argument that consideration of the taxpayers' financial status was not rationally related to the assessment of ad valorem taxes was without merit because they did not allege that defendants used the taxpayers' financial status to determine the amount of the tax.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

1025 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Prather


No. 84-2636


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


138 Ill. App. 3d 32; 485 N.E.2d 430; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 2650; 92 Ill. Dec. 619



October 29, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Romie J. Palmer, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction for distribution of look-alike substances pursuant to the Illinois Controlled Substances Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, para. 1401(b) (1983) from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois).


OVERVIEW: After a trial on the merits, the jury found defendant knowingly distributed capsules that looked like amphetamines. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded for a new trial. The court held: (1) the definition of look-alike substances in the Illinois Controlled Substances Act was not unconstitutionally vague because he was charged for conduct clearly prohibited by the statute; (2) the penalty provisions for distribution of look-alike substances was reasonably designed to remedy evils which the legislature determined threatened the public's health, safety, and general welfare; (3) there was sufficient evidence to avoid the proscription against double jeopardy but on retrial, defendant was entitled to the presumption of innocence; and (4) a jury instruction that improperly assumed one of the elements of the crime charged was fatally defective because the jury believed the pills were in fact look-alike substances. The court found the admission of two boxes of pills was erroneous. The cumulative effect was to create the impression that defendant was guilty of the charged offense because he had committed a crime by possessing the two boxes of pills.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for distribution of look-alike substances and remanded for a new trial.

People v. Fenwick


No. 3-85-0137


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


137 Ill. App. 3d 457; 484 N.E.2d 915; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 2558; 92 Ill. Dec. 184



October 18, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Bureau County; the Hon. James J. Wimbiscus, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court of Bureau County (Illinois), which convicted defendants of hunting without permission.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were charged with hunting without permission after they were found near leased property with guns and a dead deer. The State showed that the tenant did not give defendants permission to hunt but failed to present any evidence that the owner did not give defendants permission to hunt. Defendants were convicted and sought review. They contended that the State failed to prove that they lacked permission to hunt from the owners. The State contended that under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 61, para. 2.33(t) (1983), it only had to show lack of permission from the tenant or the owner but not both. The court reversed. The court found that under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 61, para. 2.33(t) (1983), the State met the burden of showing lack of permission by the tenant but that the State failed to show that defendants lacked permission from the owner. Both elements were required to be shown for a conviction.


OUTCOME: The court found that the State failed to meet its burden of proof and reversed the judgment which convicted defendants for hunting without permission.

 

1027 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. M.B. (In re M.B.)


No. 4-84-0673


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


137 Ill. App. 3d 992; 484 N.E.2d 1154; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 2630; 92 Ill. Dec. 299; 12 Media L. Rep. 1551



October 17, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Woodford County; the Hon. Richard M. Baner, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant news media challenged the decision of the Circuit Court of Woodford County (Illinois), which denied its motion to vacate a protective order, pursuant to the Juvenile Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 37, para. 705--5, prohibiting the media from revealing directly or indirectly the identity of appellee minors or the minor victim involved in a case of abuse and the state's petition to have the minors declared wards of the state.


OVERVIEW: The minors' allegedly abusive acts against a two-year-old infant caused the state to petition for their wardship. Concerned for the safety of the minor, the trial court issued a protective order preventing the media from revealing their identities. The media filed a motion to vacate, contending the trial court exceeded its authority under the Juvenile Act. The trial court denied its motion. The media applied to higher courts for vacation or stays, which were denied. The media sought review of the pretrial order. The court held that because fundamental constitutional rights were involved, the right to appeal existed. The media was not an interloper but was specifically aggrieved by the trial court's order. There was no "pecuniary interest" involved, but the invasion of a legal right had been met. The media's First Amendment rights had been prejudiced by the protective order. Therefore, they had standing to appeal. The court opinioned that the nature of the order was prohibitory and appealable under Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 307(a)(1) and that while the protection of the minors' safety was a state interest of the highest order, it did not justify the prior restraint imposed.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the protective order.

People v. Crow's Nest, Inc.


No. 3-85-0281


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


137 Ill. App. 3d 461; 484 N.E.2d 907; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 2560; 92 Ill. Dec. 176



October 16, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Will County; the Hon. Herman S. Haase, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Will County (Illinois), which enjoined defendant from further sale of drug paraphernalia and forfeited the confiscated items pursuant to the Illinois Drug Paraphernalia Control Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, para. 2101 et seq.


OVERVIEW: Police seized drug paraphernalia at defendant's business. Pursuant to the Illinois Drug Paraphernalia Control Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, para. 2101 et seq., the trial court enjoined defendant from further sales of drug paraphernalia and forfeited the confiscated items. Defendant contended that the State did not prove beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant marketed the seized items for use with illegal drugs. The court found that the record amply supported the trial court's finding that defendant marketed items for use with controlled substances. Notwithstanding defendant's assertion to the contrary, the court held that posting of signs by defendant that such items should not have been used illicitly and requiring customers to sign statements of intent supported the conclusion the items were marketed in violation of the statute. The court found that such disclaimers by defendant represented his awareness of the nature of the items sold and did not relieve defendant from the responsibility for their sale. The court found that the Act was sufficiently specific to inform a reasonably prudent businessperson what conduct was proscribed from that which was permitted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

People v. Hartfield


No. 84-2253


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


137 Ill. App. 3d 679; 484 N.E.2d 1136; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 2585; 92 Ill. Dec. 281



October 15, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Thomas A. Hett, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of rape and was sentenced to life imprisonment under the habitual criminal statute. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) entered the jury's verdict. Defendant appealed his conviction and sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was tried before a jury on charges of rape and aggravated battery. The charges arose from an attack upon complainant. At trial, complainant testified that she initially encountered defendant shortly before the attack outside of her apartment building. She was previously unacquainted with defendant when he approached her and a friend to ask for directions. A few minutes later, complainant left her friend and went up to her second-floor apartment. Defendant grabbed her as she fumbled with her keys, and dragged her into her apartment and raped her. On appeal, defendant argued that the trial court erred in denying his motion to exclude evidence of his two prior rape convictions. The court held that defendant waived that objection by failing to testify. The court affirmed the lower court. The court further held that the claimed improprieties in the state's argument were not of such magnitude as to deprive defendant of a fair trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's judgment convicting defendant.

 

1030 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Paino


No. 84-0867


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


137 Ill. App. 3d 645; 484 N.E.2d 1106; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 2584; 92 Ill. Dec. 251



October 11, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Francis J. Mahon, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions for rape, armed robbery, and deviate sexual assault and the sentences imposed against him by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois).


OVERVIEW: A jury convicted defendant of the offenses, and the trial court sentenced him to 30-years on the rape conviction consecutively to concurrent 25-year terms on the armed robbery and deviate sexual assault convictions. Defendant appealed claiming the trial court erred in failing to suppress his lineup identification, that he was prejudiced by hearsay evidence, and that his sentence was excessive. The court affirmed the convictions and the sentences. The fact that the lineup occurred on the same day that defendant was indicted, was not in itself sufficient to show that defendant's right to counsel had attached at the time of the lineup. Based on the lack of evidence to show otherwise, it was presumed that his right to counsel had not attached. The jury instruction to disregard certain hearsay evidence cured any prejudice. There was a substantial change in the criminal objective regarding the three distinct offenses; thus the consecutive sentence was warranted. Based on defendant's criminal record compared to that of his co-defendant, their degree of participation, and the co-defendant's negotiated guilty plea, the disparity in their sentences was justified.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and his resulting sentences.

East Lake Fork Special Drainage Dist. v. Ivesdale


Nos. 4-85-0080, 4-85-0084, 4-85-0086 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


137 Ill. App. 3d 473; 484 N.E.2d 507; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 2563; 91 Ill. Dec. 948



October 10, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Champaign County; the Hon. Creed D. Tucker, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in 4 -- 85 -- 0080, 4 -- 85 -- 0084; Appeal dismissed in 4 -- 85 -- 0086.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant drainage districts sought review of orders of the Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois), which sustained the objections of appellee local government units to assessments levied by the drainage districts due to the passage of Public Act No. 83-726 (Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 42, paras. 5-2, 5-3 (1983)). That act exempted public highways, streets and alleys.


OVERVIEW: The units of local government that controlled highways, streets, or alleys were assessed by the drainage districts. Due to Public Act No. 83-726, the units of local government requested that the trial court order that the public thoroughfares be removed from the maintenance assessment rolls and sought refunds from assessments paid under protest. The trial court entered orders sustaining the objections except for one, unless that objector could show that the thoroughfares over which it exercised control were public. On appeal, the court dismissed the appeal of the drainage district for the unit that the objection was overruled. The court affirmed the objections. The court found that under section 9 of article IX of the 1970 Illinois Constitution, the General Assembly could in its discretion totally abolish the Illinois Drainage Code or eliminate the authority of drainage districts to levy special assessments. The court concluded that the constitution provided that the drainage districts only had powers granted by law, and that there were no inhibitions on the plenary power of the General Assembly to enact exemptions from special assessment.


OUTCOME: The appeal of the one drainage district to the objection that was overruled was dismissed. The court affirmed the judgment sustaining the objections of the local government units.

 

1032 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Caseyville v. Cunningham


No. 5-84-0447


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


137 Ill. App. 3d 186; 484 N.E.2d 499; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 2524; 91 Ill. Dec. 940



October 9, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of St. Clair County; the Hon. Richard P. Goldenhersh and the Hon. Roger M. Scrivner, Judges, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant truck owners appealed from the order of the Circuit Court of St. Clair Court (Illinois) granting plaintiff village a permanent injunction and enjoining them from violating a village ordinance, which prohibited the operation of their refrigerated trailer during certain hours in certain areas of the village.


OVERVIEW: The truck owners used a truck and refrigerated trailer for their business and parked them in the village when they were not use. The refrigeration unit on the trailer was often left operating, and the truck owners were subsequently cited for numerous violations of the ordinance because of the noise the refrigeration unit made. The village was granted a permanent injunction against the truck owners. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that the ordinance was not preempted by the Illinois Environmental Protection Act and, further, that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 24, para. 11-60-2 (1983) delegated to the village the authority to prevent nuisances. Additionally, the ordinance bore a reasonable relationship to the interest of protecting residents from disturbing noises. Finally, the court held that the truck owners failed to show how the restrictions placed on them concerning the operation of their refrigerated trailer harmed their business. Thus, the ordinance did not constitute an unconstitutional restraint on interstate commerce.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order enjoining the truck owners from operating their refrigerated trailer at certain hours and in certain areas of the village.

People v. Dale


No. 5-84-0686


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


137 Ill. App. 3d 101; 484 N.E.2d 459; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 2513; 91 Ill. Dec. 900



October 3, 1985, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied October 29, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Saline County; the Hon. Michael J. Henshaw, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed after the Circuit Court of Saline County (Illinois) convicted him of two counts of unlawful delivery of a controlled substance, unlawful possession of a controlled substance, unlawful possession of cannabis, unlawful use of weapons, two counts of armed violence, and possession of a firearm without required identification.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested after he sold drugs to an undercover officer; he was charged on eight counts arising from the sale. Defendant appealed and argued that four counts of the indictment should have been vacated because they were included within the offense charged in the first count, unlawful delivery of more than 30 grams of cocaine. In reversing in part, the court noted that the State did not contest defendant's claim that his convictions on two counts, for unlawful possession and delivery of less than 30 grams of cocaine, were lesser offenses of the unlawful delivery count. Defendant could not be convicted of both unlawful delivery and the lesser offenses arising out of the delivery transaction; no more than one "delivery" had occurred. The court vacated the count for armed violence that was based upon the vacated lesser delivery count. The court affirmed the rest of the convictions. Defendant's conviction for driving a car while in possession of cocaine and a gun was not included within his delivery offense. Section 5-9-1.1 of the Unified Code of Corrections, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-9-1.1 (1983), under which defendant was fined, was not impermissibly vague.


OUTCOME: The court vacated defendant's convictions for possession of cocaine, delivery of less than 30 grams of cocaine, and for armed violence arising from the vacated unlawful delivery count. It affirmed defendant's other convictions and sentences.

People v. Locascio


Nos. 82-2529, 82-2530 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


137 Ill. App. 3d 201; 484 N.E.2d 451; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 2526; 91 Ill. Dec. 892



October 3, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Earl Strayhorn, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On remand from the Illinois Supreme Court, defendants appealed their convictions for official misconduct and poaching.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were convicted of official misconduct for shooting and removal of deer outside open season. On appeal, the appellate court reversed the convictions. The Illinois Supreme Court reversed the judgment of the appellate court, and remanded for a determination of those issues raised by defendants, but not previously addressed. On remand, defendants argued that the State failed to offer proof of several elements of the offense, namely, that defendants were acting in their official capacity, knew that their conduct was unauthorized, took deer outside open season, and took deer after sunset and before sunrise. The court found that defendants, as forest preserve officers, must have known it was unauthorized conduct to shoot deer in the forest preserve, or to take deer outside open season. The court found that the evidence was sufficient to prove the statutory elements compromising the crimes charged. The court rejected defendants' argument that the charging instrument was unconstitutionally vague and found that defendants were sufficiently apprised on the charges against them.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Willard v. Northwest Nat'l Bank


No. 83-1532


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


137 Ill. App. 3d 255; 484 N.E.2d 823; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 2534; 92 Ill. Dec. 92; 42 U.C.C. Rep. Serv. (Callaghan) 1179



September 27, 1985, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied November 6, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Albert Green, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, and reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, husband and wife, challenged the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed their complaint against defendant bank based on their failure to state a claim for breach of fiduciary notice and violations of the Uniform Commercial Code, in their complaint seeking to void the bank's sale of their home. The husband and wife also challenged the summary judgment granted to defendant purchaser.


OVERVIEW: A husband conveyed his home into a trust as security for a loan from a bank without his wife's authorization. The husband defaulted on the loan and the bank conveyed the property to a purchaser, who filed a forcible detainer action. The husband and wife asserted that the bank had breached its fiduciary duty and had violated § 9-504 of the Uniform Commercial Code (UCC) by not giving sale notice, and also that the sale was void because of the wife's homestead exemption. The court found that the circuit court properly dismissed the husband's cause of action for the bank's breach of fiduciary duty because Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 148, paras. 82 through 84 (1983) barred such actions. The court found that the circuit court erred in dismissing the claim under § 9-504(3) of the UCC because the bank did not provide reasonable sale notice. The court also found that the circuit court erred in not recognizing the wife's homestead interest, which she had never released. The court affirmed the circuit court's determination that the purchaser's possessory right was not precluded by a bankruptcy stay.


OUTCOME: Due to a statutory bar, the court affirmed the circuit court's dismissal of the husband's claim that the bank breached its fiduciary duty. The court reversed the circuit court's dismissal of the husband's claim under the Uniform Commercial Code because the bank had not provided the husband with sale notice, and also reversed the dismissal of the claim to maintain the wife's homestead exemption.

People v. Waters


No. 84-0113


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


136 Ill. App. 3d 858; 483 N.E.2d 1061; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 2469; 91 Ill. Dec. 575



September 27, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. George Marovich, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, and vacated in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged an order from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) that convicted him of burglary after a bench trial and that sentenced him to a term of six years and assessed a fine and costs.


OVERVIEW: After defendant was found inside a closed restaurant with a bag containing food and other restaurant property, he was convicted of burglary. The trial court sentenced him to a term of six years, a fine, and costs. On appeal, the court held that there was no constitutional infirmity in the retention of bail deposits to pay an indigent defendant's court costs at trial pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 110-7(h) (1983). However, the court vacated that portion of the trial court's order that imposed the fine. The facts before the trial court were insufficient to support a determination that defendant had the financial resources and future ability to pay the fine. The trial court erred in imposing the fine based solely on the fact that a cash bond had been posted. The ability of defendant to post a cash bond did not necessarily mean that he had the financial ability to pay restitution or reimbursement.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order that convicted defendant and sentenced him to a term of six years, but it vacated the fine. The cause was remanded for the limited purpose of conducting a hearing to determine defendant's ability to pay the fine, and, if established, the amount of the fine.

People v. Khan

The court held that the proscription against double jeopardy did not bar the institution of both civil and criminal proceedings. The court found the evidence sufficient to convict defendant.

1038 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Alexander


No. 4-84-0902


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


136 Ill. App. 3d 1047; 483 N.E.2d 1039; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 2491; 91 Ill. Dec. 553



September 26, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Macon County; the Hon. Rodney A. Scott, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order from the Circuit Court of Macon County (Illinois), which dismissed his petition for post-conviction relief.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pleaded guilty to various crimes and was convicted thereof. Subsequently, defendant filed a petition for post-conviction relief praying for an order finding that his initial arrest was illegal, withdrawing his guilty pleas, and suppressing all evidence obtained pursuant to the arrest. The State moved to dismiss the petition, and, following an ex parte hearing before the same judge who received his guilty pleas, the petition was dismissed. The court reversed the dismissal order. Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 122-8 (Supp. 1984), by its plain language, required the petition for post-conviction relief to have been assigned to a judge who did not preside at the proceedings which resulted in the defendant's conviction. Thus, the trial court's failure to assign the petition to such a judge required reversal of the order dismissing the petition. Moreover, under Ill. Rev. Stat.ch. 38, paras. 122-2.1(a) and (c) (Supp. 1984), the legislature did not intend to sanction ex parte hearings of the type which were held in defendant's case prior to dismissal of his petition. Rather, at such a preliminary stage, the trial judge alone was required to have considered the petition.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order and remanded the cause with directions that the petition be assigned to a judge who did not participate in the underlying criminal proceedings and to proceed thereafter as provided in the Code of Criminal Procedure of 1963.

People v. Goins


No. 84-0643


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


136 Ill. App. 3d 582; 483 N.E.2d 702; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 2429; 91 Ill. Dec. 356



September 23, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County; the Hon. John J. Bowman, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), which convicted him of residential burglary, a violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 19-3 (1983).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested in Kane County on July 7, 1983, and charged in that county with residential burglary. He remained in the custody of Kane County until November 30, 1983, when that charge was nol-prossed and he was arrested and taken into custody by Du Page County authorities following his indictment for the same offense in Du Page County. Defendant remained incarcerated in Du Page County until he made an oral motion for his discharge. The trial court denied the motion for discharge finding that it did not have jurisdiction to try the offense until November 30, 1983, and that 120 days had not elapsed. Defendant was convicted. The court affirmed the conviction. The court adhered to a prior decision that the residential burglary statute was constitutional. The words "court having jurisdiction" in the speedy-trial statute, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, 103-5(a) (1983), meant a court where venue to try the case lied. It was evident that defendant became in custody in Du Page County, the "court having jurisdiction," for the alleged burglary on November 30, 1983. Since 120 days had not elapsed at the time the motion for discharge was made, the trial court properly denied the motion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

People v. Cooney


Nos. 83-817, 83-886 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


136 Ill. App. 3d 989; 484 N.E.2d 802; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 2484; 92 Ill. Dec. 71



September 23, 1985, Filed

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County; the Hon. Harry D. Strouse, Judge, presiding.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants sought review of their convictions in the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois) on charges of murder and armed robbery. 1041 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Upton


No. 5-84-0632


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


136 Ill. App. 3d 1075; 484 N.E.2d 390; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 2497; 91 Ill. Dec. 831



September 18, 1985, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied October 29, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Jackson County; the Hon. Richard E. Richman, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment from the Circuit Court of Jackson County (Illinois), which convicted her on three separate counts of unlawful distribution of a look-alike substance in violation of § 404 of the Illinois Controlled Substances Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, para. 1404 (1983), and sentenced her to one year of conditional discharge and a fine of $ 100 on each count.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant alleged that § 404, as amended in 1982, violated due process because it provided for a potential penalty more severe for the crime of delivery of a look-alike substance than that which could be imposed for delivery of a real controlled substance. Distribution of a look-alike subjected violators to a possible fine of $ 150,000, without regard to the type of substance involved. Delivery of a controlled substance could result in possible penal fines ranging from $ 75,000 to $ 125,000. Section 404's predecessor had previously been declared unconstitutional because the delivery of a look-alike substance had been classified as a class 3 felony, whereas delivery of an actual controlled substance had been classified as a less sever class 4 felony. The legislature later made delivery of a controlled substance a class 3 felony. In vacating defendant's conviction, the court ruled that because the fine provisions still remained disparate, the constitutional infirmity still existed. Defendant had standing to challenge the statute, despite her low fine, because she was within the aggrieved class of those sentenced under the invalid statute.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment from the circuit court and vacated defendant's conviction.
