Calumet Country Club v. Roberts Environmental Control Corp.


No. 85-195


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


136 Ill. App. 3d 610; 483 N.E.2d 613; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 2432; 91 Ill. Dec. 267



September 10, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Myron T. Gomberg, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, and in part reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant country club sought review of an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed with prejudice, on limitations grounds, its amended complaint seeking recovery for property damage occasioned by the alleged failure of a piping connection sold and installed by appellee company.


OVERVIEW: The country club brought an action against the company to recover for property damage occasioned by the alleged failure of a piping connection sold and installed by the company. The trial court applied the two-year limitations period of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 13 -- 214(a) (1983) and dismissed the action as time-barred. The country club appealed the decision, arguing that the trial court erred by applying that statute of limitations and that § 13 -- 214(a) was unconstitutional as special legislation. The court affirmed the order in part and reversed it in part. The court found that count II of the complaint, based on product liability, was barred under either the general limitation provision used by the trial court or § 13 -- 213, which applied according to the country club. As to count I, the negligence claim, the court found the record was insufficient to determine whether the pipe installation constituted an "improvement to real property," as used in § 13 -- 214(a), and thus whether that statute was properly applied. The court further found that § 13 -- 214(a) was constitutional, as the two-year period was reasonably related to the statute's stated purpose.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed that part of the circuit court's judgment dismissing count II of the amended complaint, but reversed and remanded for further proceedings that part of the judgment dismissing count I. The court found that it was not clear that the piping connection constituted an improvement to the property, so dismissal on the basis of the corresponding statute of limitations was improper.

People v. Schubert


No. 83-2986


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


136 Ill. App. 3d 348; 483 N.E.2d 600; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 2406; 91 Ill. Dec. 254



September 10, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Robert L. Massey, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of the offense of exhibiting child pornography under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 11-20a (1981).


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged the constitutionality of the child pornography statute and the sufficiency of the evidence in his conviction. The court affirmed the conviction. Because of the proof submitted at trial, the trial court could conclusively determine that defendant had knowledge of the contents of the magazines he sold and that the contents depicted children under the age of 16. The court held that the indictment against defendant was sufficient and that the magazines were properly admitted into evidence at trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for exhibiting child pornography.

People v. Townsend


No. 83-3027


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


136 Ill. App. 3d 385; 483 N.E.2d 340; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 2412; 91 Ill. Dec. 58



August 30, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Don A. Moore, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) of attempted murder, aggravated battery, and armed violence in a jury trial. The trial court vacated the convictions for aggravated battery and armed violence and sentenced defendant to a term of eight years on the attempted murder conviction. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed he had acted in self-defense when he shot the victim, who was his girlfriend. On appeal, defendant contended that the jury was improperly instructed and that he was denied a fair trial by certain prosecutorial comments made in closing argument. The court affirmed defendant's conviction for attempted murder, finding that the jury had been properly instructed on the justifiable use of force in self-defense. The court determined that comments made by the prosecution in closing argument were provoked by the assailment by defense counsel of the honesty and character of each of the state's witnesses and thus the comments could not be advanced as a ground for reversal. Because the facts concerning the trajectory of the bullets and the relative positions of defendant and the victim at the time of the shooting were presented through the testimony of various witnesses at trial and were discussed by the attorneys in closing arguments, they were proper subjects of consideration by the court in its review of the record in its totality. On the basis of that review, the court concluded that there was ample evidence to support the jury verdict.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for attempted murder.

People v. Cooper


No. 81-2171


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


136 Ill. App. 3d 517; 483 N.E.2d 309; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 2422; 91 Ill. Dec. 27



August 28, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Lawrence I. Genesen, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) for aggravated battery. Defendant argued that section 5 -- 5 -- 3(b)(2) of the Unified Code of Corrections, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, par. 1005 -- 5 -- 3.2(b)(2) (1979), was unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with attempted murder, aggravated battery, and armed violence. His first trial ended in a mistrial based on a deadlocked jury. Following a second jury trial, defendant was convicted of aggravated battery and sentenced to an extended term of nine years. He appealed. Finally, the record failed to establish that the trial court exceeded the bounds of propriety in making its rulings. The trial court did not indicate any favoritism to the prosecutor, and defendant was not deprived of a fair trial.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

People v. Henson


No. 4-85-0131


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


136 Ill. App. 3d 183; 482 N.E.2d 1044; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 2380; 90 Ill. Dec. 761



August 27, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Piatt County; the Hon. John P. Shonkwiler, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court of Piatt County (Illinois), which convicted him on four counts of forgery in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 17-3(a)(1), (2) (1983) and sentenced him to three years on each count. Defendant contended that para. 17-3(a) was unconstitutional because there was no rational basis for treating forgery of less than $ 300 as a felony and theft of less than $ 300 as a misdemeanor.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of and sentenced on four counts of forgery, a class three felony. On appeal, defendant argued that the Illinois forgery statute violated equal protection and due process because there was no rational basis for punishing forgery of amounts less than $ 300 as a felony while theft of less than $ 300 was punished as a misdemeanor. The court affirmed, concluding that although the legislature could not discriminate against two similarly situated persons under the guise of classification, forgery and theft were not identical offenses. The intention to commit fraud by knowingly making or altering a document to defraud another was all that was required to commit fraud under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 17-3(a)(1) (1983), while theft required the accused to have knowingly obtained unauthorized control over the property of another under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 16-1(a)(1983). Because obtaining control over the property of another was not necessary to commit the crime of forgery, those who committed the offenses were not similarly situated, and equal protection was not violated.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and sentences for forgery.

People v. Jones


No. 84-2462


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


135 Ill. App. 3d 1023; 482 N.E.2d 1031; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 2347; 90 Ill. Dec. 748



August 23, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Lawrence I. Genesen, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) and was sentenced to four concurrent extended terms of 35 years each for rape, deviate sexual assault, and armed robbery, and 20 years for aggravated kidnapping. On appeal, he argued that he was denied due process by the state's recommendation of a longer term of imprisonment than it earlier offered and by his counsel's inadequate advice as to the effect of a blind guilty plea.


OVERVIEW: During plea bargaining, the state offered to recommend a sentence of 18 years, or as low as 15 years, on all charges. The defendant's counsel told him that he was likely to receive a sentence closer to the minimum six-year sentence. The trial court admonished the defendant as to his rights under Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 402, 87 Ill. 2d R. 402. On appeal, the court held that there was no merit to the defendant's claim that the state's decision to seek an extended-term sentence was evidence of prosecutorial vindictiveness. In the give-and-take of plea bargaining, there was no element of punishment or retaliation so long as the accused was free to accept or reject the prosecution's offer. There was no constitutional restriction on the state's seeking a greater penalty than that offered in unsuccessful plea negotiations. Further, the defendant was properly admonished as to the range of penalties, including the possibility of extended-term sentences. The court held that his counsel's erroneous opinion as to the likely sentence did not give the defendant a right to withdraw his guilty plea. For other reasons, the court reduced the kidnapping sentence to 15 years. As modified, the court affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court reduced the kidnapping sentence to 15 years, and, as modified, affirmed the circuit court's denial of the defendant's motion to withdraw his plea and the sentences imposed.

People v. Carter


No. 84-2083


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


135 Ill. App. 3d 997; 482 N.E.2d 662; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 2343; 90 Ill. Dec. 683



August 22, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Robert J. Collins, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which denied his motion for reduction of sentence. Defendant had been convicted of violating the Franchise Disclosure Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 121 1/2, para. 701 et seq., and had been sentenced to a prison term of three years.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of violating the Act and sentenced to three years' imprisonment in Illinois. He was later sentenced in Georgia to five years' imprisonment with his sentence there to run concurrently with any other sentences. The court reversed defendant's Illinois conviction, but on further appeal, the conviction was reinstated. The case eventually returned to the trial court, which denied defendant's motion for a reduction of sentence. On appeal of the denial, the court reversed. Although defendant had not met his 30-day deadline to apply for a sentence reduction pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-8-1(f), he reasonably believed at the time of his release from Georgia that his Illinois conviction had been reversed and would not be reinstated. It was thus not unreasonable for defendant to believe that there was no need for him to petition for a reduction of sentence. The court noted that the Illinois Supreme Court had indicated that defendant could seek a sentence modification. The court remanded the action to the trial court with directions to consider defendant's request for a sentence modification pursuant to para. 1005-8-1(f).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's decision and remanded the action to the trial court with directions to consider defendant's request for a sentence modification.

People v. Solis


No. 84-0688


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


135 Ill. App. 3d 991; 482 N.E.2d 207; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 2342; 90 Ill. Dec. 500



August 15, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County; the Hon. Joseph M. McCarthy, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois), which denied his motion to suppress evidence, convicted him of residential burglary pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, par. 19-3 (1983), and sentenced him to seven years' imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: After defendant's motion to suppress evidence found during a search of his car and his person, he was convicted of residential burglary and sentenced to a term of seven years. Defendant appealed, contending that the police officer did not have reasonable articulable suspicion to effectuate the initial stop and frisk and that para. 19-3, the residential burglary statute, was unconstitutional. Further, the pat down was merely part of the investigatory stop and the officer could rely on his own knowledge, experience, and reasonable inferences in investigating possible criminal conduct and the substantial possibility that defendant was armed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

People ex rel. Skinner v. Hellmuth, Obata & Kassabaum, Inc.


No. 84-0525


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


135 Ill. App. 3d 765; 482 N.E.2d 155; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 2313; 90 Ill. Dec. 448



August 13, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County; the Hon. John L. Hughes, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff state challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois) that dismissed its action against defendant architects for injuries caused during the construction of a public improvement pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 13-214(a) (1983), which required commencement within two years.


OVERVIEW: The state filed an action against the architects for injuries caused during the construction of a public improvement. The architects'' motion to dismiss the state's action, alleging that it was not commenced within the two-year period prescribed in § 13-214(a) (1983), was granted by the trial court. The court reversed on appeal, invalidating § 13-214(a) as special legislation. The statutory term "body politic" evidenced an intention to include the state within the scope of the statute. The statute violated the prohibition against special legislation because it contained an unreasonable classification of members of the construction industry. The statute was substantially similar to its pre-amendment form, which was constitutionally deficient, because it only provided immunity for architects and contractors from suit brought after two years. There was no similar immunity given to the person in control or to those who furnished materials used in constructing the improvement. The addition of those engaged in the "observation or management of construction" was redundant because they were already included in the classes of contractors and architects.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the dismissal of the state's action against the architects for injuries caused during the construction of a public improvement and remanded the case.

People v. Schwartz


No. 83-0552


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


135 Ill. App. 3d 629; 482 N.E.2d 104; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 2295; 90 Ill. Dec. 397



August 12, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County; the Hon. Paul W. Schnake, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois), which found him not guilty by reason of insanity of two counts of murder and guilty but mentally ill of both aggravated arson and arson. Defendant was sentenced to a 14-year term of imprisonment for aggravated arson to be served concurrently with a five-year term of imprisonment imposed for arson.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the circuit court erred when it concluded after a pretrial fitness hearing that his amnesia did not render him unfit to stand trial. He also argued that the circuit court's denial of his posttrial motion, which asserted that the pretrial ruling should have been set aside, was error because his amnesia precluded him from presenting the only possible evidence of his state of mind at the time of the fire. On appeal, the court found that the psychiatric evidence at the pretrial fitness hearing indicated that defendant understood the proceedings against him and could effectively communicate with his lawyer and make trial decisions. The court concluded that he was able to understand the nature and purpose of the proceeding against him and to assist in his defense. The evidence of defendant's inability to recollect the events on the day of the offenses due to his amnesia did not, by itself, warrant a contrary conclusion. The court did not reverse defendant's verdicts based on his fitness, but reversed his conviction for aggravated arson because a recent holding declared unconstitutional a subsection of the aggravated arson statute.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the circuit court on the conviction for aggravated arson and affirmed the judgment and sentence of the circuit court for arson.

People v. Carter


No. 84-579


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


135 Ill. App. 3d 403; 481 N.E.2d 1012; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 2268; 90 Ill. Dec. 212



July 25, 1985, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied August 28, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Ronald Crane, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), in which he was found guilty of attempted murder, but mentally ill, pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 8-4(a) (1981) and Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 115-3(c) (1981). Defendant was sentenced to eight years' imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that the State failed to prove defendant had or could formulate the specific intent necessary to establish the crime or to rebut the issue of self-defense, that the judgment and the sentence rested on the trial court's misapprehension of the law, and that the guilty-but-mentally-ill statute, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 155-3(c) (1983), was unconstitutional. The court affirmed, holding that: (1) the evidence was sufficient for a reasonable trier of fact to determine that defendant acted with intent to kill his brother in that the force used by defendant was intended or likely to cause death or great bodily harm; (2) the trial court could have inferred that defendant suffered from some degree of mental illness at the time of the offense, but that he was legally sane, and thus, that he was guilty beyond a reasonable doubt of attempted murder but mentally ill at the time of the offense; (3) defendant's sentence was clearly within the minimum and maximum sentences allowable for attempted murder; and (4) the guilty-but-mentally-ill statute was rationally based on a legitimate State interest, did not create an arbitrary classification, and thus was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

People v. Newell


No. 83-545


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


135 Ill. App. 3d 417; 481 N.E.2d 1238; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 2269; 90 Ill. Dec. 327



July 25, 1985, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied August 28, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Theodore Swain, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants sought review of their convictions for murder following a bench trial in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois).


OVERVIEW: After the juvenile defendant was ordered tried as an adult, the co-defendants were each represented by a member of the same firm. In affirming their murder convictions, the court held that the juvenile judge did not abuse his discretion by transferring the juvenile to criminal court. The record showed that the judge explicitly reviewed the evidence before him in light of the statutory criteria and made findings of fact before ordering the transfer. The court could discern from the record neither any joint representation of defendants nor the actual conflict of interests, as the attorneys each represented their individual clients. To allow isolated facts to take precedence over the general behavior of the participants, as reflected in the record, would have placed form over substance. Viewing the record as a whole, the court found no actual conflict in the manner in which defendants' counsel represented them. They thus failed to show a deprivation of their Sixth Amendment right to effective assistance of counsel.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendants' murder convictions.

 

1054 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Munday


No. 84-0285


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


134 Ill. App. 3d 971; 481 N.E.2d 338; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 2193; 89 Ill. Dec. 787



July 23, 1985, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied August 21, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County; the Hon. John J. Nelligan, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a bench trial in the Circuit Court of DuPage County (Illinois), defendant was convicted of residential burglary and he appealed, contending that the conviction should be vacated as he was placed in double jeopardy when retried on that charge. Defendant had received a new trial following a finding that he was not guilty of attempted rape and guilty of residential burglary, verdicts which he claimed were inconsistent.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was initially found guilty of residential burglary in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 19-3. The offense required proof that entry into a residence was made with the intent to commit a felony, but defendant was found not guilty of the underlying offense of attempted rape. Defendant was granted a new trial, and again found guilty of the residential burglary charge. In affirming the conviction, the court stated that it reviewed the evidence presented at defendant's first trial and concluded it was sufficient to establish he had an intent to commit rape both when he entered the apartment and while inside, and also sufficient to prove that he took a substantial step towards commission of rape. Defendant had thus not demonstrated a legal inconsistency of the verdicts, collateral estoppel could not be applied, and his retrial for residential burglary was proper. Even though the trial judge had expressed the view that the mandatory minimum sentence was excessive, the court could not reduce his sentence out of merciful benevolence.


OUTCOME: The court found that the verdicts were not inconsistent and upheld defendant's conviction for residential burglary and his sentence.

People ex rel. Irby v. Homyer


No. 5-84-0150


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


135 Ill. App. 3d 161; 481 N.E.2d 928; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 2236; 90 Ill. Dec. 128



July 19, 1985, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied August 21, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Madison County; the Hon. Charles Romani, Jr., Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant father appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court of Madison County (Illinois), which found the father in wilful contempt of court for his failure to relinquish physical custody of his daughter and failure to return the daughter to plaintiff mother in an action brought by the mother to determine the father's paternity.


OVERVIEW: The mother brought a paternity action against the father. The trial court entered an order adjudging the father to be the father of the mother's daughter. The father later took the daughter to the father's home in Nevada. Following a hearing on the mother's petition for temporary child support, custody, and injunctive relief, the trial court ordered the father to return the daughter to the mother. The trial court later found the father in willful contempt for his failure to return the daughter. The father appealed, contending that the trial court was without authority to grant custody of the daughter to the mother because the father had already been adjudged as the father and the mother's complaint in the paternity action did not pray for custodial relief. On appeal, the court held that because the trial court's paternity order contained no provisions for the support of the child, the trial court retained jurisdiction of the case and the authority to make further determinations in accordance with Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 40, para. 1363 (1983) and because the paternity order was not a final judgment, the trial court retained its statutory authority to determine custody.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, which had found the father in contempt for failing to relinquish custody of his daughter to her mother.

In re Marriage of Mullins


No. 4-84-0910


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


135 Ill. App. 3d 279; 481 N.E.2d 322; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 2252; 89 Ill. Dec. 771



July 18, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of McLean County; the Hon. William M. Roberts, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent husband appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of McLean County (Illinois) requiring the husband to pay petitioner wife child support in the wife's proceeding to have their divorce decree, which was issued by a foreign country, established and registered.


OVERVIEW: The husband and wife were divorced by a decree from a foreign country. The wife filed a petition to have that decree established and registered. The husband requested a determination of visitation rights. The trial court entered an order allowing the prayer of the petition and awarding custody to the wife. The court entered a second order on oral stipulation regarding visitation rights. That order contained a provision that child support would be paid in accordance with the decrees and orders of the foreign court. On the wife's petition to modify the judgment to order child support, the trial court entered a judgment in her favor. The court reversed, finding that the trial court's second agreed order only evidenced an intent that the foreign court would continue to have jurisdiction over a determination of child support and did not incorporate the divorce decree insofar as it contained an order of child support. Therefore, there was no valid order of support for the trial court to modify. In addition, the trial court lacked subject matter jurisdiction because the registration and enforcement of a judgment of a foreign country in a matrimonial matter was not a justiciable matter.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment, which ordered the husband to pay child support in response to the wife's petition to modify a judgment registering the parties' foreign divorce decree.

 

1057 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People ex rel. Redd v. Mulholland


No. 3-84-0805


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


134 Ill. App. 3d 929; 481 N.E.2d 307; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 2186; 89 Ill. Dec. 756



July 17, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of La Salle County; the Hon. Robert L. Carter, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant putative father challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court of La Salle County (Illinois), which denied his motion to dismiss plaintiff mother's paternity action and which found him to be the father of a child born out of wedlock to the mother.


OVERVIEW: The mother had previously filed a paternity complaint but dismissed it without prejudice. After the trial court denied the putative father's motion to dismiss, he admitted paternity. The father argued that the dismissal of the first complaint barred further litigation of the issue of his paternity. On appeal, the court disagreed. The phrase, "without prejudice" signified that the dismissal had been taken with no decision on the merits of the case and, therefore, without prejudice to refiling. Once the action was voluntarily dismissed, the mother was free to commence a new action within one year or within the remaining period of limitation for the action, whichever was greater, under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 83, par. 24a (1979). The prior statute of limitation for paternity actions had been ruled unconstitutional, and there was no limitation period for the filing of a paternity complaint during the minority of the child. The mother clearly possessed the right to refile the paternity complaint. The second complaint was not restricted to any limitation period because the former statutory two-year time limit was no longer valid. Therefore, the second paternity action was timely filed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

People v. Young


Nos. 83-1066, 84-372 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


136 Ill. App. 3d 107; 482 N.E.2d 1008; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 2369; 90 Ill. Dec. 725



July 15, 1985, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied October 1, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County; the Hon. John L. Hughes, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the order of the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois), which denied his petition for a new trial under the Post-Conviction Hearing Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 122 -- 1 et seq. (1981). The trial court vacated an initial denial order after the appeal was filed. Another trial court judge subsequently denied the petition and an amended notice of appeal was filed.


OVERVIEW: The court considered the threshold issue of which trial order was under appeal. The court held that the trial court lost jurisdiction when the appeal was initially filed so that the proceeding on the motion to vacate and all subsequent proceedings were void. The court noted that although newly enacted Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 122 -- 8 (1984) provided that all proceedings under the Post-Conviction Hearing Act shall be conducted and all petitions shall be considered by a judge who was not involved in the original proceeding that resulted in conviction, defendant had waived recusal by not objecting to the trial judge hearing the petition. The court then considered whether it should re-evaluate defendant's sole remaining issue, a claim for ineffective assistance of counsel that had been raised on direct appeal. The court found that defendant's alleged new facts outside the record added nothing to the claim. The court also held that the newly adopted Strickland test for ineffective assistance claims was substantially the same as the prior Illinois test used by the court on direct appeal, so that fundamental fairness did not require a re-evaluation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that dismissed defendant's post-conviction petition.

People v. Valentin


No. 82-1608


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


135 Ill. App. 3d 22; 480 N.E.2d 1351; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 2218; 89 Ill. Dec. 608



July 12, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. John J. Crowley, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which, after a jury trial, convicted him of possession of a controlled substance and possession with intent to deliver a controlled substance, to wit heroin, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, para. 1401, 1402 and 1204(c)(12) (1981), and sentenced him to 25 years' imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Upon an informant's statements, the police obtained a warrant that authorized the search of a specific individual, as well as for heroin and proof of residence. The police knocked and announced, heard noises and broke down the door. Defendant matched the description of the man in the warrant, and a search disclosed heroin. Defendant sought to run and was subdued. On appeal from defendant's possession conviction, the court affirmed. The court held that the police had probable cause to arrest defendant for possession of a controlled substance. The police had reliable information, defendant matched the description, they found heroin, and defendant attempted to flee. A common sense view of these circumstances would lead a cautious person to believe that defendant committed the offense. The jury was entitled to infer defendant's constructive possession of the heroin, and find that he had both the power and the intention to exercise control over the heroin either directly or through another person. Defendant's claim that the prosecutor made inflammatory statements to the jury was waived where he failed to raise the specific comments in his motion for a mistrial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for possession of, and possession with intent to deliver, a controlled substance.

People ex rel. Foreman v. Sojourners Motorcycle Club, Ltd.

Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District

July 5, 1985, Filed

DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a motorcycle club and its members, sought review of the interlocutory order of the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois), granting plaintiff state's attorney's petition for a preliminary injunction to enjoin the club from selling or distributing alcohol on specified premises and from using those premises in any manner not authorized under a county zoning ordinance.


OVERVIEW: The state's attorney's office filed a complaint alleging that a motorcycle club was distributing alcoholic beverages without a liquor license in violation of county zoning and liquor control ordinances and that such use constituted a public nuisance. The trial court granted a preliminary injunction, finding the club's use of the property to be a public nuisance and a violation of both the Liquor Control Act of 1934, Ill. Rev. On appeal, the club contended that the information underlying the complaint was gained by a search of the premises without consent in violation of the federal and state constitutions and that portions of the zoning ordinance abridged their right to peaceable assembly in violation of the First Amendment. The court affirmed the judgment. It held that the Act implicitly authorized a county zoning officer to procure and execute an administrative search warrant. It also held that the ordinance furthered an important and substantial public interest and that the incidental restriction on the club members' First Amendment rights was no greater than necessary to the furtherance of that interest.

People ex rel. Moore v. McIntosh


No. 5-84-0616


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


134 Ill. App. 3d 1070; 481 N.E.2d 833; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 2209; 90 Ill. Dec. 33



July 5, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of St. Clair County; the Hon. Roger M. Scrivner, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff State, on behalf of a mother, appealed a decision of the Circuit Court of St. Clair County (Illinois), which found that the State had not sufficiently stated a cause of action in its action to establish the paternity of defendant alleged father, had failed to timely comply with discovery, and had not filed the action within the limitations period of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 40, para. 1354, so dismissed the complaint.


OVERVIEW: On March, 19, 1983, the State filed an action under para. 1354 on behalf of the mother, asserting the alleged father's paternity of the mother's child, born out of wedlock on January, 20, 1978. The trial court dismissed the complaint with prejudice, finding that the State had not sufficiently stated a cause of action, had failed to timely comply with discovery, and had not filed the action with the limitations period. On appeal, the court reversed. The court held that a cause of action was stated, the parties were aware that the two-year limitations period was unconstitutional, and that dismissal of the action as untimely abrogated the intent of the Illinois Parentage Act of 1984. The court found that while the State committed a discovery order violation, it was not unreasonable or a contumacious disregard of its duties under the order, which effectively gave a one-week period in which to meet the father's requests. The court found that an obvious purpose of the statute was to convert a moral duty of support into a legal one and to prevent the child from becoming a public charge, so the dismissal was a drastic action for a single discovery violation, and an abuse of discretion.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's dismissal of the State's paternity action and remanded for further proceedings.

People v. Dale


No. 5-84-0761


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


135 Ill. App. 3d 15; 481 N.E.2d 821; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 2217; 90 Ill. Dec. 21



July 3, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Saline County; the Hon. Michael Henshaw, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant attorney appealed a decision of the Circuit Court of Saline County (Illinois), which after convicting his client, defendant, of all charges against him in an underlying criminal cocaine-related case, held that defendant's bail deposit should be applied to payment of a fine levied against him by the trial court.


OVERVIEW: Defendant posted $ 20,000 in bail and signed two bail bonds which provided, in part, that if a judgment was entered against him for a fine and/or court costs, the balance of the deposit, after deduction of bail bond costs, would be applied to payment of such fines and/or costs. Defendant later assigned to the attorney a sufficient part of the deposit to pay his fees and costs. Defendant was found guilty of all charges, which included cocaine delivery. The trial court fined him $ 139,200 pursuant to § 5-9-1.1 (Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-9-1.1 (1983)) of the Illinois Unified Code of Corrections and ruled that part of the fine would be satisfied from the bail deposits, which took precedent over the attorney's fees insofar as application of the bail money was concerned. The attorney appealed, arguing that the bail deposits should have been used to pay his fees and not defendant's fine. The court affirmed, concluding that the attorney, as assignee, had acquired defendant's interests, which included the bail bond agreements, that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 110-7 revealed no contrary intent, and that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-9-1.1 (1983) was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision that defendant's fine took precedence over the attorney's costs and fees insofar as defendant's bail deposits were concerned.

Meeker v. Tulis


No. 5-84-0802


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


134 Ill. App. 3d 1093; 481 N.E.2d 810; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 2213; 90 Ill. Dec. 10



July 1, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of St. Clair County; the Hon. Thomas P. O'Donnell, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff seller sought review from a judgment of the Circuit Court of St. Clair County (Illinois), which dismissed his action against defendant buyer seeking to collect payments allegedly due under an installment contract for the sale of a dwelling.


OVERVIEW: The seller sued the buyer to recover payments due under their installment contract for the sale of a dwelling. The buyer moved to dismiss, arguing that the contract was voidable because the seller failed to provide information about the dwelling's compliance with applicable codes, as required by Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 29, para. 8.22 (1983). The court granted the buyer's motion and dismissed with prejudice. On appeal, the seller argued that the statute was unconstitutional. The court upheld the statute. The state had a legitimate interest related to public health, safety, welfare, or morals in protecting inexperienced buyers from overreaching sellers. The seller failed to prove that the statute was an unreasonable means to achieve that purpose or that the classification of installment contracts was arbitrary or unrelated to the purpose. Finally, the seller's due process rights were not violated because he could overcome any presumption that the dwelling was in violation of a code by warranting that it was not.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

Heitz v. Hogan


No. 4-84-0641


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


134 Ill. App. 3d 352; 480 N.E.2d 185; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 2113; 89 Ill. Dec. 299



June 27, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Piatt County; the Hon. John P. Shonkwiler, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff decedent's administrator challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court of Piatt County (Illinois) that was entered in favor of defendants, drivers and their employers, in the administrator's wrongful death action based on the decedent's collision with the rear of one of the drivers' vehicles.


OVERVIEW: A judgment was entered for defendants in the administrator's wrongful death action based on the decedent's collision with the rear of one of the drivers' vehicles. The court reversed because the trial court failed to instruct the jury with a definition of proximate cause. The trial court's refusal to give the administrator's instruction regarding proximate cause was sufficiently prejudicial to require a new trial because it offered instruction for the case where the accident could have been caused by two distinct acts, one driver stopping in the northbound lane and the other driver stopping in the southbound lane, and because the trial court then neglected to offer any instruction defining proximate cause. The statutory provision providing for admission of the medical report to the coroner was constitutional because the legislature had the power to prescribe new and alter existing rules of evidence or to prescribe methods of proof, and the report was not inadmissible "reconstruction testimony" where it did not state the speed that the decedent was travelling at the time of the accident and the statement of the time of the accident was not deduced by reconstructing the accident.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that was entered in favor of defendants in the administrator's wrongful death action based on the decedent's collision with the rear of one of the drivers' vehicles and remanded for a new trial.

Blazejewski v. Board of Fire & Police Comm'rs


No. 84-532


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


134 Ill. App. 3d 222; 480 N.E.2d 170; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 2096; 89 Ill. Dec. 284



June 25, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County; the Hon. John Teschner, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff officer appealed a decision of the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), which denied his motion for summary judgment and granted a motion for judgment on the pleadings by defendant Board of Fire and Police Commissioners of the Village of Hinsdale (Illinois) in the officer's action for a declaratory judgment that he was entitled to 3.5 veterans' preference points to be added to his rating for promotion to police sergeant.


OVERVIEW: The officer served in the United States Marine Corps and received an honorable discharge. He then became a police officer. He took an exam for promotion to sergeant and was ranked fourth on a list that rated officers according to the sum of their score on the exam and seniority points. Only the top three officers were to be promoted. The officer's score failed to include his veterans' preference points under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 24, para. 10-2.1-10 (1983). The board changed his score, but only awarded him 2.8 points. The officer sought a declaratory judgment that he was entitled to 3.5 veterans' points. He filed a motion for summary judgment, which was denied. The board filed a motion for judgment on the pleadings, which was granted. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded. The court held that the officer was entitled to veterans' points for the period between his induction into the military and his reporting because from the moment of induction he was a member of the Armed Forces subject to the jurisdiction of the military. The fact that he was given a period of time between induction and reporting for service in no way altered his status as a member of the Armed Forces.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the circuit court and remanded the cause with directions that an order be entered allowing the officer's motion for summary judgment and that a writ of mandamus be issued requiring the board to credit the officer with 3.5 veterans' preference points.

People v. Otis


No. 84-0396


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


135 Ill. App. 3d 718; 479 N.E.2d 40; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 2306; 88 Ill. Dec. 705



June 17, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County; the Hon. William E. Black, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), which convicted him of residential burglary pursuant to his plea of guilty and sentenced him to eight years imprisonment. He argued that he was denied assistance of counsel. Defendant further argued that the residential burglary statute and the applicable sentencing statutes were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: After being charged with residential burglary, defendant pleaded not guilty. He filed a petition to elect treatment pursuant to the Dangerous Drug Abuse Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 91 1/2, para. 120.10 (1983). Counsel represented to the trial court that in order for defendant to be accepted or considered for the program that he had to first plead guilty. Defendant's changed plea was accepted. The parole board refused to consent to the election of treatment. Defendant's motion to withdraw his guilty plea was denied. On appeal, defendant asserted that his counsel's misapprehension that he had to plead guilty to elect treatment and counsel's failure to determine whether the board would consent to his election prior to the plea was ineffective assistance. The court found that under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 91 1/2, para. 120.9 (1983) counsel misapprehended that a plea was required first and that defendant established prejudice arising from that incompetence. Defendant would not have pleaded guilty had counsel made inquiries of the board where they would have revealed that they would not accept that election. The court found that no substantial question of constitutionality had been raised.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the judgment of the trial court with directions that defendant be permitted to withdraw his guilty plea and plead anew.

 

1068 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Royal Liquor Mart, Inc. v. Rockford


No. 84-0471


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


133 Ill. App. 3d 868; 479 N.E.2d 485; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 2037; 88 Ill. Dec. 872



June 12, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County; the Hon. John E. Sype, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff liquor store sought review of a decision by the Circuit Court of Winnebago County (Illinois), which found in favor of defendant city in the liquor store's action to enjoin the city from collecting a one percent sales tax on food, beverages, liquor and rentals on hotel and motel rooms, and to recover all taxes collected thereunder.


OVERVIEW: The liquor store brought an action against the city to enjoin it from collecting a one percent sales tax on food, beverages, liquor and rentals on hotel and motel rooms, and to recover all taxes collected thereunder. The liquor store argued that the city lost its authority to collect the tax after the city's home rule powers, under Ill. Const. art., § 6(a), were repealed by a referendum. The lower court found in favor of the city. Upon appeal, the court affirmed, holding that the tax was levied at the time it was imposed by the legislature. Thus, the act of collecting the tax was an administrative function, and it was the act of determining and fixing the amount of the tax that constituted its levy. Because the tax was levied at a time when the city had the authority to levy, there was no reason to presume that the subsequent referendum repealing home rule authority invalidated the future collection of the sales tax. Because the burden of establishing the invalidity of the tax rested upon the liquor store and because the liquor store presented no clear authority to support its contention, the court affirmed the trial court's determination that the tax be given continued effect.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of the city and upheld the tax.

 

1069 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. White


No. 84-0059


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


134 Ill. App. 3d 262; 479 N.E.2d 1121; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 2101; 89 Ill. Dec. 115



June 12, 1985, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied July 15, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County; the Hon. Richard F. Weiler, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, vacated in part, modified in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision of the Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois), which convicted defendant of home invasion and residential burglary, in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 12 (1983) and Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 19 (1983).


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed the convictions of defendant, rejecting defendant's contention that he was not proven guilty beyond a reasonable doubt because the only witness who identified him was an accomplice who negotiated a favorable disposition of the charges against her in return for her testimony. The court held that this testimony, even when viewed with the scrutiny accorded such testimony, was greatly corroborated by defendants' own statements, the jury was aware of the extent of the accomplice's involvement, and the jury was given an instruction on accomplice testimony. The court held that any error by the improper questions of the prosecutor, concerning the taking of rape-kit evidence, was cured when the jury was advised that there was no evidence of rape. The court vacated the sentence for residential burglary, holding that the trial court erred in sentencing defendant to an extended term for this offense. The court concluded that defendant could have only been sentenced to an extended term for the most serious class of offense for which he was convicted, which in this case was home invasion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction of defendant for home invasion and residential burglary. The court vacated the sentence for residential burglary and sentenced defendant to 15 years in the Department of Corrections for that offense, with the sentences for home invasion and residential burglary to run concurrently.

 

1070 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Heiple


No. 3-84-0609


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


133 Ill. App. 3d 583; 478 N.E.2d 1388; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 1991; 88 Ill. Dec. 662



June 5, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Peoria County; the Hon. Arthur H. Gross, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the Circuit Court of Peoria County (Illinois), which found defendant guilty, on an Illinois conservation citation and complaint, of the offense of operating a watercraft without a personal flotation device (PFD) aboard in violation of § 4-1 of the Boat Registration and Safety Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 314-1 (1983).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was operating a windsurfer at a beach location on a river. During the operation, defendant was not wearing, nor was the windsurfer equipped with a PFD. The parties agree that it was a nuisance and hindrance for defendant to have worn a PFD, although one could have been attached to some portion of the mast. Defendant was found guilty of violating the Act. On appeal, defendant argued that the Act was unconstitutional and that a windsurfer was not a "vessel" or "watercraft" within the meaning of the Act. The court reversed the judgment and held that, while the Act was constitutional, a windsurfer was not a "vessel" or "watercraft" within the definition of the Act as a matter of law. A windsurfer could have been used as a means of transportation on water, but it was not commonly so used. In the same sense, it was capable of having been used as a means of transportation on water, but it was not commonly done. The court relied on the definition of "vessel" as applied to the Jones Act, in which it was held that not everything that floated was a "vessel."


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's conviction of defendant for violating the Act by operating a watercraft without a PFD aboard.

 

1071 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Bowen


No. 83-2492


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


133 Ill. App. 3d 994; 479 N.E.2d 997; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 2053; 88 Ill. Dec. 977



May 28, 1985, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 26, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Fred G. Suria, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which imposed a sentence of natural life imprisonment under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-8-1(a)(1)(b) (1983). Following a previous appeal, the court had remanded for resentencing. Defendant had been convicted in a jury trial of murder, attempted murder, and armed robbery.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for shooting and killing a security guard and injuring another person after shoplifting clothing. The initial sentence was reversed for allowing defendant to waive a presentence investigation report. On remand, the circuit court found no circumstances to permit imposition of an extended-term sentence under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-8-2 (1983). Defendant was resentenced under the provisions of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-8-1(a)(1)(b). On appeal, defendant challenged the constitutionality of para. 1005-8-1(a)(1), arguing that the statute curtailed the sentencing judge's discretion by failing to provide an incremental range of penalties. Defendant cited no relevant case law to support her due process argument, which the court rejected, finding that defendant failed to rebut the statute's presumed constitutionality. The court also rejected her argument that the sentence imposed was an abuse of discretion because it failed to consider her potential for rehabilitation. The record showed that the sentencing judge considered all the relevant factors in reaching its sentencing decision. Under the circumstances, the sentence imposed was appropriate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment sentencing defendant to life imprisonment.

 

1072 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Weitzman v. Cook County


No. 84-1188


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


133 Ill. App. 3d 1013; 479 N.E.2d 957; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 2058; 88 Ill. Dec. 937



May 23, 1985, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied July 15, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. George Higgins, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted the motion of defendant county board (board) to dismiss the taxpayer's complaint on the basis that he lacked standing to assert the rights of a taxing district and that he failed to show that the board had abused its discretion.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer sought injunctive relief to restrain the board from violating its fiduciary duty by awarding properties purchased at a scavenger sale to Neighborhood Housing Development Organizations (NHDO) rather than selling them to the highest bidders. The trial court granted the motion to dismiss. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court noted that the taxpayer was granted leave to amend to allege that a demand had been made and that the proper authorities refused to act or that such a demand would have been futile, a precondition to bringing a taxpayer's action, but that he failed to do so. The court held that the statute that authorized the sale or assignment of the tracts of land contained no guarantee that the land would be sold to the highest bidder, and that the board had attempted to fulfill the primary purpose of the Scavenger Act. Thus, the court held that because the taxpayer failed to present factual averments in his pleading to show that 1) a prior demand had been made on the taxing body, and 2) that the board had acted unlawfully or irregularly, or 3) that the statute was unconstitutional, the motion to dismiss was properly granted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court to dismiss the taxpayer's complaint.

In re Application of Cook County Collector


No. 84-1292


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


133 Ill. App. 3d 208; 478 N.E.2d 1119; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 1941; 88 Ill. Dec. 511



May 16, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Joseph Schneider, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which overruled the taxpayer's objections to the payment under protest of his 1974 real estate taxes levied by appellee county collector on behalf of several taxing bodies and found in favor of the collector.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer contended that the equalization provisions of the Revenue Act of 1939, as amended, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 627 et seq. (1972), could not constitutionally be applied to the county under Ill. Const. art. IX, § 4(b) (1970). The court determined that equalization was required by statute and applied to the county because aggregate assessed valuation of all real property in each county had to be equalized so that the aggregate assessed valuations would have been proportionate to fair cash value in all counties. The court explained that there was no indication in the statute that the Department of Local Government Affairs (Illinois) was to disregard the statutory mandate to equalize assessments in all counties at the 50 percent of actual value level as specified under the Act. The court noted that the Department had no authority to revise or change any individual assessments made by local assessing officers. The court concluded that once local assessments were made, the Department was directed by statute to equalize assessments between counties so that in all counties the aggregate value of property would have been assessed at its fair cash value.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

East Moline v. Bracke, Hayes & Miller


No. 3-84-0117


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


133 Ill. App. 3d 136; 478 N.E.2d 637; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 1932; 88 Ill. Dec. 322



May 10, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Rock Island County; the Hon. L. E. Ellison, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Third-party plaintiff architects sought review of the judgment from the Circuit Court of Rock Island County (Illinois), which dismissed their third-party complaint against third-party defendant consulting engineer in plaintiff city's suit for negligence arising from the construction of a municipal swimming pool.


OVERVIEW: The city filed a suit against the architects for negligence arising from the construction of a municipal swimming pool building. The architects filed a third-party complaint against the project engineer and consulting engineer. The circuit court granted the consulting engineer's motion to dismiss the complaint against him on the ground that as a nonresident, he was not subject to the jurisdiction of the Illinois courts. On appeal, the architects asserted that personal jurisdiction of the consulting engineer was predicated upon § 2-209 of the Illinois long-arm statute, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 2-209 (1983). The court affirmed the judgment dismissing the complaint against the consulting engineer. The court held that an exchange of phone calls and correspondence did not support jurisdiction over the consulting engineer, where his employment under the construction contract was performed entirely from outside the state. The consulting engineer was not subject to the jurisdiction of the Illinois courts, because he had not transacted any business within the state or committed a tortious act within the state.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment dismissing the architects' third-party complaint against the consulting engineer.

People v. Knight


No. 81-2797


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


133 Ill. App. 3d 248; 478 N.E.2d 1082; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 1948; 88 Ill. Dec. 474



May 8, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. John A. McElligott, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which, after a bench trial, found him guilty of and sentenced him for five counts of drug possession and possession with intent to deliver cocaine, cannabis, and PCP in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, paras. 1402(a)(7)(iii), 1401(a)(7)(iii), 1402(b), 704(d), 705(d) (1979).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was the owner of a store for which the police obtained a search warrant and found various drugs. Defendant asserted that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, paras. 1402(a)(7)(iii), 1401(a)(7)(iii), 704(d), 705(d) (1979) were violative of the equal protection and due process clauses of the Illinois and United States constitutions because they imposed different penalties for duplicative acts. On appeal, the court reversed the judgement below in part and affirmed it in part. The court rejected defendant's arguments as waived for failure to preserve, but found that the equal protection clause did not deny states the power to treat different classes of persons differently. The court vacated defendant's convictions for possession of cannabis, possession of PCP, and possession of cocaine because it found that defendant could not stand convicted of both possession and possession with intent to deliver since the former was a lesser included offense of the latter. Based upon the amount of PCP or cannabis in defendant's possession, the court found that the trial court could have properly inferred that such were possessed with intent to deliver.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's convictions for possession of PCP, possession of cocaine, and possession of cannabis, but affirmed the remainder the judgment.

Citizens Utilities Co. v. Illinois Pollution Control Bd.


No. 3-84-0413


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


133 Ill. App. 3d 406; 478 N.E.2d 853; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 1967; 88 Ill. Dec. 362



May 3, 1985, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 19, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Will County; the Hon. Edward D. Smith, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant utility companies challenged the decision of the Circuit Court of Will County (Illinois), which affirmed a decision by appellee, the Pollution Control Board, to revoke the certification of the utility companies' plants as "pollution control facilities" as that term was defined in section 21a-2 of the Revenue Act of 1939, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 502a-2 (1983).


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to Public Act 83-883 (Act), the Pollution Control Board revoked the certification of the utility companies' wastewater treatment plants as "pollution control facilities" under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 502a-2 (1983). The lower court affirmed. On appeal, the utility companies argued that the Act was unconstitutional because it created irrelevant and artificial differences between wastewater treatment plants owned and operated by the utility companies and all other pollution control facilities; between the utility companies' plants and wastewater treatment plants that processed nonsewage wastewater; and between the utility companies' plants and wastewater treatment plants operated by governments. The court disagreed and affirmed. The court held that a rational basis for the distinction between sewage treatment facilities and other types of pollution control devices existed. The court noted that sewage treatment plants provided the service ultimately sold by the company, whereas industrial pollutants were byproducts of the ultimate service or product sold by the company. The court held that the classifications under the Act were not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the Pollution Control Board to revoke the certification of the utility companies' plants as "pollution control facilities."

 

1077 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Baugh


No. 4-84-0727


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


132 Ill. App. 3d 713; 477 N.E.2d 724; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 1864; 87 Ill. Dec. 598



April 24, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Macon County; the Hon. Rodney A. Scott, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate appealed the order of the Circuit Court of Macon County (Illinois), which dismissed, as meritless, his request for post-conviction relief and appointment of counsel by respondent state.


OVERVIEW: After losing an appeal of his conviction for felony theft, the inmate filed a pro se post-conviction petition and request for appointment of counsel. The circuit court dismissed the petition as without merit and refused to appoint counsel. The inmate appealed. The court affirmed because the constitutional challenge to Ill. Code Crim. P., Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 122 -- 2.1 (1984), was without merit. The court found that § 122 -- 2.1 dealt with post-conviction procedure at the trial level and did not usurp the supreme court's power to make rules regarding appeals. The court found that the state did not deprive the indigent due process or pursuing a meritorious post-conviction petition by providing, in § 122 -- 2.1, that the trial court make a determination that the petition had merit before appointing counsel. The court found that § 122 -- 2.1 did not violate equal protection because the different treatment of indigents in the direct appeal, during which the state had the burden of proof, and in the post-conviction petition, during which the indigent had the burden, had a rational basis.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the inmate's request for relief from his state conviction and for appointment of counsel.

S & D Service, Inc. v. 915-925 W. Schubert Condominium Asso.


No. 84-1035


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


132 Ill. App. 3d 1019; 478 N.E.2d 478; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 1908; 88 Ill. Dec. 163



April 23, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Jerome Garoon, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant lessor appealed an order from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which found that plaintiff lessee was entitled to possession of a laundry room facility in the lessee's action for forcible entry and detainer. The lessee filed its action after the lessor cancelled a lease agreement with the lessee pursuant to the Illinois Condominium Property Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 30, para. 318.2 (1979).


OVERVIEW: The lessor was a condominium association although the developer originally executed the lease for the operation of a laundry facility. The lease covered a five-year period. The lessor cancelled the lease and when the lessor did not relinquish the premises by removing its equipment, the lessor had the equipment removed. On appeal, the issue was who had the superior right of possession. The court reversed the judgment in favor of the lessee. Section 318.2 was incorporated into the lease and allowed termination of leases executed by a developer that extended for more than two years beyond the date of the filing of a condominiums declaration. The lessor properly terminated the lease under the provisions of § 318.2. Once the lease was terminated, the lessee had no right to possession. Because the lessor raised the termination of the lease as an affirmative defense the trial court erred in finding the lessee had the right of possession. The court further held that § 318.2 was a constitutionally valid exercise of the state's police powers.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment in favor of the lessee in its forcible entry and detainer action.

People v. Reynolds


No. 84-1339


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


132 Ill. App. 3d 559; 478 N.E.2d 33; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 1843; 87 Ill. Dec. 894



April 16, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Edwin J. Richardson, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the suspension of his driver's license based upon his refusal to take a breathalyzer test following his arrest for driving under the influence of alcohol and improper lane usage in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois).


OVERVIEW: When police stopped defendant, they detected the odor of alcohol. Defendant suffered an asthma attack in the police car. He took his medicine and then refused to take a breathalyzer test. The trial court found that defendant was able but refused to submit to the breathalyzer test and suspended his driver's license. On appeal, defendant argued that he was unable to take the breathalyzer test because of the asthma attack and therefore did not refuse to take it. The court affirmed. The court noted that the lower court chose to believe evidence from police that defendant's breathing returned to normal and that he could have taken the test but refused. Defendant failed to present medical evidence that it took a day or two before he could resume normal breathing. The lower court's finding was therefore not against the manifest weight of the evidence. The court held the availability of alternative tests was immaterial in light of the holding that defendant's breathing returned to normal after he took his medicine. The court rejected defendant's argument that the implied consent law as applied to him violated his fourteenth amendment rights of due process and equal protection.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed suspension of defendant's driver's license.

Family Life League v. Department of Public Aid


No. 82-651


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


132 Ill. App. 3d 929; 478 N.E.2d 432; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 1898; 88 Ill. Dec. 117



April 10, 1985, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 4, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Arthur L. Dunne, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, antiabortion group and officers, appealed the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) that issued a writ of mandamus and entered judgment on the pleadings ordering that defendant Illinois Department of Public Aid (department) was not required to provide records as to the number of welfare abortions but was required to provide the names and addresses of the doctors and providers. The department cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: The antiabortion group sought an order to force the department to provide records related to the use of public funds paid to doctors and medical providers for welfare abortions. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded, holding that otherwise required disclosure of public records had to yield to the constitutionally protected privacy right of women on welfare to make and effectuate their abortion decisions because compelling disclosure of the physicians and providers would have resulted in their unwillingness to perform legal abortions for welfare recipients in light of the social climate of dangerous emotional highs on both sides of the abortion issue with insidious threats of harassment and harm to physicians performing legal abortions and the terrorism of abortion clinics by antiabortion vigilante groups. The court also held that the disclosure of the information, either by deleting information from the existing record or by extracting information, did not require the creation of a new public record pursuant to the State Records Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 116, para. 43.4 et seq. (1979), and the Freedom of Information Act, Ill. Ann. Stat. ch. 116, para. 43.29 (Supp. 1984-85).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's issuance of a writ of mandamus and the entry of judgment on the pleadings in favor of the department in plaintiffs' action seeking records related to the use of public funds paid to doctors and medical providers for welfare abortions.

Boyd v. Ford


No. 5-83-0674


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


133 Ill. App. 3d 626; 479 N.E.2d 337; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 1999; 88 Ill. Dec. 724



April 4, 1985, Filed

DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner voter sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court of Madison County (Illinois), which affirmed a decision of the Township Electoral Board that dismissed a petition filed by the voter against respondents, the objector and the township supervisor, to call a referendum upon a proposition to discontinue the maintenance and operation of a township hospital.


OVERVIEW: The voter petitioned the township to call a referendum pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 139, para. 160.3 upon a proposition to discontinue the maintenance and operation of a township hospital. An objection that the township hospital was organized pursuant to the authority of the Township Hospital Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch.139, paras. 160.6 - 160.16 (1945) and that the legislature had not provided a method where the voters of a town could seek a referendum filed by the objector. The Township Electoral Board sustained the objection and provided that the referendum procedure provided in Ill. Rev.
