On appeal, the court found that the trial court had authority to review a final judgment of the Township Electoral Board. The court held that the Township Hospital Fund Act had no express application to the Township Hospital Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 139, paras. 160.6-160.16 (1945) because the legislature had not provided any means for discontinuance of operations of a township hospital.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court.

 

1082 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Brown v. Mason


No. 4-84-0464


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


132 Ill. App. 3d 439; 477 N.E.2d 61; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 1827; 87 Ill. Dec. 460



April 1, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Vermilion County; the Hon. Carl A. Lund, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff victim challenged the decision of the Circuit Court of Vermilion County (Illinois), which dismissed her medical malpractice claim against defendant tortfeasors, holding that the action was barred.


OVERVIEW: A surgical sterilization had been performed on the victim, but she later became pregnant. Under both negligence and breach of contract, she filed for damages for pain of pregnancy and childbirth, loss of income, medical expenses, and child-rearing expenses. The trial court held that her complaint was barred by Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 13 -- 212 (1983), because it was filed more than four years after the surgery. On review, the victim contended that a different statutory period should have been applied. The court affirmed. The court found that the victim must have discovered that the tortfeasors' representations about the surgery were false sometime between the date she became pregnant and the date she delivered. The court determined, therefore, that the date of discovery was between 5 1/2 months and almost 15 months prior to the date the statute of limitations would have run. The court concluded that with the exercise of diligence, the victim's cause of action would not have been barred.


OUTCOME: The order dismissing the medical malpractice action because it was barred was affirmed.

 

1083 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Krankel


No. 4-84-0577


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


131 Ill. App. 3d 887; 476 N.E.2d 777; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 1751; 87 Ill. Dec. 75



March 29, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of McLean County; the Hon. William T. Caisley, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of McLean County (Illinois), which convicted him of burglary and sentenced him to imprisonment that was consecutive to concurrent sentences he was then serving.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that he was not proven guilty beyond a reasonable doubt, that he was denied effective assistance of counsel, and that the trial court erred in sentencing. The court found that defense counsel was not ineffective because he allegedly failed to investigate defendant's alibi. Defense counsel investigated the alibi, but because it could not be verified, he made a strategic decision to not present it. This did not constitute ineffective assistance. The uncorroborated accomplice testimony of defendant's wife was the key element in the state's case and was sufficient to sustain the conviction. The jury was aware of the issue surrounding her credibility in evaluating her testimony. Defendant's actions to which his wife testified were not substitutes for speech. Thus, her testimony did not violate marital privilege. The sentencing court could consider defendant's prior convictions in sentencing as aggravating factors. The extended sentence he received as a result of three separate sentences by three different counts was not improper and would not be modified absent an abuse of discretion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction and sentencing.

 

1084 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Curtis


Nos. 83-2339, 83-2395 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


132 Ill. App. 3d 241; 476 N.E.2d 1162; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 1805; 87 Ill. Dec. 170



March 29, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Richard J. Petrarca, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted them of armed robbery.


OVERVIEW: Defendants asserted that his Sixth Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. XIV, right to counsel was violated after adversarial judicial proceedings had been initiated against them and because of the exploitation of the results of that constitutional violation at trial. Specifically, defendants argued that their constitutional right to counsel at a lineup was violated, and therefore the lineup evidence and the in-court identifications of defendants at trial should have been suppressed. The court agreed with defendants and reversed the conviction. The court found that adversarial judicial proceedings had already been initiated against defendants before the lineups took place, thus defendants' Sixth Amendment right to assistance of counsel had already attached at the time of the lineups. Thus, defendants should had had the right to counsel at the lineups. Further, the court found that defendants did not intelligently waive his constitutional right to assistance of counsel because he did not know that the police could not demand that he appear at the lineup without assistance of counsel. Thus, the court erred in finding a waiver.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the convictions of defendants.

 

1085 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Schlenz v. Castle


No. 2-84-0301


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


132 Ill. App. 3d 993; 477 N.E.2d 697; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 1907; 87 Ill. Dec. 571



March 26, 1985, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Supplemental Opinion Filed on Denial of Rehearing May 24, 1985, Reported at 132 Ill. App. 3d 993 at 1016.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County; the Hon. Robert K. McQueen, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff claimant appealed an order from the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois), granting defendant city officials' motion to deny, and an objection to the motion for, determination of a class in a class action determination.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff claimants brought an action against defendant city officials for allegedly failing to equalize real property assessments. The main issues on appeal were: whether the lack of a finding as to the existence of a subclass was error; whether the proposed substitute plaintiffs were properly dismissed as individuals for failure to exhaust their administrative remedies; whether notice must be given to members of the class where the class representative was not permitted to continue; and whether change of venue was improperly denied. The court held that the trial court acted properly in deciding defendants' motion to dismiss. Therefore, the trial court could not be charged with any error for the absence of a determination of whether a subclass existed. The court concluded the futility exception was not applicable to this case, and plaintiffs would not be relieved of their duty to pursue administrative remedies on that basis. Moreover, the court held that plaintiffs' notice contention was without merit, and that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying plaintiffs' motion for change of venue.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court granting defendant city officials' motion to deny, and an objection to the motion for, determination of a class in a class action determination. There was no error or abuse of the trial court's discretion in making its rulings.

 

1086 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Leonora


No. 83-1053


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


133 Ill. App. 3d 74; 477 N.E.2d 1277; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 1926; 87 Ill. Dec. 749



March 26, 1985, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 3, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County; the Hon. Lawrence D. Inglis, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a jury verdict of the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois), which found him guilty of reckless homicide. Defendant argued that the circuit court improperly excluded evidence of other accidents and subsequent safety measures, the circuit court erred regarding jury instructions and verdict forms, the state failed to prove guilt beyond a reasonable doubt, and that his sentence resulted from improper factors.


OVERVIEW: Defendant maintained that evidence of prior accidents should have been admitted to show that the road was unsafe. The court found that the evidence was properly excluded because record was incomplete with respect to the prior accidents. The court held that evidence of safety measures concerning the roadway taken after the collision involved herein was inadmissible to show contributory negligence by roadway authority. The court found that defendant had waived his right to object to the use of general verdict forms, jury instructions, and certain statements by the prosecutor. The court held that there was sufficient evidence presented to convict defendant under the counts alleging driving under the influence of alcohol. The court refused to create a rule that the circuit court in a criminal case must sua sponte sift through the evidentiary facts and inform the jury which combination thereof can support a finding beyond a reasonable doubt of each element of the offense. The court found that the state was correct in telling the jury that the proceeding was not a drunk-driving case. The court found that the superior court had not considered improper factors in imposing a sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court.

 

1087 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Bell


Nos. 83-1642, 83-1735 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


132 Ill. App. 3d 354; 476 N.E.2d 1239; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 1818; 87 Ill. Dec. 247



March 22, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Kenneth Gillis, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On consolidated appeals, defendants challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted them of rape, deviate sexual assault, robbery, and attempted deviate sexual assault. They argued that they were denied their right to confront the victim, that her preliminary hearing testimony was allowed at trial, and that the arresting officer was allowed to testify as to her identification of defendants.


OVERVIEW: At the preliminary hearing, the victim was the only witness to testify. She stated that she could see defendants' faces because they attacked her in a well-lighted park. The victim died of natural causes before trial. On appeal, the court determined that defendants' right to confrontation were not violated because her testimony at the preliminary hearing was admitted into evidence at trial. At the preliminary hearing, defense counsel was allowed to cross-examine the victim concerning her ability and opportunity to observe her attackers, her identification of any other persons as her assailants, and the specific elements of the crimes charged. The possibility that some inconsistencies in the victim's description of the offenders' clothing might have been adduced affected the weight to be given her testimony rather than its admissibility. The victim testified in her preliminary hearing testimony that she had pointed out both defendants, and no one else, to the police. When introduced at trial, her testimony regarding her identification of defendants was a sufficient foundation for the police officer's corroborative testimony. The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court on all issues raised by defendants.

People v. Blackwood


No. 3-84-0295


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


131 Ill. App. 3d 1018; 476 N.E.2d 742; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 1770; 87 Ill. Dec. 40



March 15, 1985, Filed

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Rock Island County (Illinois), which convicted him of violating an order of protection in derogation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 111- 3(a)(3) (1981) and Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 40, para. 2302-12a (1983). Defendant challenged the sufficiency of the complaint and the constitutionality of the Domestic Violence Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 40, paras. 2302-8(c)(1) through 2302-12(a) (1983).


OVERVIEW: The circuit court entered an order of protection on behalf of defendant's ex-wife. The order directed defendant to refrain from "striking, threatening, harassing or interfering with the personal liberty in any fashion" of his ex-wife. The ex-wife filed a criminal complaint against defendant alleging that he had violated the order of protection because he had threatened her and verbally harassed her. Defendant made an oral motion to dismiss the complaint for failure to state an offense and because the complaint lacked specificity. The circuit court denied the motion. The prosecution amended the complaint to add specific details for the benefit of the defense. The amended complaint alleged that defendant yelled at his ex-wife, called her a "whore, a dead bitch, and that he had a plot waiting for her" and that "it's not over" and that "he would get his chance." The court affirmed the conviction. The court held that: (1) § 111-3(a)(3) of the Criminal Code of 1961 did not require a specific mental state to violate the statute; (2) the complaint sufficiently placed defendant on notice of the charges made against him; and (3) the statute was not unconstitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court.

In re R.D.


No. 5-83-0340


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


131 Ill. App. 3d 612; 476 N.E.2d 62; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 1704; 86 Ill. Dec. 886



March 14, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of St. Clair County; the Hon. Milton Wharton, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a juvenile, challenged an order of the Circuit Court of St. Clair County (Illinois), which adjudicated him a delinquent in connection with a charge of sexual abuse of a child in violation of § 115-10 of the Criminal Code of 1963, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 115-10 (1982).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was adjudicated a delinquent. On appeal, he claimed that the admission of the hearsay testimony of a registered nurse and an investigator constituted reversible error. The court affirmed the adjudication, finding that (1) the corroborative complaint exception to the hearsay rule was codified in § 115-10 and applied in a sexual assault case to show that the alleged victim was not silent but made a complaint; (2) the section's application was not limited to cases where consent was an issue; and (3) the scope of the section was exceeded by the witnesses' testimony as to the victim's report of the details of the sexual activity, but no prejudicial error occurred because the victim was present in court and was subjected to cross examination.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the adjudication.

People v. Boswell


No. 83-169


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


132 Ill. App. 3d 52; 476 N.E.2d 1154; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 1787; 87 Ill. Dec. 162



March 14, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. John J. Crowley, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) for murder, in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9-1 (1983). Defendant argued that the trial court's refusal to ask certain questions requested by defense counsel during voir dire was reversible error.


OVERVIEW: The victim and others were standing on a street corner when defendant approached them. Defendant made a derogatory remark and an argument ensued. Defendant pulled out a gun, the argument subsided, the others left, and a gunshot was heard. The victim was found lying at the bottom of the stairs mortally wounded. Defendant was identified from witnesses and a warrant was issued. Defendant did not testify. Prior to voir dire, the defense submitted a list of supplemental questions concerning the jurors' attitude toward the failure of defendant to testify in his own behalf, the necessity of a not guilty verdict if the state failed to prove its burden beyond a reasonable doubt, and that defendant was presumed innocent. The trial court rejected these questions because they covered matters of law about which the jury would be later instructed. On appeal, the court found that the matter concerning defendant's failure to testify in his own behalf was not covered in voir dire. Given that an understanding of the concept was vital to the selection of a fair and impartial jury, the court reversed defendant's conviction.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's murder conviction and remanded to the trial court.

Margulis v. Illinois Racing Bd.


No. 83-2571


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


132 Ill. App. 3d 38; 476 N.E.2d 1116; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 1785; 87 Ill. Dec. 124



March 8, 1985, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied April 30, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Arthur L. Dunne, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state racing board (board) sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which reversed the board's disqualification of appellee horse owner's winning horse, which had been based on a post-race urine test that tested positive for the drug procaine.


OVERVIEW: The horse owner owned a winning horse, in whose post-race urine sample an unauthorized foreign substance, the drug procaine, was discovered. For that reason, the state racing board (board) disqualified the horse and canceled and redistributed the winning purse. After the horse owner appealed that decision, the court below reversed the board's decision. The court below held that the applicable state statute, § 37-36(a) of the Illinois Horse Racing Act of 1975, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 8, para. 37-36(a) (1981), and board rules had not been violated because the quantity of the drug procaine in the horse did not have a therapeutic effect on the horse during the race. The judgment of the court below was reversed on appeal and the findings and decision of the board were affirmed because Illinois Horse Racing Board Rule C9.4 prohibited a horse from racing with any foreign substance in its body, regardless of its effect on the horse during the race.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the court below, which reversed the board's disqualification of the horse owner's winning horse following a post-race detection of a prohibited foreign substance, was reversed and the board's findings and decisions were affirmed.

 

1092 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People ex rel. Reeder v. Reeder


No. 5-84-0340


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


131 Ill. App. 3d 841; 476 N.E.2d 50; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 1743; 86 Ill. Dec. 874



March 7, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Madison County; the Hon. Thomas Hildebrand, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant father sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Madison County (Illinois), which denied his motion to dismiss a paternity action brought by plaintiff mother.


OVERVIEW: At the time the mother filed the action, the child was 14 years of age. On appeal, the father argued that the mother's paternity action was barred by the doctrine of laches. Upon review, the court held that the trial court properly denied the father's motion to dismiss. Because there was no limitation period for filing a paternity action as long as the child at issue was a minor, and because, by statute, the father's moral obligation of support was converted into a legal one, the doctrine of laches was inapplicable and unavailable as a defense.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of the father's motion to dismiss, and held that the father was not able to use the doctrine of laches as a defense to the mother's paternity action.

Sheldon v. Edgar


No. 84-1155


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


131 Ill. App. 3d 489; 475 N.E.2d 956; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 1685; 86 Ill. Dec. 577



February 26, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. James C. Murray, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Illinois Secretary of State challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which reversed the Secretary's decision denying plaintiff driver's petition for reinstatement of his restricted driving privileges. The Secretary contended that the trial court erred in finding that the Secretary's refusal to reinstate the driver's privileges was against the manifest weight of the evidence.


OVERVIEW: The driver was convicted for the third time for driving while under the influence of an intoxicating liquor in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 11-501(a) (1977), and his license was revoked pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 6-205(a)(2). The trial court subsequently reversed the Secretary's determination and ordered the driver's privileges reinstated. The Secretary sought review of the trial court's decision. The court on appeal reversed the trial court's judgment based on its determination that the Secretary's denial was reasonable in light of the requested objective evidence that the driver did not provide. The Secretary's decision in denying the driver's petition for reinstatement was not against the manifest weight of the evidence based on the driver's refusal to cooperate with the Secretary's policy providing for the driver's completion of a profession alcohol evaluation and a driver remedial course under Ill. Stone v. Omnicom Cable Television, Inc.


No. 84-102


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


131 Ill. App. 3d 210; 475 N.E.2d 223; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 1647; 86 Ill. Dec. 226



February 21, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County; the Hon. Terrence J. Brady, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, and reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowner appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois), which held that his trespass complaint against defendants, cable company and city (cable company), was not justiciable because there was no actual controversy between the parties. The application of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 24, para. 11-42-11.1 (1983), was at issue.


OVERVIEW: The cable company claimed the right to construct and maintain the cable on the landowner's property independently of the rights granted to it by § 11-42-11.1. The landowner filed a declaratory judgment action against the cable company, seeking injunctive relief for himself and other persons similarly situated to stop the cable company's alleged continuing trespass. The lower court dismissed the count of the landowner's complaint which sought relief for the trespass, holding that there was no actual controversy. The court reversed in part and affirmed in part. The court held that there was an actual controversy because, even though the cable company was not relying upon § 11-42-11.1, that section cast doubts and uncertainty over the landowner's property rights. The fact that the cable company installed its cable upon the landowner's property before the statute was passed did not deprive the landowner of the right to challenge the statute because the landowner alleged a continuing trespass. The lower court's dismissal of the landowner's claim against county regulation of cable companies was dismissed because no county was a party to the action.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's holding that there was no actual controversy between the landowner and the cable company, and the court affirmed the lower court's ruling that the landowner could not challenge any law applying to counties. The matter was remanded to the lower court.

People v. Williamson


No. 83-2547


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


131 Ill. App. 3d 321; 475 N.E.2d 938; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 1656; 86 Ill. Dec. 559



February 20, 1985, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied April 8, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Robert J. Collins, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which found him guilty of voluntary manslaughter and sentenced him to four years' imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, 16 years old at the time of the offense, was charged by indictment with murder and armed violence for the shooting death of a victim. The circuit court found defendant guilty of voluntary manslaughter and sentenced him to four years' imprisonment. On appeal, the court affirmed the circuit court's judgment. The sentencing judge was required to follow certain standards and guidelines in determining whether to sentence a minor as a juvenile or as an adult. Three of the matters which the Juvenile Court Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 37, para. 702-7 (1983), required the circuit court to consider were clearly established by the record. The first factor, whether there was sufficient evidence to return an indictment, was shown by the fact that defendant was actually convicted of voluntary manslaughter. Second, the evidence showed that defendant shot the victim while the victim was running away. Third, defendant was only six months away from the upper age limit of juvenile court jurisdiction. The court was of the opinion that the trial judge did not abuse his discretion in sentencing defendant as an adult. Defendant was also not penalized for exercising his right to remain silent.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment, which found defendant guilty of voluntary manslaughter and sentenced him to four years' imprisonment.

OVERVIEW: The District was a governmental entity organized pursuant to the provisions of the Park District Code, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 105, para. 1 et seq., (1981). The District sought to expand the existing park and acquired a parcel of land directly west of the park. The District's plans to improve the parcel of land were halted by the village which argued that the District lacked authority to develop and operate a park on property outside its boundaries. On appeal, the District brought a motion to take judicial notice of two ordinances enacted after the trial court's order. The village argued that the court could not take judicial notice of the ordinances because the trial court did not do so at the time of the summary judgment motion. The court concluded that: (1) the two ordinances were proper subjects for judicial notice; (2) the parcel of land in question was now within the corporate boundaries of the District; and (3) there was no continuing or recurring controversy which existed between the adverse parties for which a judicial decision would be of any consequence.

Soldano v. Illinois Liquor Control Com.


No. 83-2437


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division


131 Ill. App. 3d 10; 475 N.E.2d 560; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 1618; 86 Ill. Dec. 346



February 4, 1985, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 21, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. James C. Murray, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, and reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff lounge owner appealed the order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which affirmed the order of defendant liquor control commission which affirmed the revocation of his liquor license.


OVERVIEW: The police went to the lounge and subsequently brought a complaint for solicitation of drinks and prostitution. A hearing was held, and the evidence conflicted as to whether a go-go dancer solicited drinks and prostitution. The local liquor commissioner found that the licensee and/or his agent allowed these activities and revoked the lounge owner's license. The lounge owner appealed to the commission, which affirmed the revocation. He then requested judicial review and the trial court affirmed the revocation. He again appealed and argued that the finding that solicitation for prostitution was against the manifest weight of evidence and the order of revocation was based on a violation of an ex post facto law. The court found that the ex post facto prohibition only applied to criminal law, and that a liquor law violation was civil. The court found that the finding of solicitation of prostitution was not against the manifest weight of evidence, and that even if the lounge owner did not have personal knowledge of it, by statute, he was still liable. The court found, however, that the punishment was excessive and affirmed in part and reversed in part the judgment of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part the order of the trial court, which affirmed the finding the solicitation of drinks and prostitution had occurred. The court reversed that part of the order of the trial court that affirmed the revocation of the lounge owner's license as too severe and remanded the matter for further proceedings.

Sanders v. Springfield


No. 4-84-0355


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


130 Ill. App. 3d 490; 474 N.E.2d 438; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 1543; 85 Ill. Dec. 710



January 30, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Sangamon County; the Hon. Jerry S. Rhodes, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff policeman sought review of an order of the Circuit Court of Sangamon County (Illinois), which held that a city ordinance that conditioned employment upon membership and participation in the city police pension fund was valid, and denied the policeman's motion for injunctive relief against defendant city.


OVERVIEW: The city enacted an ordinance that required all policemen within the city to join the police pension fund as a condition of their employment. A policeman commenced suit and sought to invalidate the ordinance. The trial court dismissed the complaint and the policeman sought review. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held: (1) administrative remedies did not need to be exhausted prior to the commencement of the action; (2) the ordinance was not preempted by § 3--150 of the Police Pension Fund Act of the Illinois Municipal Code (Code), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 108 1/2, para. 3--150 (1983) because the local ordinance did not affect any provision of the Code, since the Code was silent as to whether participation was mandatory; (3) the ordinance was not preempted by the Illinois Civil Service in Cities Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 24, para. 10--1--1 et seq., because the Act did not contain a provision limiting the city's exercise of home rule powers; (4) the ordinance did not violate equal protection because the ordinance did not result in the kind of "invidious discrimination" that was prohibited by equal protection guarantees; and (5) the statute was not unconstitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court that held that a city ordinance that conditioned employment upon membership and participation in the city police pension fund was valid and denied the policeman's motion for injunctive relief against the city.

 

1099 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Citizens State Bank v. Johnson


No. 84-35


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


130 Ill. App. 3d 925; 474 N.E.2d 791; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 1597; 85 Ill. Dec. 831



January 23, 1985, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 15, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Ogle County; the Hon. Alan W. Cargerman, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff corporate taxpayer challenged the order of the Circuit Court of Ogle County (Illinois) that awarded summary judgment in favor of defendants, Illinois Department of Revenue and state treasurer, in the taxpayer's injunctive action alleging that defendants improperly disallowed deductions of interest income from Government National Mortgage Association (GNMA) participation certificates under § 203 of the Illinois Income Tax Act.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer brought a complaint for an injunction against defendants for improperly disallowing deductions of interest income earned from GNMA participation certificates. The court affirmed the grant of defendants' motion for summary judgment finding that the department was not estopped by the erroneous listing of exempt property in an information bulletin from making a retroactive application of the provisions of the subsequent bulletin. Estoppel did not apply to the state in the exercise of its taxing power except under extraordinary circumstances, which were not present where the taxpayer relied on the mistakes of the department's agents in determining the taxability of the GNMA certificates that had long been in question. The application of the second bulletin did not violate the taxpayer's due process rights because the only alleged detriment was the taxpayer's increased tax liability and its reliance on the bulletins was misplaced where they were for informational purposes only. Section 203 was not vague and uncertain because it could not have delineated every possible exemption, but required reference to federal regulations in order to determine its scope.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order awarding summary judgment in favor of defendants in the taxpayer's injunctive action alleging that defendants improperly disallowed deductions of interest income from GNMA participation certificates under § 203.

People v. Sturlic


No. 84-185


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


130 Ill. App. 3d 120; 474 N.E.2d 1; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 1504; 85 Ill. Dec. 587



January 17, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County; the Hon. Bruce R. Fawell, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a from judgment from the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), which convicted defendant of residential burglary under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 19-3 (1981), theft exceeding $ 300 under Ill. Rev. Stat., ch. 38, para. 16-1(a)(1) (1981), and possession of burglary tools, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 19-2 (1981).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty of residential burglary, theft exceeding $ 300, possession of burglary tools, but not guilty of conspiracy. Defendant was sentenced to concurrent terms of imprisonment for four years for residential burglary, three years for felony theft, and one year for possession of burglary tools. Defendant appealed his convictions, and the court affirmed the judgment. The court held that the trial court did not err in denying defendant's motion to suppress evidence seized during a search and seizure of his vehicle because probable cause existed for the search and that the subsequent search of defendant's trunk was consensual and also based on probable cause. The court held that the residential burglary statute, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 19-1 (1981), was not unconstitutional and was distinct in its purpose from the burglary statute, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 19-1 (1981). The court disagreed with defendant's argument that his sentence for residential burglary was unconstitutional. The court ruled that the legislature had the power to declare and define conduct constituting a crime, as well as to determine the nature and extent of the punishment for it.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for residential burglary, theft exceeding $ 300, and possession of burglary tools.

People v. Sampson


Nos. 4-84-0300, 4-84-0573 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


130 Ill. App. 3d 438; 473 N.E.2d 1002; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 1540; 85 Ill. Dec. 403



January 17, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Moultrie County; the Hon. Worthy B. Kranz, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in 4 -- 84 -- 0300; judgment reversed in 4 -- 84 -- 0573.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his convictions by the Circuit Court of Moultrie County (Illinois), for driving while under the influence and of driving too fast for conditions, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, paras. 11-501(a), 11-601(a) (1983).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for driving while under the influence and of driving too fast for conditions pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, paras. 11-501(a), 11-601(a) (1983). He was sentenced to six months' probation and ordered to attend an alcohol treatment program at his expense and pay court costs on one charge and sentenced to pay a $ 50 fine, inclusive of court costs on another. Upon appeal, the court affirmed the first conviction and reversed the second. The court found that defendant's stipulated bench trial was not tantamount to a guilty plea and therefore he was not required to have been admonished under Ill. Code Crim. Proc. 402. The court found that defendant failed to met his burden to establish that his equal protection rights had been violated as he had not shown that similarly situated individuals were being treated differently. The court found, though, that the stipulated facts proved that defendant was intoxicated and that he lost control of the car, but that the evidence presented by the stipulated facts was insufficient to find him guilty of driving too fast for conditions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for driving while under the influence. The court reversed defendant's conviction for driving too fast for conditions.

 

1102 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Greater Peoria Sanitary & Sewage Disposal Dist. v. Kellstedt


No. 3-83-0815


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


130 Ill. App. 3d 1002; 474 N.E.2d 1267; 1985 Ill. App. LEXIS 1605; 86 Ill. Dec. 70



January 8, 1985, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied February 8, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Peoria County; the Hon. Charles J. Perrin, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant resident appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court of Peoria County (Illinois), which was entered in favor of plaintiff, a sanitary district, in an action filed by the district to recover unpaid sewage charges from the resident. The trial court awarded damages in favor of the district for unpaid sewage charges, litigation costs, and attorney fees.


OVERVIEW: The resident argued that the application of Peoria, Ill., Ordinance 301, § 206, as to him was unconstitutional. The ordinance set rates based upon water consumption and provided for a credit for water used but not discharged into the district's sewers, such as lawn-watering. Specifically, the resident alleged that his user fees were disproportionately higher than other users who used less water outdoors because 75 percent of his water consumption was not discharged into the sewers. The court reversed the trial court's judgment and held that the ordinance was invalid to the extent that it failed to permit a credit for substantial nonsanitary services. There was substantial evidence to support the resident's contentions that he used as much as 75 percent more water when the unpaid user charges were incurred. Thus, the cause was remanded to determine the proper amount of credit the resident was entitled to for sewage charges. The court also reversed the award of attorney fees as improper under the circumstances. The provisions relied upon by the district for fees applied only to the collection of moneys due the district.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the cause to the trial court with instructions to vacate the award for attorney fees and to determine the proper credit to be allowed the resident.

 

1103 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Parting v. Nalco Chemical Co.


No. 83-1108


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


129 Ill. App. 3d 639; 472 N.E.2d 1220; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 2615; 84 Ill. Dec. 824



December 31, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County; the Hon. Charles R. Norgle, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Counterplaintiff chemical company appealed from the judgment of the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), which held that counterdefendant shareholder could not be held liable by the chemical company in its action to pierce the corporate veil of the corporation whose stock the shareholder owned.


OVERVIEW: The shareholder claimed that a chemical company was liable for injuries which occurred when the shareholder was washing windows. The shareholder was the president of the window washing corporation and had negotiated the corporation's agreement to indemnify the chemical company for any injuries that occurred as a result of the window washing. Thereafter, the window washing company filed for bankruptcy, and the chemical company did not participate in the bankruptcy proceedings. After the bankruptcy filing, the chemical company filed a counterclaim against the shareholder, claiming that he was the alter ego of the corporation. The lower court held that the chemical company was required to file its counterclaim in the bankruptcy court, and the court reversed. The court held that pursuant to 28 U.S.C.S. § 1471(b), (c), the bankruptcy court did not have exclusive jurisdiction over the chemical company's counterclaim. Because the bankruptcy court did not have exclusive jurisdiction over the chemical company's attempt to pierce the corporate veil, the chemical company could pursue its counterclaim in the lower court.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's judgment that the chemical company was prohibited from pursuing its counterclaim against the shareholder, seeking to pierce the corporate veil of the window washing corporation.

 

1104 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Lakin v. Peoria


No. 3-84-0163


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


129 Ill. App. 3d 651; 472 N.E.2d 1233; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 2617; 84 Ill. Dec. 837



December 31, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Peoria County; the Hon. Robert E. Manning, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owner appealed from the judgment of the Circuit Court of Peoria County (Illinois), which held that defendant city's zoning ordinance, Peoria, Ill., Code app. B, § 2-6.2013 (1969), was constitutional and denied the property owner's request for a writ of mandamus.


OVERVIEW: The property owner was granted a variance by the city which permitted her to put a two-family dwelling on a lot that was smaller than was required by the city's zoning ordinances. However, § 2-6.2013 required that before a two-family dwelling could be approved, the adjacent property owners had to consent, and the property owner could not obtain that consent. Additionally, § 2-6.2013 required the consent of the director of community development as to what would be considered a proper location for a two-family dwelling, and the director's decision was not reviewed by any city authority. The lower court held that § 2-6.2013 was constitutional, and the court reversed in part. The court held that to the extent that § 2-6.2013 gave adjacent property owners the right to reject the property owner's application for any reason, § 2-6.2013 was an unconstitutional delegation of legislative power. The court ruled that the authority given to the director to review the property owner's application was not an unconstitutional delegation of power because the city's zoning ordinances set standards governing his decision as to whether the property owner's application would be approved.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's judgment and remanded, holding that the city zoning ordinance was unconstitutional to the extent it required the property owner to obtain consent from adjacent property owners for the development of her property. The court ordered the lower court to issue a writ of mandamus requiring the city to process the property owner's zoning application under that portion of the zoning ordinance that was constitutional.

 

1105 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Costello v. Unarco Industries, Inc.


No. 4-84-0081


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


129 Ill. App. 3d 736; 473 N.E.2d 96; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 2628; 84 Ill. Dec. 880; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P10,686



December 28, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of McLean County; the Hon. Luther H. Dearborn, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff wife, individually and in her role as executor, appealed a decision of the Circuit Court of McLean County (Illinois), which entered judgment in favor of defendant asbestos suppliers, in an action alleging negligence and product liability for personal injuries her husband sustained from his long exposure to asbestos while he was employed at a shipyard, and in which the wife added a claim for wrongful death following the husband's death.


OVERVIEW: The husband and his wife brought an action against the asbestos suppliers, alleging negligence and product liability for personal injuries the husband sustained from his long exposure to asbestos while he was employed at a shipyard. When the husband died from a malignancy caused by exposure to asbestos particles, the wife added a count for wrongful death to the action. The trial court dismissed the compliant as to strict liability and negligence, holding that the strict liability claim was time-barred and the negligence counts were insufficient because they had failed to allege the asbestos suppliers knew or should have known that exposure to the type of asbestos particles they were involved with would have caused a disease like that contracted by the husband. The wife appealed. The court affirmed, holding that the complaint was insufficient in that it failed to specify the disease contracted by the husband and it failed to indicate where in the chain of production the various-named defendants were located and did not apprise them of sufficient facts upon which they could rely in making a defense.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment dismissing portions of a complaint against asbestos suppliers that was brought by the wife of a decedent that alleged negligence and product liability for personal injuries he had sustained from exposure to asbestos.

 

1106 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Belville v. Illinois Racing Bd.


No. 84-1452


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


129 Ill. App. 3d 970; 473 N.E.2d 500; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 2647; 85 Ill. Dec. 132



December 28, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. James C. Murray, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff jockey challenged the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) upholding the decision of defendant Illinois Racing Board to suspend the jockey's racing license for life for possession of a battery on the grounds of a racetrack.


OVERVIEW: While being led to the post by a pony person, racetrack officials stopped the jockey. A battery fell to the ground between the horse and the pony. The officials found that the battery was carried by the pony person, but the Board reversed the decision and found that the jockey had possessed the battery. The jockey appealed his lifetime suspension, and the court affirmed. The court held that while the testimony was disputed, there was ample, consistent circumstantial evidence in the record to support the Board's decision that the jockey was in possession of the battery that was dropped on the racetrack between his horse and the pony. The Board's decision that it was the jockey, not the pony person, who had possession of the battery was supported by the manifest weight of the evidence. The Illinois Horse Racing Act gave the Board broad discretionary power to regulate horse racing, and Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 8, para. 37-16(a) (1983) specifically authorized the Board to suspend or revoke licenses for conduct that was prohibited. The conduct of a jockey found in possession of a battery on a racetrack warranted the most severe sanction available.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision.

 

1107 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Woods v. Brucker Co.


No. 83-2572


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


129 Ill. App. 3d 983; 473 N.E.2d 472; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 2649; 85 Ill. Dec. 104



December 28, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Worthy B. Kranz, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order vacated and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff former employee appealed from an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which entered summary judgment for defendant former employer in the employee's employment discrimination action.


OVERVIEW: The employee had filed with the Illinois Fair Employment Practices Commission (FEPC) an employment discrimination action against the employer after he was discharged while hospitalized. The FEPC did not act upon the charge in any way but advised the employee that he could file a complaint in the circuit court. The employee filed in the circuit court an employment discrimination complaint, which was dismissed on the employer's motion for summary judgment. The court vacated the order dismissing the action. The employee had been prevented from having his claim disposed of by the FEPC because of administrative inaction; and he was denied relief in the trial court. Thus, he was entitled to remandment to the trial court with permission to join the Human Rights Commission and the Department of Human Rights, which had replaced the FEPC under the Illinois Human Rights Act, as necessary party defendants; and an order from the trial court to those entities to accept and process the employee's charge. Under the circumstances of the case, there was no waiver of the employee's constitutional right to a hearing.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the order and remanded the action, with directions that the employee be allowed to join the Department of Human Rights and the Human Rights Commission as parties defendants, and that the trial court order the Department to accept and process plaintiff's charge as set out in the Illinois Human Rights Act.

People v. Pollution Control Bd.


No. 84-126


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


129 Ill. App. 3d 958; 473 N.E.2d 452; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 2646; 85 Ill. Dec. 84



December 27, 1984, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 23, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Petition for review of order of Pollution Control Board.



DISPOSITION: Order vacated, and cause reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner motor racing facility appealed for review of the order of respondent Illinois Pollution Control Board. The Board issued an order wherein it declared that 1981 Ill. Laws 82-654 amounted to an unreasonable limitation of Ill. Const. art. XI, § 2 and was unconstitutional. The facility, pursuant to Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 308, filed application for an interlocutory appeal, raising a certified question of law on appeal.


OVERVIEW: The State initiated an action by filing with the Board a complaint against the facility that alleged that it had violated through certain noise emissions § 24 of the Environmental Protection Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111 1/2, para. 1024 (1979) and Illinois Pollution Control Board Rule 102. During the pendency of this proceeding, the Illinois General Assembly, on two separate occasions, enacted legislation intended to remove from the Board's jurisdiction complaints concerning noise emissions from sporting events, and particularly to prohibit enforcement of the Board's noise regulations applicable to motor sports facilities. The Board found that the second enactment, 1981 Ill. Laws 82-654, was unconstitutional, and the facility filed its interlocutory appeal on the certified legal issue of the constitutionality of the enactment. The court reversed the order and remanded to the Board for further proceedings. 1981 Ill. Laws 82-654 did not limit the ability of an individual to sue in the public interest to remedy environmental harm caused by noise pollution, but rather removed sporting event noise from the Board's regulatory regime. The enactment was neither arbitrary nor unreasonable.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the order of the Board and reversed and remanded the cause for further proceedings.

1110 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Leck v. Michaelson


No. 83-3000


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


129 Ill. App. 3d 593; 472 N.E.2d 1166; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 2610; 84 Ill. Dec. 770



December 18, 1984, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 16, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Joseph Schneider, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, and reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant candidates sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) that removed two defendants from office and directed that a runoff election be held for the resultant vacant offices of trustee, pursuant to the provisions of Village of Lansing, Ill., Ordinance No. 539. Plaintiffs, a candidate and voters, cross-appealed from the denial of their request for attorney fees.


OVERVIEW: In their action, plaintiffs asserted that No. 539 mandated a runoff election because none of the candidates had received 50 percent of the votes cast at an election for the office of trustee. The trial court in part sustained the validity of No. 539, removed two defendants from office, and ordered a runoff election. On appeal, the court held that the provisions of No. 539 that conflicted with the election schedules and procedures set forth in the Illinois Election Code were invalid. However, the provisions regarding the 50 percent majority requirement, were valid because the village as a home rule unit was constitutionally empowered to establish that requirement and to implement a runoff election system to effect it. The court held that the trial court erroneously applied the requirement and thus one defendant was improperly removed from office. A runoff election between defendant who was properly removed from office and plaintiff candidate was warranted. The court also held that plaintiffs were properly denied attorney fees because there was no basis for an award under the Federal Civil Rights Attorneys Fees Award of 1976, 42 U.S.C.S. § 1988.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed that part of the trial court's judgment that directed a runoff election and denied plaintiff's request for attorney fees. The court reversed that part of the judgment that removed two defendants from office, holding that only one defendant should have been removed. The court remanded for further proceedings.

 

1111 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Fireside Chrysler-Plymouth Mazda, Inc. v. Chrysler Corp.


No. 84-527


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


129 Ill. App. 3d 575; 472 N.E.2d 861; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 2608; 84 Ill. Dec. 724



December 13, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Albert Green, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, automobile franchisee, brought an action against defendant, automobile franchiser, alleging violation of the Illinois Motor Vehicle Franchise Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 121 1/2, paras. 751-764 (1981 & 1983 supp.). The franchisee appealed an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) granting summary judgment to the franchiser.


OVERVIEW: After a franchiser granted a new auto dealership franchise, an existing franchisee brought an action claiming that the new franchise violated the Act. In affirming a grant of summary judgment in favor of the franchiser, the court held that it was clear from the plain language of the 1971 direct dealer agreement that the new location was not within the existing franchisee's "area of primary responsibility" as defined by its franchise. The only way the existing franchisee would have standing under the Act to prevent a competing dealership from being established in was if the court were to retroactively apply a 1983 amendment, which defined "relevant market area," so as to broaden the scope of agreed-on sales locality. Because such application would have impaired the vested contractual rights of the parties, the court declined to do so. By its finding that application of the Act as applied to these parties was retroactive and therefore impermissible, the court stated that it did not suggest that application of the Act to conduct arising from pre-existing franchise agreements would always have been improper or retroactive.


OUTCOME: The court held that amendments to the Act were not retroactive and affirmed the grant of summary judgment to the franchiser.

People v. Dickerson


Nos. 3-84-0278, 3-84-0279, 3-84-0280, 3-84-0281 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


129 Ill. App. 3d 59; 471 N.E.2d 1046; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 2545; 84 Ill. Dec. 280



November 30, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Will County; the Hon. Thomas W. Vinson, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded in 3 -- 84 -- 0278, 3 -- 84 -- 0279, 3 -- 84 -- 0280; appeal dismissed in 3 -- 84 -- 0281.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The People of the State of Illinois appealed a decision by the Circuit Court of Will County (Illinois), which dismissed implied consent proceedings after finding that the underlying municipal ordinances were invalid. Defendants were charged in separate incidents with driving under the influence of alcohol (DUI) and related traffic offenses. Each DUI charge was brought under a municipal ordinance.


OVERVIEW: Each defendant refused to take a breathalyzer test at the time of his arrest. The court first granted one defendant's motion to dismiss the State's appeal because the State did not timely file a notice of appeal as required by Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 303 when the final judgment was made according to Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 272. The court reversed the grant of the other defendants' motions to dismiss, however, because the issues of whether the arresting officers had reasonable grounds and whether defendants refused to take the tests were unaffected by the validity of the municipal ordinances. At issue was whether defendants were properly placed under arrest where the ordinances violated were subsequently declared invalid. The court determined that they were because the arresting officers were relying in good faith on an ordinance that was not grossly and flagrantly unconstitutional. Police officers were charged with enforcement of laws unless and until the laws were declared unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the dismissal of the proceedings as to three of the four defendants, and those causes were remanded for further proceedings on those additional issues that defendants chose to raise in their implied consent hearings. As to the fourth defendant, the court affirmed the dismissal of the State's appeal.

Radcliff v. Berwyn


No. 83-1746


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division


129 Ill. App. 3d 70; 472 N.E.2d 98; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 2547; 84 Ill. Dec. 348



November 26, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Joseph M. Wosik, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff resident appealed an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which upheld the constitutionality of defendant city's ordinance, Berwyn City, Ill. Ord., § 6 - 12(1 - b), which regulated the off-street parking of motor vehicles. The resident was arrested for a violation of the ordinance, and he sought injunctive relief. The quasi-criminal proceedings against him were held in abeyance pending the appeal.


OVERVIEW: The resident bought old cars and parked them in his driveway. On the basis that the storage of vehicles on open private land in the city contributed to unhealthful and unsanitary conditions, the ordinance made it unlawful to store an inoperable vehicle not regularly used for transportation on private land. He sought an injunction, alleging that the ordinance was an unconstitutional attempt to regulate the parking of vehicles on private property. At the hearing, photos showed at least seven inoperative vehicles on his driveway. The trial court upheld the constitutionality of the ordinance. On appeal, the resident contended that the ordinance did not provide appropriate standards and guidelines and was an unlawful extension of municipal authority upon the use of private land. The court disagreed and affirmed. The proscribed conduct was sufficiently articulated in the ordinance. The term "open private land" was land not enclosed by a garage or carport. The plain language constituted sufficient notice to potential violators. Also, the city had the power to prohibit the storing of inoperable vehicles on private property, and the ordinance promoted the health and safety of the community.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order.

People ex rel. Hartigan v. Dynasty System Corp.


Nos. 4-84-0337, 4-84-0414 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


128 Ill. App. 3d 874; 471 N.E.2d 236; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 2510; 83 Ill. Dec. 937



November 15, 1984, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied December 12, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Adams County; the Hon. Robert W. Cook, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a Texas corporation, its two shareholders, and a resident distributor, filed interlocutory appeals from orders entered by the Circuit Court of Adams County (Illinois), which granted appellee attorney general's request for a preliminary injunction following the expiration of a temporary restraining order. The circuit court also denied appellants' motion to vacate the injunction. The actions were consolidated on appeal.


OVERVIEW: The Consumer Fraud and Deceptive Business Practices Act (Act) in § 1(g) of the Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 121 1/2, para. 261(g) (1983) defined a pyramid scheme, and in Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 121 1/2, para. 262A(2) (1983) stated it was unlawful for any person, by himself or through others to sell, offer to sell, or attempt to sell the right to participate in a pyramid sales scheme. The state attorney general filed for a temporary restraining order (TRO) against a Texas corporation, its shareholders, and a resident distributor of the corporation, alleging that they were engaged in a pyramid scheme. The TRO was granted, and after a hearing a preliminary injunction was entered. The corporation and individuals' motions to vacate the TRO and the injunction were denied, and they appealed. The court affirmed and held that the Act was not void for vagueness and that it did not improperly intrude on interstate commerce. It was immaterial that a participant was not required to purchase anything in the scheme. The Act authorized the attorney general to seek an injunction on his belief that the Act was violated. He was not required to establish the common law grounds for injunctive relief.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's judgment to issue a preliminary injunction against the Texas corporation, its shareholders, and a resident distributor pursuant to the state attorney general's motion to enjoin them from further pyramid scheme activities in the state.

People v. Lucien


No. 2-84-0030


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


128 Ill. App. 3d 706; 471 N.E.2d 210; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 2482; 83 Ill. Dec. 911



November 9, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County; the Hon. John Bowman, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), which on remand after reversal of most of defendant's convictions for rape, armed robbery, intimidation, aggravated kidnapping, and various forms of armed violence, imposed sentence on two counts of armed violence predicated on intimidation, over defendant's objection.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of rape, armed robbery, intimidation, aggravated kidnapping, and various forms of armed violence. The trial court did not impose sentence on two counts of armed violence predicated on intimidation. An appellate court reversed most of the convictions as either duplicative or illegal double enhancement. However, it treated those armed violence counts as unsentenced and unappealed convictions. On remand, the trial court imposed sentence on those counts over defendant's objection. On appeal, defendant contended that the enhancement of intimidation to a Class X felony under the armed-violence statute, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 33A-2 (1979), constituted a sentence disproportionate to the offense charged, as proscribed by Ill. Const. art. I, §§. 2, 11 (1970). The court affirmed, first finding that the doctrine of res judicata could be relaxed for fundamental fairness. The court held that the intimidation statute as enhanced in the case by the armed-violence statute was constitutional because a rational legislature could have decided that a threat of physical harm with the intent to overcome the will of another was a more serious crime than assault or battery.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment imposing a sentence, on remand, on two counts of armed violence predicated on intimidation.

 

1116 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Waukegan Port Dist. v. Kyritsis


No. 2-83-0998


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


128 Ill. App. 3d 751; 471 N.E.2d 217; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 2491; 83 Ill. Dec. 918



November 9, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County; the Hon. Harry D. Strouse, Jr., Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff port district sought review of an order of the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois), which held that defendant landowners were entitled to interest based on the rate for United States treasury bills on the monies awarded them as just compensation for the port district's taking of their property.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to its eminent domain powers, the port district took a parcel of property owned by the landowners. A jury awarded the landowners just compensation for the taking and the trial court held that the landowners were entitled to interest based on the rate for United States treasury bills on the compensation award. The port district sought review and claimed that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 17, para. 6403 (1981) limited the interest recovery to six-percent. On appeal, the court agreed, reversed and remanded. The court held: (1) § 3 (Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 17, para. 6043 (1981)) of the Interest Act was applicable to condemnation judgments in eminent domain proceedings; (2) the only exception to § 3 was for so-called "quick-take" condemnations, in which Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 47, para. 2.6 (1957) applied; (3) despite the fact that title to the land was somewhat encumbered from the time of filing of the petition to condemn, the landowners were entitled to use the property and any income that may have been earned therefrom; (4) therefore, the "quick-take" provisions did not apply and interest was limited to six-percent under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 17, para. 6403 (1981).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court, held that the landowners were entitled to six-percent interest on the monies awarded them for just compensation for the port district's taking of their property, and remanded the case to the trial court for the computation of the interest.

People v. Coleman


No. 5-82-0329


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


128 Ill. App. 3d 538; 470 N.E.2d 1277; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 2460; 83 Ill. Dec. 857



November 8, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Jackson County; the Hon. Richard Richman, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his conviction from the Circuit Court of Jackson County (Illinois) for armed robbery and his sentence, under the statute relating to habitual criminals, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 33B--1, (1981), to life imprisonment without parole.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with armed robbery after a store clerk identified him as the person who threatened him and then stole money from his car. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court found that the jury's determination of the weight and credibility of the witnesses' testimony was not so improbable as to raise a reasonable doubt of the defendant's guilt. The court reasoned that the jury was justified in accepting the victim's explanation and his identification testimony and, conversely, was not obligated to believe the alibi testimony offered by defendant; the testimony of a single identification witness, if positive and credible, was sufficient to support the conviction. The court then found that the presence of a weapon for the robbery was sufficiently established by circumstantial evidence of something pointed at the victim like a weapon that matched the description of the dangerous weapon found in defendant's car the night of the robbery. This, along with evidence that defendant's car was observed near the scene of the robbery and that the shotgun and towel were found in the car, was sufficient evidence for the jury to infer the presence of the gun.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for armed robbery.

 

1118 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Inn of Lamplighter, Inc. v. Kramer


No. 4-84-0254


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


128 Ill. App. 3d 317; 470 N.E.2d 1205; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 2427; 83 Ill. Dec. 785



October 31, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Sangamon County; the Hon. Richard J. Cadagin, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owners appealed from an order of the Circuit Court of Sangamon County (Illinois) striking their complaint for the issuance of a writ of mandamus against defendant state officials. The writ was sought to compel the state officials to bring an action in eminent domain to compensate the property owners for their alleged loss of access to their property.


OVERVIEW: Part of the property owners resort area was taken for construction of an interstate highway, and the state agreed that access would be provided by a frontage road. When a later reconstruction closed the original access road, the owners of the resort claimed that they had suffered substantial losses. In reversing an order denying the property owner's request for a writ of mandamus to force state officials to compensate them, the court held that to justify issuance of the writ, the mandamus proceeding had to determine the fact of damage. As the pleadings stood that fact was disputed, and it was therefore error to enter judgment on the pleadings. The pleadings raised the question of access. If no damage had occurred, the writ would not issue. However, if damage had occurred, the compensation would be determined in the eminent domain proceeding.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order dismissing the complaint for mandamus and the cause was remanded with directions to reinstate the petition. The trial court was instructed proceed to determine upon such evidence and upon such authority as it might see fit whether there had been a material impairment of access. If it so found, then it was to issue the writ of mandamus compelling the state officials to file an eminent domain suit to determine damages.

 

1119 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Brucato v. Edgar


No. 83-3093


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


128 Ill. App. 3d 260; 470 N.E.2d 615; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 2420; 83 Ill. Dec. 489



October 26, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Harold A. Siegan, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee appealed an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed her complaint against defendants, employer and union, in an action seeking injunctive relief, an accounting, and damages. The employee alleged that collective bargaining agreements entered into between the employer and the union in 1978 and 1981 were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The employee challenged the legality of agreements between the employer, which was a state agency, and the union and alleged that the agreements sanctioned a wage differential between county employees and downstate employees. The court affirmed the order of the trial court, which dismissed the employee's complaint on both jurisdictional and procedural grounds. The court held that the trial court lacked jurisdiction because the employee filed the action against the employer in his official capacity. The court explained that under § 8(b) of the Court of Claims Act, specifically Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 37, para. 439.8(b) (1981), the Court of Claims had exclusive jurisdiction to hear and determine all claims against the state, including claims for equitable relief, that were founded upon any contract entered into with the state. The court also held that the union, a voluntary unincorporated association, lacked capacity to be sued under common law at the time that the complaint was filed. The court found that Ill. Code Civ. P. Ill. Ann. Stat. ch. 110, para. 2-209.1 (Supp. 1984), which permitted unincorporated associations to sue and be sued, was not intended to apply retroactively.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court, which dismissed the employee's complaint against defendants, employer and union, in an action seeking injunctive relief, an accounting, and damages.

Rockford Life Ins. Co. v. Department of Revenue


Nos. 83-626, 83-627 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


128 Ill. App. 3d 302; 470 N.E.2d 596; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 2426; 83 Ill. Dec. 470



October 26, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County; the Hon. John E. Sype, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insurance company sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Winnebago County (Illinois), which affirmed the 1978 assessment of its capital stock by appellee Department of Revenue (department).


OVERVIEW: The insurance company possessed securities (mortgage-backed securities of the Government National Mortgage Association, and obligations issued pursuant to the New Communities Act, the New Community Development Act, and the Merchant Marine Act), which the department exempted from the capital stock assessments in 1974 through 1978. In 1978, the department decided to include these securities in the capital assessment and the company challenged this decision and alleged that these securities were direct obligations of the United States and were immune from state taxation. The lower court affirmed the department's assessment and the court affirmed. The court found that the obligations at issue were not direct obligations issued by the Federal government because the company was the actual issuer. The court determined that the doctrine of equitable estoppel was not applicable because the company did not show that the department acted fraudulently and the company's reliance on the previous assessments was not reasonable. The court held that as the tax did not fall directly on any federal instrumentality, the company was not constitutionally or statutorily immune from state tax.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's decision to affirm the department's assessment of the insurance company's capital stock.
