People v. Polachek


No. 83-1183


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


128 Ill. App. 3d 200; 470 N.E.2d 584; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 2414; 83 Ill. Dec. 458



October 24, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Donald E. Joyce, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which found him unfit to stand trial, dismissed his criminal charges with leave to reinstate, and remanded him to custody of the Illinois Department of Mental Health and Developmental Disabilities (DMHDD) under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 104 -- 25(g)(2) (1983).


OVERVIEW: After defendant stabbed two people, he was indicted for attempted murder and aggravated battery under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, paras. 8-4, 12-4(a), 12-4(b)(1) (1975). He was found unfit to stand trial and held by the DMHDD. Defendant filed a petition for a discharge hearing under the Code of Criminal Procedure, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 104-25 (1983). The court heard testimony about why he was considered to be a danger to other people. The court remanded defendant to the DMHDD under the criminal code rather than under the Mental Health and Developmental Disabilities Code, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 91 1/2, par. 1-100 et seq. (1983). On appeal, the court affirmed. The court found that the continuing jurisdiction of the criminal court did not violate equal protection because there was a rational basis for it because the primary reason for defendant's commitment was the criminal acts he perpetrated. Additionally, the court found the standards for commitment were the same under the criminal and civil codes. The court found that the commitment did not violate due process under Ill. Const. art I, § 2 because the jurisdiction of the criminal court was limited under the statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's commitment of defendant under the criminal code.

Pavlakos v. Illinois Dep't of Labor


No. 82-2635


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


128 Ill. App. 3d 783; 471 N.E.2d 547; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 2495; 84 Ill. Dec. 18



October 24, 1984, Filed

DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs sought review of an order from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which affirmed the decision of defendant Department of Labor finding plaintiffs liable, pursuant to § 2600 of the Illinois Unemployment Insurance Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 48, para. 750 (1979), for unpaid contributions, interest, and penalties incurred by a certain medical personnel agency.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs agreed to purchase all the assets of a medical personnel agency. As consideration for the sale, plaintiffs were to pay certain liens which had been filed against the agency. The Department of Labor mailed to plaintiffs a notice of determination and assessment against purchaser or transferee and demand for payment informing plaintiffs that the agency was indebted to the department for unpaid contributions, interest, and penalties; that the agency had failed to pay the amount of the contributions, interest, and penalties; and that plaintiffs, as purchasers of all the assets of the agency, were being assessed the sums due. The Director of Labor found plaintiffs liable and the trial court affirmed. Plaintiffs appealed and the court affirmed the order of the trial court. The court held that § 2600 of the Illinois Unemployment Insurance Act was constitutional because the classification that it created bore a reasonable relationship to a legitimate legislative purpose and that it did not deny plaintiffs equal protection of the laws. The court held that the department was under no duty to record a lien or to respond to the notice of bulk sale.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court that affirmed the decision of the department that found plaintiffs liable for unpaid contributions, interest, and penalties incurred by a certain medical personnel agency.

 

1123 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Chicago v. Strauss


No. 83-2168


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


128 Ill. App. 3d 193; 470 N.E.2d 563; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 2412; 83 Ill. Dec. 437



October 18, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. William Wood, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his conviction by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) for attempting to sell a ticket to a baseball game in front of the baseball park, in violation of Chicago, Ill., Mun. Code ch. 36, § 36-48 (1982). Defendant contended that his conviction had to be reversed because his attempt to sell the ticket for not more than its face value did not constitute "speculating" as used in § 36-48.


OVERVIEW: The city maintained that defendant violated the ordinance by attempting to sell a ticket in his possession in front of the baseball park, regardless of price. The court held that: (1) Chicago, Ill., Mun. Code ch. 36, § 36-48 (1982) prohibited defendant from selling or offering to sell a ticket in his possession in front of a baseball park in an attempt at speculating in that ticket; (2) the same rules applied in construing municipal ordinances that governed the construction of statutes; (3) where the language was susceptible of differing interpretations, it was necessary to consider the purpose and to choose the interpretation leading to a logical result; (4) penal statutes were to be strictly construed in favor of an accused, with any ambiguity resolved in favor of defendant; (5) the proper interpretation to be placed on § 36-48 was that the city council intended that persons intending to sell or offering to sell tickets in their possession at, or near any amusement park, were prohibited from selling those tickets at a price greater than their face value; and (6) since defendant offered his ticket for sale at or below face value, he did not violate § 36-48.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction of speculating.

 

1124 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Bradley


No. 4-84-0019


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


128 Ill. App. 3d 372; 470 N.E.2d 1121; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 2438; 83 Ill. Dec. 701



October 16, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Livingston County; the Hon. William T. Caisley, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate challenged a decision from the Circuit Court of Livingston County (Illinois), which denied the inmate's petition for post-conviction relief under the Post Conviction Hearing Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 122--1 et seq. (1983).


OVERVIEW: The inmate was convicted of indecent liberties with a child. His direct appeals were denied, and he filed a petition for post-conviction relief. The trial court denied his petition, and the inmate sought review. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's decision. The inmate waived the alleged errors by failing to object at trial or raise them on direct appeal. The court found that the inmate's petition did not present a substantial showing of a denial of constitutional rights. The court held that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 11--4(a)(3) (1983) was not unconstitutionally vague. Moreover, the use of the word "or" in the information did not render the charge uncertain. The inmate's conviction did not constitute double jeopardy merely because the prosecution mentioned another offense date in its opening statement. The inmate's comment to a caseworker was admissible at trial because no privilege existed. Evidence of other crimes were admissible because it showed the familiar relation of the parties and it corroborated the victim's testimony. Finally, the court determined that the inmate failed to show that his trial or appellate counsel were ineffective.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of the inmate's petition for post-conviction relief.

 

1125 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Moorhead


No. 2-83-1013


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


128 Ill. App. 3d 137; 470 N.E.2d 531; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 2404; 83 Ill. Dec. 405



October 15, 1984, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied November 20, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County; the Hon. Lawrence D. Inglis, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois) that convicted her upon a jury verdict of solicitation to commit murder in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 8--1(a) (1983). Defendant was sentenced to a 25-year term of imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of solicitation to commit murder after she requested an undercover officer to kill her husband. Defendant was sentenced to 25 years in prison. She appealed from her conviction and sentence, and the court affirmed. Defendant contended that the statute setting forth the penalty for solicitation to commit murder, found at Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 8--1(b) (1983), was an unconstitutional deprivation of due process because the penalty was more severe than the maximum penalty for conspiracy to commit murder, which defendant argued was a more severe offense. Solicitation was not a lesser-included offense of conspiracy. Rather, the two offenses were wholly distinct. In determining whether the penalty set for solicitation was unconstitutional, the court examined whether the penalty statute was reasonably designed to remedy the evils which the legislature determine were a threat to the public health, safety, and general welfare. The court concluded that conspiracy did not present a more serious threat to the public than solicitation, and therefore, the relative penalties were proper.


OUTCOME: The judgment convicting defendant upon a jury verdict of solicitation to commit murder and sentencing her to 25 years in prison was affirmed.

No. 83-2465


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


128 Ill. App. 3d 70; 470 N.E.2d 54; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 2393; 83 Ill. Dec. 299



October 11, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Arthur L. Dunne, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff job applicant sought review of an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed his complaint against defendant employer for employment discrimination.


OVERVIEW: The applicant sought a position with the employer, but was not hired. The applicant filed a complaint with the fair employment practices commission (FEPC), charging racial discrimination. The FEPC notified the applicant that he could sue the employer. An administrative law judge (ALJ) recommended dismissal of the charge and the state human rights commission affirmed the ALJ and denied the applicant's motion for reconsideration. The trial court dismissed the portion of the applicant's complaint that sought administrative review of the commission's decision and then held that the applicant's failure to seek the administrative review of the commission's decision barred the action. The court reversed. The court held that the applicant timely filed a charge with the FEPC and that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 68, para. 9-102(b), which would have preserved the chare was declared unconstitutional. The applicant had a protected property interest in his discrimination claim and the FEPC could not deprive him of that right. A U.S. Supreme Court decision governing the case could be applied retroactively.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court, which dismissed the applicant's action, seeking review of the commission's denial of his petition for reconsideration of the dismissal of his complaint.

Great Plains Resources, Inc. v. Benton


No. 5-83-0858


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


127 Ill. App. 3d 971; 469 N.E.2d 341; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 2368; 82 Ill. Dec. 807; 83 Oil & Gas Rep. 495



September 19, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Franklin County; the Hon. Lehman D. Krause, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review of a declaratory judgment from the Circuit Court of Franklin County (Illinois), which found a city ordinance regulating the drilling of oil and gas wells violative of the Constitutions of the United States of America and the State of Illinois, in appellees' action challenging the ordinance.


OVERVIEW: The city ordinance imposed spacing requirements for the drilling of oil and gas wells. The trial court found no valid reason for such a rule. The trial court also found that the deposit of $ 3,000 plus a 1/32 overriding interest bore no relation to the city's administrative costs and constituted a confiscation of property in violation of the due process and equal protection clauses of the federal and state constitutions. The trial court concluded that the ordinance was unconstitutional. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court found that the trial court's conclusion that the spacing requirements of the ordinance was arbitrary could reasonably have been based on the evidence presented at trial that the ordinance required the drilling of more wells than needed. Further, the court held that the city was prohibited from raising revenue by the exercise of its police power. The court concluded that the finding of the trial court, that the license and royalty fees were a veiled attempt to exact by means of the city's police power revenue it could not exact by means of a tax, was neither contrary to law nor against the manifest weight of the evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment that found the city drilling ordinance was unconstitutional.

People v. Smith


No. 82-1773


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


127 Ill. App. 3d 622; 469 N.E.2d 634; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 2324; 83 Ill. Dec. 27



September 18, 1984, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied October 17, 1984.
Habeas corpus proceeding at Smith v. Fairman, 862 F.2d 630, 1988 U.S. App. LEXIS 16562 (7th Cir. Ill., 1988)
Post-conviction relief denied at People v. Smith, 307 Ill. App. 3d 1075, 760 N.E.2d 1063, 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 3786, 260 Ill. Dec. 290 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 1999)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Remanded by People v. Smith, 337 Ill. App. 3d 1160, 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 2194 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2003)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at People v. Smith, 2011 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1670 (2011)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Earl Strayhorn, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, and reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), following a jury trial, in which he was sentenced to concurrent to serve concurrent terms of imprisonment for murder, attempted murder, burglary, aggravated battery, home invasion, and two counts of armed violence predicated on murder and attempted murder, respectively.


OVERVIEW: Defendant broke into his elderly victim's two-story residence and fatally stabbed her. Defendant was convicted of murder, attempted murder, burglary, aggravated battery, home invasion, and armed violence. The court reversed the case in part. The court held that the trial court erred when it excluded the testimony of defendant's mother. A prior inconsistent statement submitted for the purpose of impeaching a declarant was not hearsay because it was not submitted to prove the truth of the matter asserted. In addition, the sentencing alternatives available at the time of sentencing differed from those available at the time of the commission of the offense and, therefore, defendant was entitled to be informed that the two sentencing schemes existed and to choose between the two. Defendant was not, however, informed of the existence of the sentencing alternatives and was not, therefore, afforded his statutory right to select one of the two applicable sentencing schemes. Therefore, the court vacated defendant's sentence. Finally, the court vacated defendant's armed violence conviction because it was based on the same act as the predicate felony.


OUTCOME: The court vacated defendant's armed violence conviction and the extended term sentence for murder. The court otherwise affirmed defendant's convictions and sentences for attempted murder, burglary, aggravated battery, and home invasion.

Kline v. Illinois Racing Bd.


No. 83-1870


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


127 Ill. App. 3d 702; 469 N.E.2d 667; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 2335; 83 Ill. Dec. 60



September 18, 1984, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied October 16, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. James C. Murray, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff horse trainer appealed a decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which upheld the determination of defendant, the Illinois Racing Board, to suspend the trainer's occupation license for two concurrent 90-day periods and to order a forfeiture and redistribution of the purse money for two races won by one of the trainer's horses.


OVERVIEW: Tests by the Board on the urine of one of the trainer's horses after each of two races which the horse won disclosed the presence of scopolamine in the horse. The initial steward's ruling found that the trainer had violated Ill. Racing Bd. R. C9.4, which banned foreign substances in horses, and Ill. Racing Bd. R. C9.20, which required trainers to guard their horses prior to a race. The trainer asserted that the substance had been introduced into the horse by being naturally present in small amounts in the hay it was fed. The trainer admitted to leaving the horse unguarded for 35 to 40 minutes before each of the two races. The court held that: (1) the rule banning foreign substances was a valid exercise of the Board's authority because the rule bore a rational and reasonable relationship to the state's interest in a fair and honest horse racing industry; (2) there was sufficient evidence upon which the Board could have found that the trainer had violated the rule banning foreign substances; and (3) the trainer's stipulation that he left the horse unguarded before each of the two races was sufficient to establish his violation of the guarding rule.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order.

Heckmann v. Cemeteries Asso. of Greater Chicago


No. 84-1480


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division


127 Ill. App. 3d 451; 468 N.E.2d 1354; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 2300; 82 Ill. Dec. 574; 119 L.R.R.M. 3131; 37 Fair Empl. Prac. Cas. (BNA) 156; 106 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P55,711; 40 Empl. Prac. Dec. (CCH) P36; 40 Empl. Prac. Dec. (CCH) P36,157



September 17, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Arthur L. Dunne, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff union representatives (representatives) appealed an order from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted a motion for summary judgment filed by defendants, cemeteries association and its director, in the representatives' declaratory judgment action challenging the constitutionality of an Act to permit certain burials on Sundays and legal holidays (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 21, para. 101 et seq. (1983).


OVERVIEW: The representatives filed the declaratory judgment action challenging the constitutionality and validity of the Act. The circuit court granted defendants' motion for summary judgment. On appeal, the court affirmed the circuit court's order, finding that the Act did not violate the establishment clause because the Act had a valid secular purpose. The court found further that the statute did not foster excessive government entanglement with religion because the government did not have to involve itself in any administration or planning, and religion was not politicized. The court could not say that the classification in the statute was arbitrary or that the legislature acted unreasonably in singling out the workers' association agreements. The court determined that the legislation in issue did not offend the state and federal constitutions' contract clauses. The court concluded that the provisions of the Act were narrowly drawn to permit the free exercise of religious rights while allowing labor to restrict their working schedules accordingly. It was, therefore, a reasonable exercise of legislative authority in an area of legitimate legislative concern.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's order, which granted defendants' motion for summary judgment in the representatives' declaratory judgment action challenging the constitutionality of the Act.

Escalona v. Board of Trustees


No. 84-0534


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


127 Ill. App. 3d 357; 469 N.E.2d 297; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 2289; 82 Ill. Dec. 763



September 14, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Arthur L. Dunne, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) affirmed a decision of defendant retirement system, which terminated plaintiff employee's disability compensation. The employee appealed the order.


OVERVIEW: After the retirement system notified the employee that her disability benefits would be terminated as of a certain date, the employee submitted reports from her physicians stating that she was disabled. After a physician for the retirement system who had examined the employee stated that she was capable of returning to work, the retirement system notified the employee that her benefits would be terminated. The retirement system denied several appeals by the employee, and the circuit court affirmed the retirement system's decision. Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 108 1/2, para. 14-124(2) (1983) provided an adequate standard on which the retirement system could rely to determine whether the employee was disabled. The requirements of due process were met because nothing in the record indicated that the employee could not understand from the language of the statute that she must have a condition that rendered her unable to perform her duties in order to continue to be eligible for disability benefits.


OUTCOME: The decision of the retirement board, which terminated the employee's disability compensation, was affirmed.

 

1132 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Weyerhaeuser Co. v. Department of Revenue


No. 81-2936


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


127 Ill. App. 3d 323; 469 N.E.2d 267; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 2285; 82 Ill. Dec. 733



September 13, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Earl Arkiss, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer, a corporation, requested review after defendant Department of Revenue of the State of Illinois determined it owed additional income taxes following the disallowance of a claimed valuation limitation in computing taxable gain on property. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) upheld the determination, and the taxpayer appealed. The taxpayer claimed its taxable year ended before the deduction was eliminated.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to federal income tax law, the taxpayer elected to use a taxable year which varied from 52 to 53 weeks and ended on the last Sunday in December. The taxable year at issue ended before the last day in December. The court explained that the taxable year was transformed to one beginning on the first day of the next calendar year. The court said that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, paras. 2-203(a)(2)(F) and 2-203(c)(2)(F) (1973) eliminated the valuation limitation in computing taxable gain on property for corporations. The court said that the amendment applied to the taxable year at issue. The court noted that 26 U.S.C.S. § 441(f)(2)(A)(1)(i) provided that, with the accounting method chosen by the taxpayer, the effective date for statutory changes expressed in terms of taxable years beginning with a specified date would be the first day of the calendar month beginning nearest to the first day of the taxable year. The court explained that accepting the benefits meant accepting the limitations and ruled that the deduction was properly invalidated. Citing a ruling from the Illinois Supreme Court, the court rejected the taxpayer's claims that the amendment was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1133 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Kaiser v. Dixon


No. 2-83-0671


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


127 Ill. App. 3d 251; 468 N.E.2d 822; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 2279; 82 Ill. Dec. 275; 120 L.R.R.M. 2619



September 7, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County; the Hon. John S. Teschner, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, an employee, filed an action against appellees, the police chief and the city, seeking a writ of mandamus to order them to hold a hearing, to vacate the employee's termination, and to reinstate her as a member of the city police department. A hearing officer denied the request for reinstatement, back pay, and attorney fees. The Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois) confirmed the hearing officer's decision. The employee appealed.


OVERVIEW: The employee was a radio dispatcher in the police department. The chief expressed an intent to discharge the employee for violations of the staff manual policies to the president, who concurred, but the director decided to suspend her. Later, while the director was away, the employee was discharged by the president, who was then the acting director, and orally notified thereof. The director denied her request for a hearing, but later held a hearing pursuant to a trial court order. The hearing officer denied the employee's request for reinstatement and found the discharge was for cause. The employee argued the discharge was void. The court held (1) the chief lacked authority under Roselle, Ill., Municipal Code § 16-7, to discharge her because she was an unsworn employee; (2) the director had authority to discharge such employee; (3) the employee was properly discharged with the concurrence of the president, who was then the acting director of services and personnel; (4) the department regulations granting the chief power to discharge the employee was invalid; and (5) due process was not violated because the employee received a hearing, which upheld the discharge as for cause.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment.

 

1134 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Lang


Nos. 82-429, 82-2302, 83-2218, 84-1238, 84-1341 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


127 Ill. App. 3d 313; 468 N.E.2d 1303; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 2284; 82 Ill. Dec. 523



September 4, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Joseph Schneider, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent mental patient sought review of an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which denied his petition for a readjudication of his fitness to stand trial on a charge of murder. The trial court had found for petitioner state three years before and involuntarily civilly committed the patient to a mental health facility. In the intervening years, the trial court had made six redeterminations of the patient's commitment status.


OVERVIEW: It had been found that the visually impaired, deaf-mute patient was unfit to stand trial on the murder charge. He was civilly committed and the charge was dismissed with leave to reinstate. Over the next three years, pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 91 1/2, § 3-813 (1978), six redeterminations of his commitment status were made but he was not given a new hearing on his fitness to stand trial. On appeal, the court reversed the order and remanded for a fitness hearing. The court noted that there was evidence that the patient had shown some improvement in his ability to communicate by sign language and might now be better able to assist in his own defense. The court stated that the results of civil commitment hearings, no matter how many in number, are not indicative of a person's mental capacity to stand trial on criminal charges, because a defendant may have a physical or mental problem, or a combination of both, yet may actually meet the fitness standards under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 104-10 (1983). The court noted that three years had gone by since a finding had been made that no substantial probability existed that the patient would attain fitness within one year.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order in favor of the state, which had denied the patient's petition for a readjudication of his fitness to stand trial on a murder charge, and remanded for a formal hearing into his fitness to stand trial.

 

1135 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Chicago v. State & Municipal Teamsters


No. 84-1433


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


127 Ill. App. 3d 328; 468 N.E.2d 1268; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 2286; 82 Ill. Dec. 488



August 31, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. James C. Murray, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant unions, challenged an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed the unions' complaint, denied their amended petition for preliminary injunction, and granted respondent city's complaint for declaratory relief, certifying the election results.


OVERVIEW: The city notified the unions that it intended to conduct union representation elections. The unions filed a complaint, seeking a declaration as to the rights of the parties and the legality of the city's actions in establishing and conducting the presentation elections. Various motions were filed during the elections. The trial court granted the city's complaint for declaratory relief, certifying the election results, held that the commissioner's rule-making procedure was lawful, dismissed the unions' complaint, and denied the unions' amended petition for preliminary injunction. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court ruled that the Public Labor Relations Act (Act), Ill. Ann. Stat. ch. 48, para. 1601 et. seq., had no preemptive effect, therefore the city was not precluded from holding the elections. The court held that the commissioner was authorized under the grant of authority to establish rules and procedures for the elections, thus there was no delegation problem. Finally, the court held that the rule-making procedure was not deficient, because the commissioner complied with the provisions of Chicago, Ill., Municipal Code ch. 25.1, para. 5 (1982).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the unions' complaint and denial of their petition for preliminary injunction. The court upheld the granting of declaratory relief in favor of the city, certifying the election results.

Chicago Park Dist. v. Chicago


No. 84-450


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


127 Ill. App. 3d 215; 468 N.E.2d 1261; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 2273; 82 Ill. Dec. 481



August 29, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Paul F. Elward, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff Chicago Park District appealed from an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which denied the Chicago Park District's motion for a temporary restraining order and preliminary injunction to prevent defendant city from collecting a mooring tax. The action filed by the Chicago Park District sought a declaratory judgment that the city's boat-mooring tax was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The Chicago Park District claimed that the city's imposition of a 50 percent boat-mooring tax on all boats moored in any body of water within the city's corporate limits was unconstitutional. The trial court ruled that the Chicago Park Department did not have standing to sue and did not demonstrate irreparable harm or a likelihood of success on the merits of the motion for a temporary restraining order and preliminary injunction. The court held that the Chicago Park District had standing to bring the case because the impact of the tax on mooring benefit holders directly injured the Chicago Park District and its revenue planning, but the court affirmed the denial of the preliminary injunction. The Chicago Park District failed to show probable success on the merits because the state's extensive regulation of recreational harbors did not preclude the city from imposing a tax; Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 19, para. 73 (1983) and Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 105, para. 333.23n(g) (1983) did not reflect a statewide constitutional interest in recreational harbors overriding the city's home rule power to tax; and the mooring tax did not usurp authority or regulate access to recreational harbors.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which denied the Chicago Park District's motion for a temporary restraining order and preliminary injunction to prevent the city from collecting a boat-mooring tax in the declaratory judgment action against the city.

 

1137 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Richman v. Chicago Bears Football Club, Inc.


No. 83-2188


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


127 Ill. App. 3d 75; 468 N.E.2d 487; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 2250; 82 Ill. Dec. 225



August 28, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. John F. Hechinger, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff season ticket holders appealed an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted defendant football team's summary judgment motion and which dismissed the amended complaint with prejudice on the grounds that there was no legal basis for awarding prejudgment interest and that the football team had not wrongfully withheld the season ticket holders' refunds and, thus, had not been unjustly enriched.


OVERVIEW: The football team went on strike and some of the games were postponed and later cancelled. The season ticket holders sought to recover prejudgment interest and interest earned by the football team from the time of the cancellation of four home games to the time the purchase price of their tickets was refunded to them. The trial court granted summary judgment to the football team. In affirming, the court held that the football team was not under any contractual obligation to present games on dates certain. The contractual relationship between nongovernmental parties lacked unique factual circumstances. To award interest not authorized by statute or by agreement, an element of bad conduct was required, and there was no evidence of bad conduct by the football team. The uncontested affidavit of the football team's treasurer showed that the four strike-delayed home games were not officially cancelled until the day of the settlement of the players' strike and that the football team offered full refunds 10 days later. Thus, the football team was not guilty of wrongfully withholding the season ticket holders' funds and there was no basis for an award of prejudgment interest.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order, which granted the football team's summary judgment motion and dismissed the season ticket holders' amended complaint with prejudice.

People v. Wisslead


No. 3-83-0744


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


126 Ill. App. 3d 1078; 468 N.E.2d 470; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 2710; 82 Ill. Dec. 208



August 24, 1984, Filed

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Circuit Court of McDonough County (Illinois), which convicted him of unlawful restraint in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 10-3 (1981), aggravated assault in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 12-2 (1981), and simple assault in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 12-1 (1981).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged by a two-count information alleging armed violence predicated on unlawful restraint and unlawful restraint. The trial court dismissed the armed violence count, and defendant was tried on the remaining unlawful restraint count. Defendant was convicted of aggravated assault, simple assault, and unlawful restraint. Defendant filed a motion in arrest of judgment and challenged the sufficiency of the information. The motion was denied, and defendant sought review of his conviction. The State conceded that simple assault was a lesser-included offense of aggravated assault and that conviction was vacated. Defendant argued that the information was insufficient to sustain his conviction for aggravated assault and unlawful restraint because if failed to set forth the nature and elements of the offenses charged. The court found that the information failed to set forth the nature of defendant's alleged unlawful restraint and that his motion in arrest of judgment should have been granted. The court also found that aggravated assault was not a lesser-included offense of unlawful restraint.

Mt. Prospect State Bank v. Kirkland

Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District

DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff land trustee sought review of an order from the Circuit Court of De Kalb County (Illinois), which granted defendant village's motion to dismiss the land trustee's action seeking an order of mandamus directing the village to provide garbage collection to the land trustee's mobile home park and damages.


OVERVIEW: The land trustee owned a parcel of land on which it established a mobile home park that housed between 70 and 77 mobile homes. The village contracted with a refuse collection company for garbage collection service for the village's residences. The contract specifically excluded the land trustee's mobile home park, which was the only mobile home park in the village. The land trustee argued that its exclusion was discriminatory and violated the land trustee's right to equal protection. The land trustee also sought punitive damages under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 and compensatory damages for the years in which garbage service was denied but the land trustee paid taxes to the village. The trial court granted the village's motion to dismiss and the land trustee sought review. The court found that there was no right to garbage collection and that the land trustee was not among the recognized suspect classes. The court also found that there was a rational basis for the exclusion of the land trustee and that the action was therefore properly dismissed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's dismissal of the land trustee's action.

City of Chicago v. John Hancock Mut. Life Ins. Co.


No. 83-2237


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


127 Ill. App. 3d 140; 468 N.E.2d 428; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 2261; 82 Ill. Dec. 166



August 17, 1984, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Supplemental Opinion Filed on Denial of Rehearing September 28, 1984, Reported at 127 Ill. App. 3d 140 at 148.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Simon S. Porter, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner resident appealed from an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), denying her petition to intervene in this action for building code violations brought by plaintiff city against defendants, owners and homeowners association (association). The trial court found that the resident's interests would be adequately represented by the city and the association.


OVERVIEW: The city alleged that the owners and the homeowners association failed to provide sufficient ventilation as required by the municipal code and sought fines, injunctive relief, the appointment of a receiver and an order of demolition. The resident alleged that she was a condominium owner in the building and that her health, safety, and property interests would be affected by the outcome of the case. The resident maintained that the city would not represent her particular interests and had failed to pursue discovery. She argued that the association could not represent her because it denied the existence of a violation. In reversing the trial court, the appellate court held that the statutory requirements of timeliness and sufficiency of interest were met pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, paras. 2- 408(a)(2), 2- 408(b)(2). In addition, the court held that differences in scope and intensity between the city's public health interest and the resident's private health interest, and between the association's property interest and resident's property interest, shed significant doubt on the adequacy of representation.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court that denied the resident's petition to intervene in the city's action against the owner for building code violations.

People v. Raseaitis


No. 82-262


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which found that the state proved that defendant committed murder and ordered him to undergo a treatment period of five years with the Department of Mental Health and Developmental Disabilities.


OVERVIEW: Defendant confessed to committing murder. He was found unfit to stand trial and was given a discharge hearing. The lower court found that defendant was guilty and imposed a maximum treatment period of five years with the department. The court affirmed and held that the state met its burden of proof under Ill. Stat. ch. 38, para. 104-25 (1983) did not violate equal protection, and it provided a reasonable means of balancing and protecting society's interests and the interests of defendants found unfit for trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order finding that the state proved that defendant committed murder and ordering him to undergo a treatment period of five years with the department.

People v. Sanchez


No. 83-400


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


126 Ill. App. 3d 746; 467 N.E.2d 1085; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 2199; 82 Ill. Dec. 12



August 7, 1984, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied September 5, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Samuel S. Berger, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent acquittee sought review of a decision from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which determined that the acquittee, who had been found not guilty of homicide by reason of insanity, was in need of mental health treatment on an inpatient basis as petitioner state contended.


OVERVIEW: The acquittee was found not guilty of homicide by reason of insanity. The trial court determined that the acquittee was in need of mental health treatment on an inpatient basis as the state contended. On appeal, the acquittee contended that the standard for involuntary admission to mental health treatment set forth in § 5-2-4(a)(2)(B) of the Unified Code of Corrections, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-2-4(a)(1)(B), was unconstitutionally vague and therefore violative of due process. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The court held that: (1) contrary to the acquittee's contention, the statute did not circuitously define "in need of mental health services on an inpatient basis" as a need for inpatient care; (2) the requirement of the statute that an acquittee would benefit from inpatient care provided a sufficient foundation for commitment; (3) the requirement that an acquittee would benefit from inpatient care and the requirement that there be a finding that the acquittee was reasonably expected to inflict physical harm on himself or another were meaningful criteria that precluded arbitrary commitment decisions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which determined that the acquittee was in need of mental health treatment on an inpatient basis.

People v. Decker


No. 4-83-0729


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


126 Ill. App. 3d 428; 467 N.E.2d 366; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 2148; 81 Ill. Dec. 666



August 2, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Vermilion County; the Hon. Ralph S. Pearman, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged her convictions for two counts each of armed violence and aggravated battery and her sentence of 18 years imprisonment by the Circuit Court of Vermilion County (Illinois).


OVERVIEW: When officers attempted to arrest her husband, defendant shot and wounded an officer. She was convicted of two counts each of armed violence and aggravated battery and sentenced to 18 years imprisonment The court affirmed in part and vacated. The court noted that defendant was sentenced on only one conviction for armed violence and, due to merger and redundancy, the court vacated the three extra convictions. Because the use of a weapon was not an element of the predicate felony of aggravated battery causing great bodily harm, the court held that the offence could serve as the predicate felony for armed violence even though the harm was caused by the weapon. The court held that the Class X penalty imposed for defendant's conviction was not unconstitutional when aggravated battery causing great bodily harm, when committed with a weapon, was more serious than voluntary manslaughter committed with a weapon. No error was found in the exclusion of testimony concerning domestic violence that occurred years before because it was too remote to be relevant. Lastly, the court held that the sentence was not an abuse of discretion given the nature of the offence and defendant's history.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence for one count of armed violence and vacated the remaining convictions for one count of armed violence and two counts of aggravated battery.

Sale v. Allstate Ins. Co.


Nos. 82-655, 82-720, 82-2326 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


126 Ill. App. 3d 905; 467 N.E.2d 1023; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 2220; 81 Ill. Dec. 901



August 2, 1984, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied August 30, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Warren D. Wolfson, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, and reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, the conservator of the estate of an insured whose benefits had been discontinued, appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed her claims for punitive damages, actual fraud, and constructive fraud for failure to state a cause of action; entered a jury verdict in favor of defendant insurer on the count of intentional infliction of mental distress; and awarded attorney fees to the conservator.


OVERVIEW: The court held that the trial court did not err in refusing to instruct the jury regarding the prior finding of wilful refusal to pay under the insurance policy, where it was the jury's duty to determine whether the insurer's intent met the standards for intentional infliction of emotional distress. The conservator's claim for punitive damages for the wilful refusal to pay benefits was properly dismissed where the award of treble damages constituted punishment for the refusal to pay. The conservator did not show that Illinois Insurance Code § 155, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 73, para. 767 (1977) (remedy for wrongful conduct by insurer) was unconstitutional. There was no reversible error in the dismissal of the actual fraud and constructive fraud counts or in the tendering or refusing of jury instructions on actual causation and intentional infliction of emotional distress. The conservator's motion for a new trial predicated upon the affidavit of a juror was properly denied. The trial court should have considered the amount of time which was reasonably expended in the prosecution of the conservator's claim and the appropriate amount of attorney fees to be assessed against the insurer.


OUTCOME: The dismissal of the claims for punitive damages, actual fraud, constructive fraud, and intentional infliction of mental distress was affirmed. The award of attorney fees was reversed and the case was remanded, with directions.

People v. Brewer


No. 83-0659


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division


127 Ill. App. 3d 306; 468 N.E.2d 1242; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 2283; 82 Ill. Dec. 462



July 30, 1984, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied October 3, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Christy S. Berkos, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of indecent liberties with a child in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, paras. 11 -- 4(a)(1), (a)(2) (1981), and sentenced him to an extended term of 25 years' imprisonment. He claimed that he was not proven guilty beyond a reasonable doubt and that the trial court erred in denying his motion to order a psychiatric examination of the child.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with indecent liberties with a child. The complaining witness, defendant's step-daughter, was seven years old at the time of the incident and nine years old at the time of the trial. She testified that defendant attacked her when she got home from school and described acts of oral copulation and fondling performed against her. A teacher and an emergency room doctor testified as to what the girl told them, and described the same attack. Defendant was acquitted of a count alleging intercourse and found guilty of a count alleging oral copulation. On appeal, the court agreed with the State that a seven-year-old child would not be able to accurately and consistently describe the sexual acts at issue unless the acts had been performed against her, and that any discrepancies in her testimony were minor and did not detract from the reasonableness of her testimony as a whole. The court found further defendant failed to present adequate reasons for an order for a psychiatric examination of the victim, holding that a psychiatric examination was not warranted just because the complaining witness did poorly in school or became confused under cross-examination.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

People v. Frazier


No. 83-1155


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


127 Ill. App. 3d 151; 469 N.E.2d 594; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 2263; 82 Ill. Dec. 950



July 25, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. John J. Crowley, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of theft, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 16-1(a)(1) (1983). The State filed a petition confessing error on defendant's contention that he was denied his right to a bench trial. Based on its confession of error, the State filed a motion to vacate defendant's conviction and sentence for theft and remand the case for a new trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty of theft and he was sentenced to seven years in the Illinois Department of Corrections. Although defendant had filed a jury demand, at the time the case was called for trial he chose to waive a jury and he requested a bench trial. The trial judge denied defendant's request. Plainly, the trial court erred when it denied defendant a bench trial because the request was made before the commencement of trial. The court reversed the theft conviction and remanded for a new trial. The court chose to publish the opinion to condemn the State's practice of using preemptory challenges to exclude all of the available black jurors who were questioned during the voir dire proceedings. Thus, defendant, who was black, was tried and convicted by an all-white jury of the theft of a white woman's purse. The court also found that the evidence at trial was sufficient for the trier of fact to conclude that defendant was guilty beyond a reasonable doubt. The court considered the sufficiency of the evidence admitted at trial to remove the risk of subjecting defendant to double jeopardy.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's theft conviction and remanded for a new trial. The court reported the case as a published opinion so that the State's unconstitutional use of peremptory challenges to systematically exclude blacks from the jury solely because of their race did not go unnoticed.

People v. Stevens


No. 3-83-0677


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


125 Ill. App. 3d 854; 466 N.E.2d 1321; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 2062; 81 Ill. Dec. 519



July 20, 1984, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied August 22, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Tazewell County; the Hon. William H. Young, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction, entered by the Circuit Court of Tazewell County (Illinois), for driving while his license was suspended in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 6-303 (1983). He contended that the conviction violated his due process rights because the State had failed to notify him that his license was suspended.


OVERVIEW: After defendant was cited for driving while his license was suspended, he filed a pretrial motion to dismiss the citation on the ground that the controlling statute, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 6-303 (1983), was void as applied because it violated his right to due process. The court affirmed the circuit court's denial of the motion and found that the statute was valid because due process did not require the State to give him actual notice that his license was suspended in order to convict him. In its ruling, the court found that the offense involved absolute liability and that conviction required only proof that defendant drove in violation of the statute at the time his license was suspended. His actual receipt of notice or knowledge of suspension was immaterial to the offense. Because he failed to provide supporting authority, the court declined to address his related argument that the State's certification of proper notice established a rebuttable presumption of such notice. In addition, the record was incomplete on the issue of whether the circuit court excluded testimony as irrelevant evidence of actual notice or as irrelevant evidence of statutory notice.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction.

Azzone v. Bricco


No. 2-83-0940


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


125 Ill. App. 3d 818; 466 N.E.2d 671; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 2057; 81 Ill. Dec. 85



July 19, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County; the Hon. Emilio Santi, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff mother sought review of the judgment from the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois) that granted defendant father's motion to dismiss the mother's complaint to establish paternity and enforce support against the father on the basis that the cause was barred by the statutory two-year limitations period as set forth by Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 40, para. 1354 (1983).


OVERVIEW: The mother filed a suit against the father that sought to establish paternity and enforce support against the father of a child born out of wedlock. The father moved to dismiss the complaint on the ground that it was not filed within the two-year statutory time limit. The trial court granted the motion and on review the issue was whether the two-year time limit for bringing a paternity action as provided in Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 40, para. 1354 (1983) was an unconstitutional denial of the equal protection clause of both the United States and Illinois Constitutions. The court held that the two-year limitations period of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 40, para. 1354 (1983) was unconstitutional. Therefore, the court concluded that the two-year limitations period violated the Equal Protection Clause of U.S. Const. amend XIV, and required reversal of the trial court's dismissal of the mother's complaint to establish paternity and enforce support. Further, the court found that in view of its ruling on the legal issue involved, the mother's motion to strike a portion of the father's brief as containing assertions of fact not contained in the record became moot.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that dismissed the mother's complaint that sought to establish paternity and enforce support against the father for a child born out of wedlock. Additionally, the court remanded the matter for further proceedings.

People v. Dugan


Nos. 2-83-0444, 2-83-0452, 2-83-0503 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


125 Ill. App. 3d 820; 466 N.E.2d 687; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 2058; 81 Ill. Dec. 101



July 19, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County; the Hon. William D. Block and the Hon. William F. Homer, Judges, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed a decision from the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois), which convicted them of syndicated gambling in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 28-1.1(b)(1981) in connection with the operation of a gambling casino at a local restaurant. Defendants asserted insufficient evidence, that the statute was unconstitutional, and that the forfeiture order was against the manifest weight of the evidence.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were indicted on charges of syndicated gambling following an undercover investigation, which revealed that the basement of the restaurant housed a private club where the club provided food, drinks, and cigarettes to its patrons free of charge and the patrons in exchange purchased poker chips from dealers at the tables and used the chips to bet at the various games. Defendants were convicted of syndicated gambling, and a vehicle owned by one defendant was confiscated and subjected to a forfeiture action. Defendant asserted insufficient evidence, that the statute was unconstitutional, and that the forfeiture order was against the manifest weight of the evidence. The court affirmed the forfeiture action, holding that defendant was the true owner of the vehicle and had allowed the vehicle to be used in the commission of a crime with his knowledge and consent. The court reversed defendants' convictions, holding that the State failed to establish a recording of the bets and wagers beyond a reasonable doubt because the sale and use of color-coded poker chips in the casino was insufficient to satisfy the recording requirement of the bookmaking statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court as to the forfeiture action but reversed as to defendants' convictions.

 

1150 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Rosenberger


No. 4-83-0214


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


125 Ill. App. 3d 749; 466 N.E.2d 608; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 2049; 81 Ill. Dec. 22



July 10, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Champaign County; the Hon. Robert J. Steigmann, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction and sentence in the Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois) for murder in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para 9-1 (1981).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murder in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para 9-1 (1981) and sentenced to 60 years of imprisonment in the beating death of his infant son. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court found that there was sufficient evidence, including testimony by the medical examiner, the emergency room director, and an investigating officer, to convict defendant of murder beyond a reasonable doubt. Also, defendant's story was not credible and showed consciousness of guilt. Defendant was not denied equal protection based on ch. 38, para. 9-1 not being sufficiently distinct from the involuntary manslaughter statute under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9-3 (1981). Murder required the mental state of knowledge while involuntary manslaughter required recklessness. It was not error to allow the state's rebuttal witnesses to testify although they were not on the witness list because it was not possible to determine such witnesses until the defense was concluded. It was not error to refuse to allow the prosecutor to be called as a witness to testify as to a conversation with an investigator because it was a collateral matter, and the impeachment value was questionable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for murder and sentence of an extended term of 60 years of imprisonment.

 

1151 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Flieger


No. 3-83-0813


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


125 Ill. App. 3d 604; 465 N.E.2d 1376; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 2032; 80 Ill. Dec. 739



July 6, 1984, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied August 7, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Tazewell County; the Hon. William J. Reardon, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant putative father appealed a ruling by the Circuit Court of Tazewell County (Illinois), which denied his motion to quash a summons served upon him in another state in an action by plaintiff, the People of the State of Illinois, pursuant to the Illinois Paternity Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 40, para. 1354 (1981). The issue was whether personal jurisdiction over him existed where the mother and child were Illinois residents but he was not.


OVERVIEW: In the State's paternity action against the non-resident putative father, he was served with a summons in another state, and he unsuccessfully sought to have the summons quashed for lack of personal jurisdiction. The court reversed the circuit court's order, which denied his motion to quash service, and found that the circuit court lacked personal jurisdiction over him because he did not have sufficient minimum contacts with the forum state of Illinois. He had no contact whatsoever with the forum state even if, as the complaint alleged, he had made one payment to the mother while she was in Illinois. The court found that the statute on which the circuit court relied, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 40, para. 1354 (1981), was a venue provision that had no bearing on the personal jurisdiction issue. As to personal jurisdiction, the court held that, where the only connection between the putative father and Illinois was the present residence of his alleged child, there were not sufficient minimum contacts to allow the circuit court to exercise jurisdiction over the putative father. Minimum contacts could not be based in tort because it had not been determined that he owed the mother a duty.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the circuit court's order.

 

1152 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Goble


No. 4-83-0791


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


125 Ill. App. 3d 289; 465 N.E.2d 1371; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 1976; 80 Ill. Dec. 734



June 29, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Vermilion County; the Hon. Ralph S. Pearman, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, who was convicted of five counts of burglary in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para 19-1(a) (1983) and who was sentenced to a certain term of imprisonment, sought review of the judgment from the Circuit Court of Vermilion County (Illinois). Defendant contended that his sentence was disparate.


OVERVIEW: Following the judgment convicting defendant of burglary and sentencing him to a certain term of imprisonment, he sought review of the decision. Defendant argued that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-5-3(c)(2)(F) (1983) applied only to offenses and offenders within the State of Illinois. The court held that an examination of the transcript of defendant's sentencing hearing revealed no mention by either court or counsel of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-5-3(c)(2)(F) (1983). It was reasoned that the statute itself contained no language which indicated that a differentiation existed between offenses committed in Illinois and elsewhere. Further, the court held that as the record stood, defendant had a prior conviction of a Class 1 felony within 10 years of the instant offense, and his accomplice had only a bare statement in a presentence report, prepared by a layman, indicating some offense in Canada for which he received a prison sentence. Thus, it concluded that it was the burden of a defendant, when arguing disparate sentences, to produce a record upon which a rational comparison could be made.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment convicting defendant of burglary and sentencing him to a certain term of imprisonment.

People v. Reed


No. 4-83-0789


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


125 Ill. App. 3d 319; 465 N.E.2d 1040; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 1983; 80 Ill. Dec. 694



June 29, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Sangamon County; the Hon. Jerry S. Rhodes, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions, as entered by the Circuit Court of Sangamon County (Illinois), for the offenses of armed robbery in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 18-2 (1981) and attempt murder, under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, paras. 8-4, 9-1 (1981).


OVERVIEW: The trial court convicted and sentenced defendant to a single sentence for armed robbery and attempt murder. He argued that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 2-7(6)(a) (1981) was unconstitutional. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The court held that there was no procedural issue with this statute because there was no decision to make. Under this section, when a defendant was charged with the commission of certain crimes, he was to be tried automatically in adult proceedings. The court further ruled that there was a rational basis for the distinctions made for certain heinous crimes that, when committed by a person at least 15 years of age, required that the prosecution be in criminal court, not in juvenile proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence in criminal court.

 

1154 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Isenstein v. Rosewell


No. 83-2419


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


126 Ill. App. 3d 211; 466 N.E.2d 1187; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 2125; 81 Ill. Dec. 385



June 29, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Anthony J. Scotillo, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant county assessor appealed a decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted plaintiff property owners motions for summary judgment and which permanently enjoined the county collector from collecting rollback real estate taxes for several years.


OVERVIEW: The property owners applied for special farmland valuations of their properties. When the applicable statute was repealed, they were required to elect under a new statute, § 20e of the Revenue Act of 1939, as amended by Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 501e (1983), to preserve the farmland valuation of the properties. On appeal, the county assessor contended that the trial court erred in holding that § 20e impliedly repealed §§ 20a--1 through 20a--3 of the Revenue Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, paras. 501a--1 through 501a--3 (1981), and that the injunction was improperly issued. The court rejected the argument concluding that had the county assessor not required the property owners to make an election under § 20a -- 1, the property owners would have qualified for the lower farm valuation under § 20e automatically. The court concluded that the express repeal of § 20a--3, which provided for the rollback tax, left the assessor without any statutory authority for the assertion of the rollback. The court stated that it believed that the legislature did not intend to preserve the county assessor's power to assert liability for rollback taxes under the repealed sections.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1155 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Lenoir


No. 4-83-0859


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


125 Ill. App. 3d 260; 465 N.E.2d 1027; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 1972; 80 Ill. Dec. 681



June 27, 1984, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied July 25, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Macon County; the Hon. Donald W. Morthland, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions after a bench trial in the Circuit Court of Macon County (Illinois) for two counts of armed violence, in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 33A-2 (1983). He argued that the crime of possession could not serve as an underlying offense for armed violence.


OVERVIEW: The evidence at trial showed that police officers entered the home of defendant's girlfriend with her permission. An officer found defendant, who claimed to have been asleep, in a room with drugs and a gun next to the bed. He argued that he was asleep and had no knowledge of the drugs or the weapon, which he contended were placed there by his girlfriend. He was convicted of two counts of armed violence, based on his possession of two separate narcotics. He argued that the crime of possession was a nonviolent offense, which could not have served as an underlying felon for armed violence. On appeal, the court ruled that defendant was properly convicted of armed violence. The court ruled that suspects were guilty of armed violence when, while armed with a dangerous weapon, they commit a felony. The court determined that to sustain a conviction for armed violence, the State need not prove that a suspect had used the weapon, rather, its mere presence was sufficient. Thus, the court ruled that the underlying offense of possession was not inconsistent with the legislature's purpose in prosecuting suspects under the armed violence statute, which was to punish armed felons more severely.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for armed violence in part. The court reversed his second conviction for armed violence, because, as the State conceded, the second conviction was based on a single offense.

People v. McNeil


No. 82-1752


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


125 Ill. App. 3d 876; 466 N.E.2d 1058; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 2068; 81 Ill. Dec. 256



June 26, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Robert Sklodowski, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of two counts of armed robbery, two counts of unlawful restraint, two counts of armed violence, one count of home invasion and one count of felonious unlawful use of weapons and sentenced him to a term of natural life imprisonment pursuant to the Habitual Criminal Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 33B-1.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of two counts of armed robbery, two counts of unlawful restraint, two counts of armed violence, one count of home invasion, and one count of felonious unlawful use of weapons and sentenced him to a term of natural life imprisonment for an incident in which defendant and two others forcibly entered one of the victim's apartments, after having falsely identified themselves as police officers, bound a gagged the victims and robbed them at gunpoint. On appeal, the court vacated defendant's convictions for armed violence and affirmed the remainder of the trial court's judgment. The court held that defendant's sentence of natural life imprisonment under the Habitual Criminal Act was proper because the Habitual Criminal Act did not violate the United States and Illinois constitutions. However, the court held that the convictions on the two armed violence counts were improper because they were both predicated on the offense of unlawful restraint. The court also held that defendant was not entitled to resentencing because imposition of the natural life imprisonment sentence was based on the conviction for armed robbery.


OUTCOME: The court vacated defendant's convictions of armed violence and affirmed defendant's convictions of two counts of armed robbery, two counts of unlawful restraint, one count of home invasion, and one count of felonious unlawful use of weapons and his sentence to a term of natural life imprisonment.

People v. Washington


No. 82-302


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


125 Ill. App. 3d 109; 465 N.E.2d 666; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 1958; 80 Ill. Dec. 554



June 21, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Robert Sklodowski, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of murder under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9-1(a) (1979), and armed violence in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 33A-2 (1979). Defendant asserted that the State failed to proved guilt beyond a reasonable doubt, that the habitual criminal statute was unconstitutional, and that the trial judge violated the habitual offender statute.


OVERVIEW: Defendant entered a restaurant and became involved in a scuffle with the security guard. Other employees ran for cover, but they testified that they heard gunshots; after the police arrived, the security guard was found dead on the floor, and defendant fired shots at the officers. He was convicted of murder and armed violence. On appeal, defendant asserted that the State failed to proved his guilt beyond a reasonable doubt, that the habitual criminal statute was unconstitutional, and that the trial judge violated the habitual offender statute. The court affirmed defendant's murder conviction, but it reversed his armed violence conviction, holding that the armed violence conviction was intended only to enhance the minimum penalty upon conviction of a felony when the violator was in possession of a weapon while committing the felony, and in defendant's case, the purpose of the statute was not fulfilled because defendant's penalty could not be further enhanced. The court held that there was sufficient evidence to convict defendant of murder; the trial court properly invoked the habitual criminal statute because defendant was previously convicted of attempted murder and armed robbery.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's murder conviction and reversed his conviction for armed violence.

People v. Tobias


No. 82-2162


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


125 Ill. App. 3d 234; 465 N.E.2d 608; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 1970; 80 Ill. Dec. 496



June 19, 1984, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied July 12, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Robert Sklodowski, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him for armed robbery, aggravated kidnapping and deviate sexual assault and sentenced him to life in prison as an habitual offender under the Habitual Criminal Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 33B-1 et seq. (1981).


OVERVIEW: Police stopped defendant during a search for three men who had abandoned a stolen car. An investigatory search of turned up a gun holster and a gun was found in the back seat of the car he had been sitting in. Defendant was arrested and the victim later identified him as the man who had attacked her. Defendant was convicted and sentenced to life in prison under the Act as an habitual offender. Defendant contested the admission of evidence from his arrest and the constitutionality of the Act. The court affirmed defendant's conviction and found that the existence of defendant and two other men in close proximity to an abandoned stolen vehicle and a radio report concerning three men fleeing on foot from the stolen vehicle was sufficient information to justify an investigatory stop. Discovery of the gun holster justified a search of the car where the gun was found in plain view. The court also found that the state's failure to notify defendant that he was to be sentenced as a recidivist until the day of sentencing did not violate due process because the petition to sentence defendant under the Act was read to him in open court and he was given a chance to reply to the charges.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for armed robbery, aggravated kidnapping, and deviate sexual assault, and his sentence of life imprisonment as an habitual offender.

Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant City of Chicago appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted plaintiff utility company's action to have the city's Winter Gas Termination and Reconnection Ordinance, Chicago, Ill., Mun. Code ch. 187.1 (1983), declared invalid and for a permanent injunction.


OVERVIEW: The trial court held the ordinance unconstitutional as it was pre-empted by the Illinois Public Utilities Act. Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111 2/3, para. 1 et seq. (1983).
