Oak Lawn v. Rosewell


No. 83-1895


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


128 Ill. App. 3d 639; 471 N.E.2d 203; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 2472; 83 Ill. Dec. 904



June 12, 1984, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Modified on Denial of Rehearing December 4, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. George A. Higgins, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant village challenged the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted appellee treasurer's motion to dismiss an action challenging the constitutionality of a statute which authorized the collection of a penalty on delinquent real estate taxes and the payment of those penalties collected into the county treasury.


OVERVIEW: On review, the court affirmed. The court found that the challenged payments were penalties which were not for the purpose of generating additional tax revenues for the taxing bodies, but rather, to aid in the administration of tax collections by the county, the entity charged with the duty of collecting such taxes. The court determined that, as such, the penalties were clearly distinguishable from those "fees" which were prohibited by Ill. Const. art. VII, § 9(a). Moreover, because the delinquency penalty constituted a separate charge to the individual taxpayer, the court found that it did not constitute the type of "hidden county tax" or "unlawful skim off" which § 9(a) was designed to circumvent. The court concluded that the village failed to meet its burden of establishing that the challenged statute was clearly unreasonable and palpably arbitrary.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of dismissal.

 

1161 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Smith


No. 82-2459


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


124 Ill. App. 3d 805; 465 N.E.2d 101; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 1900; 80 Ill. Dec. 310



June 7, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Francis J. Mahon, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part and vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court, Cook County (Illinois), finding him of guilty but mentally ill under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 115-4(j)(1981) for the charge of murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with murder. Defendant was found guilty of the charge but mentally ill pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 115-4(j)(1981). Defendant appealed, arguing that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 115-4(j)(1981) violated the ex post facto clause because the statute was passed after the offense was committed. The court ruled that in order for a law to be ex post facto it must materially alter the legal situation of the accused to his disadvantage. Further, the court held that to disadvantage defendant the statute must punish as a crime an act which was previously lawful, increase the penalty for the crime, or deprive one charged with a crime of any defense available according to the law at the time when the act was committed. The court affirmed in part, vacated in part, and remanded the judgment, concluding that while defendant could be correct in maintaining that he was stigmatized by the adjudication of mental illness, that his potential ability to retain custody of a child was impaired, and that the probability of his future commitment to a mental hospital was increased, these findings did not materially alter the legal situation to his disadvantage.


OUTCOME: The judgment convicting defendant was affirmed in part, vacated in part, and remanded.

Yount v. Hesston Corp.


No. 83-803


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District

1163 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Weisberg v. Royal Ins. Co.


No. 83-2240


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


124 Ill. App. 3d 864; 464 N.E.2d 1170; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 1906; 80 Ill. Dec. 187



June 1, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Thomas J. O'Brien, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs insureds sought recovery from defendant insurer under a homeowner's policy for a theft loss. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) dismissed the action as time-barred on the basis that the tolling provision of § 143.1 of the Illinois Insurance Code, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 73, para. 755.1 (1981), was inapplicable to insurance policies entered into before its effective date. The insureds sought review.


OVERVIEW: The insureds claimed that the lower court erred in holding that § 143.1 was inapplicable and that their claim was thus properly dismissed as time-barred. The insureds argued that a statutory amendment affecting only procedures or remedies could be applied retroactively. The court rejected this claim and affirmed the lower court's judgment. The court found that § 143.1 tolled the running of the period for filing an action on an insurance policy from the date a proof of loss was filed until the date the claim was denied. The court further found that that the parties' insurance policy was entered into prior to the effective date of § 143.1. The court held that statutes could not be applied retrospectively if they would either impair the obligation of contracts or interfere with vested rights and that statutes that served to alter a contractual limitation period were not exempt from this rule. The court further held that § 143.1, which extended the parties' contractual limitation period, constituted an impairment of the obligations of the parties' contract, and interfered with the insurer's vested rights. Thus, the court affirmed that § 143.1 could only be applied prospectively.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's judgment that dismissed the insured's action as time-barred.

 

1164 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Graven


No. 4-83-0725


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


124 Ill. App. 3d 990; 464 N.E.2d 1132; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 1922; 80 Ill. Dec. 149



May 30, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Moultrie County; the Hon. Worthy B. Kranz, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from an order from the Circuit Court of Moultrie County (Illinois), which found defendant guilty of the offenses of driving while the alcohol concentration in his breath was .10 or more in violation of the Illinois Vehicle Code (Code), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 11-501(a)(1) (Supp. 1982), and unlawfully transporting alcoholic liquor in violation of the Code, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95, para. 11-502 (1981).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of two alcohol related charges, from which he appealed. On appeal, the court affirmed the convictions. The court held that when §§ 11-501(a)(1) and 11-501.2(a)(5) of the Code were read together, the term "breath units" was sufficiently defined for a person of common intelligence. The court found that the state produced evidence of defendant's intoxication by an Intoxilyzer unit, which was in working order. In addition, the circuit court's inquiry as to the numerical division of the jury, although improper, was not reversible error because it did not interfere with the jurors' deliberation or hasten their verdict. Also, the circuit court's statement concerning its unwillingness to give an unspecified instruction was not of a coercive nature, but indicated the jury should continue deliberations. Moreover, the statutory context of the two charges and the instructions explaining them were likely to confuse a jury, but there was no reversible error. Finally, the court overruled People v. Hutchison, 46 Ill. App. 3d 725, 361 N.E.2d 328 (1977), and held that knowledge of an open container of alcohol was not a necessary element of the illegal transportation charge.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for driving while the alcohol concentration in his breath was .10 or more, and unlawfully transporting alcoholic liquor.

 

1165 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People use of Bernardi v. Bethune Plaza, Inc.


No. 83-1984


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


124 Ill. App. 3d 791; 464 N.E.2d 1116; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 1898; 80 Ill. Dec. 133



May 29, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Earl Arkiss, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant employer appealed from an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which entered an adverse judgment in plaintiff state's action under the Unemployment Insurance Act (the Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 48, para. 300 et seq. (1983), to collect delinquent unemployment insurance taxes assessed against the employer.


OVERVIEW: The employer argued that the Act was unconstitutional as applied and the circuit court should have enjoined collection of the tax. The taxes at issue were imposed by separate governmental entities, which the court found of itself would ordinarily put them outside the sphere of double taxation; however, the employer maintained their collection was for the same purpose and would benefit the same governmental entity, the state. The court found that the argument was invalid because, though taxes under the Federal Unemployment Tax Act were paid to the state, failure to apply a credit for their payment against his tax debt under the Act was not an impermissible double taxation. The tax was permissible and an injunction was properly denied. The employer's state tax liability was authorized by the Act and did not contravene any constitutional proscriptions; thus, the circuit court judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The judgment directing collection of taxes assessed against the employer by the state was affirmed.

 

1166 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Harmison


No. 3-83-0529


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


124 Ill. App. 3d 236; 463 N.E.2d 1373; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 1826; 79 Ill. Dec. 598



May 24, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Peoria County; the Hon. Richard E. Eagleton, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, and reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court of Peoria County (Illinois), which convicted him of delivery of a controlled substance and calculated criminal drug conspiracy, under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, paras. 1401(b)(2), 1405(a) (1983), as charged by the State, and sentenced him to six years in prison for the conspiracy conviction and a concurrent term of probation for the delivery conviction and also imposed a $ 2,000 fine.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of calculated criminal drug conspiracy and delivery of a controlled substance. The indictment charging defendant with calculated criminal drug conspiracy did not identify both individuals with whom he allegedly conspired to sell drugs. The evidence showed defendant asked another man to get drugs from a third individual and give them to defendant. However, it also showed that the third individual did not know that the drugs would be given to defendant to sell to an undercover officer. On appeal, the court agreed with defendant that the indictment for calculated criminal drug conspiracy was fatally defective because it did not identify the third individual so defendant could prepare his defense. The court held that the State failed to prove criminal drug conspiracy because it did not prove an agreement between all three individuals. The court also held that the mandatory fine of $ 2,000 imposed under section 5-9-1.1 of the Illinois Unified Code of Corrections, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-9-1.1 (1983), based on the "street value" of the illegal drug, did not violate the separation of powers and due process provisions of the Illinois Constitution.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment in favor of the State to the extent that it convicted defendant of calculated criminal drug conspiracy and imposed a sentence of probation on his conviction for the delivery of a controlled substance. The court affirmed the remainder of the judgment and remanded for resentencing on the delivery of a controlled substance conviction.

 

1167 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Chicago Bar Asso. v. County of Cook


No. 84-890


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division


124 Ill. App. 3d 355; 464 N.E.2d 728; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 1847; 79 Ill. Dec. 824



May 17, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Joseph Schneider, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant County Board of Commissioners appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted declaratory relief to plaintiffs, city bar association and four individual taxpayers. The circuit court held that the Cook County, Ill. Ordinance No. 115923 (1983) was invalid and unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs challenged the authority of the Board to enact Cook County, Ill. Ordinance No. 115923 (1983), which altered the County Board of Appeals. The ordinance added a third commissioner, staggered the terms of the present two commissioners, changed the manner of election, and provided that the Board could elect a chairperson. The circuit court permanently enjoined any election under the ordinance. On appeal, the Board contended that the subject ordinance was authorized by the county's home rule powers in Ill. Const. art. VII, §§ 4(c), 6 (1970) and did not violate the revenue article in Ill. Const. art. IX, § 4 (1970). The Board was established and was granted authority pursuant to the Revenue Act of 1939, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 492 (1983). The court affirmed that the ordinance exceeded legislative authority and that the Board did not have authority under its home rule powers to enact the ordinance. The county voters were expressly allowed to select the manner of election of county officers pursuant to Ill. Const. art. VII, § 4(c) (1970). Reenactment of the constitutional provision after it was so construed represented an approval of the prior interpretation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed that the subject ordinance was invalid and unconstitutional.

People ex rel. Hartigan v. National Anti-Drug Coalition


No. 83-981


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


124 Ill. App. 3d 269; 464 N.E.2d 690; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 1832; 79 Ill. Dec. 786



May 11, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. John F. Hechinger, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant organizations challenged the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which ruled pursuant to a complaint filed by plaintiff, the Illinois Attorney General, that defendants were charitable organizations and must comply with the Charitable Trust Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 14, para. 51 et seq. (1981) and the solicitation act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 23, para. 5101 et seq. (1981).


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff, the Illinois Attorney General, filed a complaint and sought an injunction and an accounting from defendant organizations that solicited donations in Illinois but failed to register with plaintiff as a charitable organization under the Charitable Trust Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 14, para. 51 et seq. (1981), and the solicitation act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 23, para. 5101 et seq. (1981). The trial court found that the organizations were charitable because defendants' stated goal was public education and one had registered in New York as a charitable organization. The trial court ruled in favor of plaintiff on a partial motion for summary judgment, finding that defendants were subject to the acts, and issued a preliminary injunction requiring defendants to register as charitable organizations and conduct an accounting. Defendants challenged the ruling on constitutional grounds. The court affirmed and held that the constitutional questions were not preserved for review. The issuance of an injunction and order for an accounting was not an abuse of discretion. The court held that the trial court correctly ruled that defendants had a charitable purpose.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of plaintiff, the Illinois Attorney General, and held that the constitutional questions were not preserved for review. There was no abuse of discretion in the trial court's ruling that defendant organizations were charitable organizations required to register with the attorney general and conduct and accounting.

Adams v. Brooks


No. 3-83-0678


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


123 Ill. App. 3d 840; 463 N.E.2d 460; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 1768; 79 Ill. Dec. 119



May 10, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Peoria County; the Hon. Calvin R. Stone, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Orders affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff homeowners field a negligence action against defendant fireman. The Circuit Court of Peoria County (Illinois) found that the Local Governmental and Governmental Employees Tort Immunity Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 85, para. 5 - 102 & 5 - 103(b) (1983) protected the fireman from liability and dismissed the complaint. The homeowners appealed.


OVERVIEW: The fireman supervised the firefighting activities at the homeowners' residence. The homeowners alleged that the fireman negligently performed his duties and that he engaged in willful and wanton misconduct. The homeowners contended that the immunity provided by the Local Governmental and Governmental Employees Tort Immunity Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 85, para. 5 - 102 & 5 - 103(b) (1983) was unconstitutional because there was a discrepancy between two exceptions in § 5 - 103(b). The court held that the sections did not create divergent and unconstitutional classifications based upon the same government function because both sections only exempted only the operation of a motor vehicle from the blanket immunity provided by §§ 5 - 102 and 5 - 103(b) of the Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. 1981, ch. 85, para. 5 - 102 & 5 - 103(b).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment dismissing the homeowners' negligence action.

People v. Berry


No. 4-83-0664


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


123 Ill. App. 3d 1042; 463 N.E.2d 1044; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 1795; 79 Ill. Dec. 490



May 10, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Coles County; the Hon. Paul C. Komada, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court of Coles County (Illinois), which found defendant guilty of two counts of residential burglary, in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 19-3 (1983), and sentenced him to four years' imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: During an interrogation, defendant orally confessed to two burglaries. He thereafter gave taped statements, in the presence of his mother, in which he repeated the confession. During the interrogation, the detective informed defendant that he was not under arrest and the detective did not give defendant any Miranda warnings. Defendant filed a motion to suppress his the oral and taped statements, claiming that they were not given voluntarily and that his Miranda rights were violated. The trial court denied the motion and, following a nonjury trial, found defendant guilty of two counts of residential burglary. The court reversed, holding that defendant's oral statements should have been suppressed because defendant was 17 years of age, of limited intelligence, and had no experience with the criminal justice system, and, therefore, he could not give a voluntary statement in the intimidating, coercive, and deceptive atmosphere in which he was interrogated. The court also found that the taped statements should have been suppressed because defendant was in custody when he gave the statements and the detective failed to give him Miranda warnings prior to taking the statements.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's convictions and sentence on two counts of residential burglary and remanded the matter for a new trial.

Handley v. Unarco Industries, Inc.


No. 4-82-0380


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


124 Ill. App. 3d 56; 463 N.E.2d 1011; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 1810; 79 Ill. Dec. 457



May 9, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of McLean County; the Hon. James A. Knecht, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, and reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, an employee and others, challenged an order of the Circuit Court of McLean County (Illinois), which granted summary judgment to defendant asbestos corporations in plaintiffs' suit for damages from asbestos exposure and denied a motion to dismiss a cross-appeal. Plaintiffs sought to hold the corporations jointly and severally liable. The corporations' challenged the denial of a motion to dismiss.


OVERVIEW: In a prior action against the corporations and others, plaintiffs obtained a default judgment against one defendant after the corporations were voluntarily dismissed without prejudice. An issue presented on appeal was whether the default judgment in the first action barred a separate action against the corporations, where all of the defendants were allegedly jointly and severally liable for the injuries caused by asbestos exposure. The court reversed the order that granted summary judgment to the corporations because it concluded that plaintiffs had not taken a previous judgment against the corporations that were voluntarily dismissed without prejudice before a judgment was issued against the defaulters. The corporations' motion to dismiss alleged that claims of intentional torts against employers who used asbestos material were barred by the exclusive remedy provisions of the Workers' Occupational Diseases Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 48, paras. 172.40, 172.46 (1981). The court found that plaintiffs' sufficiently alleged that the corporations directed, encouraged, or committed an intentional tort, which fell outside of the exclusive remedy provisions of the Act.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order granting summary judgment for the corporations and remanded the case for further proceedings. The court affirmed the order denying the corporations' motion to dismiss and the plaintiff's motion to dismiss the cross-appeal was denied. A motion to strike portions of plaintiffs' reply brief was also denied.

Waste Management of Illinois, Inc. v. Illinois Pollution Control Bd.


No. 83-166


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


123 Ill. App. 3d 1075; 463 N.E.2d 969; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 1800; 79 Ill. Dec. 415



May 8, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for review of order of Pollution Control Board.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner waste management sought review of an order of respondent Pollution Control Board (Illinois) that affirmed the denial of an application for location approval pursuant to the Environmental Protection Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111 1/2, para. 1001 et seq. (1981).


OVERVIEW: Waste management appealed an order affirming the denial of an application for expansion location approval by the pollution control board, urging that the decision was the result of a fundamentally unfair procedure. Waste management argued that the pollution control board acted in a legislative, rather than judicial capacity by merely accepting a five member regional pollution control hearing committee's report. The court affirmed the denial, finding that the decision satisfied statutory requirements that the record was made available for review by the entire pollution control board, the decision was in writing, and the reasons were specified. The court explained that fundamental fairness did not require that the application be personally attended by the entire committee. The court found that no fundamental unfairness occurred when the adjudicatory function was properly performed by the collection and review of evidence. The court rejected the argument that the substantial negative public reaction resulted in a decision based on political concerns instead of the actual evidence. The court observed that a decision was not unfair merely because officials recognized public sentiment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the pollution control board order affirming the denial of waste management's application for an expansion location approval.

 

1173 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Mazzotti v. Edgar


No. 4-83-0563


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


123 Ill. App. 3d 1058; 463 N.E.2d 960; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 1798; 79 Ill. Dec. 406



May 7, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Sangamon County; the Hon. Simon L. Friedman, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff notary public agency appealed from the judgment of the Circuit Court of Sangamon County (Illinois), which denied the agency's motion for a preliminary injunction to command defendant State to furnish the agency with copies of certain lists of persons commissioned by the State as notaries public.


OVERVIEW: The agency sought to order the State to furnish it with copies of notaries' lists. The State argued that the agency's practice of soliciting notaries to provide surety bonds more than 30 days prior to the expiration of a notary's commission constituted a violation of the Illinois Notary Public Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 99, para. 1 et seq. (1981). The agency appealed the trial court's order permanently enjoining the agency from issuing solicitations more than 30 days prior to the expiration of notaries' commissions. The agency argued that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 99, para. 16 constituted an impermissible restraint on commercial speech in violation of the First Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. I. The court found that para. 16 did not violate the first amendment because it directly advanced a substantial government interest in preventing the dissemination of confusing solicitations to notaries by prohibiting solicitations until after the State informed notaries that their commissions were about to expire. The statute was also not more extensive than was necessary to serve that interest. Also, without question a solicitation to renew a notary commission concerned a lawful activity.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision entered in favor of the State, which permanently enjoining the agency from issuing solicitations more than 30 days prior to the expiration of notaries' commissions.

Chicago v. Pudlo


No. 82-2256


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division


123 Ill. App. 3d 337; 462 N.E.2d 494; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 2721; 78 Ill. Dec. 375



May 7, 1984, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 123 Ill. App. 3d 337 at 345.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original Opinion of December 30, 1983, Reported at 123 Ill. App. 3d 337.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant restaurant owners filed a petition for rehearing on appeal of a circuit court (Illinois) judgment finding them guilty of violating food establishment ordinance, Chicago, Ill., Mun. Code ch. 130, § 9 (1980), in favor of plaintiff city.


OVERVIEW: The restaurant owners sought a rehearing upon appeal from a judgment finding them guilty of violating a municipal food establishment ordinance, urging that the city's warrantless search of food establishments was unconstitutional. The court considered the argument despite the fact the search of the restaurant owners' establishment was conducted pursuant to a warrant. The court rejected the contention that food establishment businesses were not within a pervasively regulated industry for purposes of falling within an exception to the warrant requirement for commercial premises inspections, and affirmed the judgment. The court explained that the warrant exception applied to some regulatory statutes applicable to a single industry where regulations were pervasive. The court found that the food industry was one in which regulations were so pervasive that subjecting industry businesses to warrantless inspections was constitutional. The court noted that there was an urgent public health interest served by such inspections and that there were additional municipal ordinances which further continued the long standing regulation of the industry pursuant to the state's police power.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment finding the restaurant owners guilty of violating the city's food establishment ordinance.

Nutrition Headquarters, Inc. v. Department of Revenue


No. 5-83-0377


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


123 Ill. App. 3d 997; 463 N.E.2d 926; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 1786; 79 Ill. Dec. 372



May 4, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Jackson County; the Hon. Bill F. Green, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court of Jackson County (Illinois), which affirmed appellee department of revenue's assessment of service use tax against the taxpayer.


OVERVIEW: The court considered the question of whether the act of placing mailing labels on, sorting and mailing advertising circulars in Illinois was taxable under the Service Use Tax Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 439.31 et seq. (1983), when the circulars were printed outside Illinois and were mailed to locations outside Illinois. The taxpayer argued that its act of processing the circulars was not a use within the meaning of the Act, that its actions were within the "temporary storage" exception to the tax, and that application of the tax to its processing of all circulars would be an unconstitutional burden on interstate commerce. The court agreed with the taxpayer that the temporary storage exception covered the taxpayer's processing of circulars which were sent to locations outside Illinois. The court found that the taxpayer's preparation of the circulars for mailing fell squarely within the wording of the temporary storage exception and held that where a taxpayer accepts fully printed advertising material from outside Illinois and did no more than address it, sort it and mail it in Illinois, it was not subject to service use taxes on that material which was sent out of Illinois.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment upholding the department's assessment of a deficiency against the taxpayer.

In re Marriage of Hagaman


No. 4-84-0072


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


123 Ill. App. 3d 549; 462 N.E.2d 1276; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 1730; 78 Ill. Dec. 922



April 25, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Sangamon County; the Hon. Stuart Shiffman, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner wife filed a request for an order for protection pursuant to § 101, et seq., of the Illinois Domestic Violence Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 40, para. 2301-1 et seq. (1983). The Circuit Court of Sangamon County (Illinois) granted her request and denied respondent husband's motion to reconsider. The husband appealed.


OVERVIEW: The parties were married and the wife filed for divorce. The parties continued to reside together while the divorce was pending. One night the husband came home and he and the wife argued. The husband went into the wife's daughter's room and began to argue with her and dragged her into the living room by her feet. The husband slapped her also. The wife then sought a personal protection order and alleged abuse. The trial court granted the order after a hearing and denied the husband's request to reconsider. The court affirmed the grant of the personal protection order and held that the testimony supported a finding of abuse within the meaning of the Illinois Domestic Violence Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 40, para. 2301-1 et seq. (1983). The court further held that it was for the trial court, in its discretion, to determine on a case-by-case basis whether there had been abuse. The trial judge had to assess the credibility of the witnesses, the acts and statements described, and the tension between household members. In so doing, the trial judge necessarily considered the potential for further abuse.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's judgment that granted a personal protection order to the wife and forced the husband to move out of the marital home.

People v. Ellison


No. 82-578


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


123 Ill. App. 3d 615; 463 N.E.2d 175; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 1738; 79 Ill. Dec. 37



April 24, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County; the Hon. Robert K. McQueen, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction after a jury trial in the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois) on charges of home invasion and rape in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 12-11, 11-1(a)(1) (1981).


OVERVIEW: With his brother-in-law, defendant approached a woman in a car and flashed a badge, pretending to be a police officer. Later that night, the brother-in-law presented the badge to gain entry to another woman's apartment, where he and defendant raped the woman. After trial, defendant was convicted on charges of home invasion and rape. On appeal, the court vacated the home invasion conviction because the information charging defendant did not specifically allege an essential element of the offense that defendant entered the victim's apartment "without authority," which rendered the information fatally defective. The court affirmed defendant's conviction on the rape charge, holding that: (1) the rape shield law, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 115-7 (1981), prohibited testimony concerning the victim's prior sexual activity or reputation because the public policy interest in the law outweighed defendant's right of confrontation; (2) testimony concerning defendant's earlier impersonation of a police officer was properly admitted to negate the existence of innocent intent; (3) the evidence was not so unreasonably improbable that there was a reasonable doubt as to defendant's guilt.


OUTCOME: The court vacated defendant's conviction on a charge of home invasion and affirmed his conviction on a charge of rape.

People v. Pettigrew


No. 4-83-0743


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


123 Ill. App. 3d 649; 462 N.E.2d 1273; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 1741; 78 Ill. Dec. 919



April 24, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Champaign County; the Hon. Robert J. Steigmann, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois), which convicted defendant of two counts of armed robbery and sentenced him as an habitual offender to life imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: After a jury found defendant guilty of two counts of armed robbery, the state filed a verified statement advising the trial court that defendant had been twice convicted previously of armed robbery and thus was eligible for a life sentence under the Habitual Offender Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 33B-1. The trial court, finding that defendant now had the requisite three convictions, sentenced defendant to life imprisonment. Defendant sought review, claiming that the Act was unconstitutional because it violated separation of powers principles and impermissibly infringed on the trial court's sentencing power. On appeal, the court rejected defendant's claim. The court held that the state's power to petition the court to invoke the sanctions of the Act was not the power to sentence. The court also held that under the Act, the power to sentence still remained with the trial court. The court concluded that the Act was clearly constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1179 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Frazier


No. 4-83-0204


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


123 Ill. App. 3d 563; 463 N.E.2d 165; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 1732; 79 Ill. Dec. 27



April 19, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Champaign County; the Hon. John G. Townsend, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois), which convicted him of driving while under the influence of alcohol and sentenced him to 300 days of imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant argued that the results of his breath test should not have been used at trial and that the jury received misleading instructions on the subject of intoxication. Upon review, the court concluded that no reversible error occurred and that defendant was proven guilty of the offense. Defendant's initial refusal to take the test was of no consequence once he completed the test. Defendant's decision to submit to the test was made freely and voluntarily. The officer merely advised defendant to think carefully about what he wanted to do and gave defendant some time to reflect. Whatever error occurred pertaining to the jury instructions was harmless. Defendant's own testimony showed that he consumed a fair amount of alcohol in the several hours preceding the accident. The officers believed that defendant was under the influence of alcohol when they took him from his car, and their later observations bore that out. The results of the breath test showed a relatively high blood-alcohol concentration. Therefore, any error emanating from the presumption instruction was harmless beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence for driving under the influence of alcohol, and held that the trial court properly admitted the results of defendant's breath test.

State Farm Mut. Auto. Ins. Co. v. Palmer


Nos. 3-83-0163, 3-83-0177, 3-83-0268, 3-83-0188, 3-83-0308 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


123 Ill. App. 3d 674; 463 N.E.2d 129; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 1745; 78 Ill. Dec. 951



April 16, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Tazewell County; the Hon. John A. Gorman and the Hon. Stephen J. Covey, Judges, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In the consolidated appeal of five cases arising from an automobile accident, appellants, husband, wife, and township challenged an order of the Circuit Court of Tazewell County (Illinois), which determined that the wife's auto insurance policy provided no coverage to the husband. The trial court granted summary judgment for the husband in the wife's negligence action against him, but denied it as to an intentional tort action by the wife.


OVERVIEW: The husband and wife engaged in an altercation while the husband was driving a vehicle insured by the wife's insurer. The husband and wife were injured in a subsequent car accident. The wife brought a suit against the husband for negligence and battery, later amended to include the township in which the accident took place. The township filed a countersuit against the husband for indemnity and contribution and the insurer filed a suit against the wife, husband, and township for declaratory judgment. The trial court granted summary judgment for the husband on the negligence charge, denied summary judgment as to the battery charge, and found that the wife's insurance policy afforded no protection to the husband. The wife, husband, and insurer appealed, and the court affirmed, holding that the negligence action was barred by the interspousal immunity in Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 40, para. 1001 (1981) because the tort was committed during marriage. The intentional tort was not barred because intentional torts against a spouse were excluded from the bar by 1982 Ill. Laws 288, which the court found was properly applied retroactively.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order, which determined that the wife's auto insurance policy provided no coverage to the husband. The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment for the husband in the wife's negligence action against him, and the denial of summary judgment for the husband in the wife's battery action against him.

People v. Paden


No. 82-914


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


123 Ill. App. 3d 514; 462 N.E.2d 989; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 1724; 78 Ill. Dec. 870



April 13, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County; the Hon. John Bowman, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), which convicted defendant of attempt armed robbery in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 8 -- 4(a) (1981) and armed violence in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 33A -- 2 (1981) and sentenced defendant to a minimum term of six years imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: The charges against defendant were based on defendant's demand of property from the victim while armed with a dangerous weapon, a gun. The jury convicted defendant of attempt armed robbery and armed violence. Defendant was sentences to the minimum term of six years for the offense of armed violence. On appeal, defendant argued that her sentence for armed violence was improper and should have been vacated and the matter remanded to the trial court for resentencing for the offense of attempt armed robbery. In affirming defendant's sentence, the court held that where defendant's act constituted both armed violence and attempt armed robbery, it was proper to enter a judgment of conviction and sentence on the most serious of the offense. Thus, the trial court properly sentenced defendant on the armed violence conviction because armed violence as a Class X offense was more serious than the Class 1 felony of attempt armed robbery.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and sentence.

 

1182 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Dunne v. County of Cook


No. 83-661


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


123 Ill. App. 3d 468; 462 N.E.2d 970; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 1718; 78 Ill. Dec. 851



April 12, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. James C. Murray, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant county board sought review of a judgment by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which ruled in favor of plaintiff president of the county board, granted the president's motion for summary judgment, and found that a proposed ordinance was an unconstitutional enactment that was therefore null and void.


OVERVIEW: The president possessed the statutory authority to veto ordinances enacted by the board, which the board could then override by a four-fifths vote. The board approved an ordinance that changed the majority vote necessary to override an executive veto from four-fifths to three-fifths. The president vetoed the ordinance and it was overridden by a four-fifths vote. The president then filed a declaratory judgment action and the trial court granted the president's summary judgment motion, finding the ordinance unconstitutional. On appeal the court affirmed the trial court's decision. The court held that the proposed ordinance attempted to transfer power from the executive branch to the legislative branch of the county. The court found that by attempting to change the pattern set by the legislature which defined the relative powers between the executive and legislative branches of county government the board's action constituted a change in the form of government under Ill. Const. art. VII, § 6(f). The court stated that such a change in the form government could only be accomplished by a referendum, which was not conducted, and that the ordinance as enacted was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court granting the president's motion for summary judgment and finding that the proposed ordinance was an unconstitutional enactment and therefore null and void.

 

1183 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Brownell


No. 82-155


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


123 Ill. App. 3d 307; 462 N.E.2d 936; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 1701; 78 Ill. Dec. 817



April 11, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County; the Hon. David F. Smith, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the order of the Circuit Court of Winnebago County (Illinois), which, on remand from an earlier appeal, convicted him following a bench trial of rape, attempted murder, aggravated kidnapping, armed robbery, and armed violence, in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 11-1, 8-4, 10-2, 18-2, 33A-2 (1977), and sentenced him to 50 to 150 years for each offense.


OVERVIEW: Following a round of appeals, defendant was convicted of the abduction at gunpoint, rape, and attempted murder of a woman who was seven months pregnant, as well as other charges. The circuit court sentenced defendant to 50 to 150 years concurrently for all but the attempted murder, which was to be consecutive, and the entire sentence was to be consecutive with any penalty imposed in another county. The death sentence in another county was vacated. Defendant appealed. The court affirmed in part and reversed in part and found that defendant's motion to suppress his written statement was properly denied because defendant intentionally relinquished his known right to remain silent after his attorney had advised him to do so. The court found that the later vacation of the death penalty did not change the conviction because the conviction was considered legitimately as part of the prior criminal history for aggravation of the sentence. The state conceded that the armed violence charge was improper because it was a lesser-included charge of rape. However, the court found that a remand for resentencing was unnecessary because the circuit court considered each offense separately.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the judgment and sentence of the circuit court for the offense of armed violence and affirmed the judgments and sentences for the offenses of rape, attempted murder, aggravated kidnapping, and armed robbery.

 

1184 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People ex rel. McCoy v. Sherman


No. 4-83-0488


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


123 Ill. App. 3d 444; 462 N.E.2d 817; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 1714; 78 Ill. Dec. 698



April 4, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Macon County; the Hon. James A. Hendrian, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff mother sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Macon County (Illinois) dismissing her paternity action as untimely.


OVERVIEW: The mother had a child out of wedlock, but did not file a paternity action until more than two years later. Defendant father filed a motion to dismiss the action based on Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 40, para. 1354 (1981) which specifically provided that paternity actions were to have been commenced within two years of the child's birth. The trial court granted the father's motion to dismiss, and the mother appealed the judgment contending that the statute was unconstitutional. The court noted that a recent United States Supreme Court case considered a similar time constraint in Tennessee. The Court in that action held that the time limit was violative of the equal protection clause. Appropriating the analysis used by the Court in that case, namely applying scrutiny somewhere between the most rigorous and the lease rigorous, and determining a time limit that must have satisfied two related requirements, long enough to have given potential plaintiffs a reasonable opportunity to have brought their actions, and substantially related to the state's interest in barring stale and fraudulent claims, the court concluded that the instant statute was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed and remanded.

 

1185 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. De Wit


No. 81-3019


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division


123 Ill. App. 3d 723; 463 N.E.2d 742; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 1752; 79 Ill. Dec. 188



March 30, 1984, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 29, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Arthur J. Cieslik, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) that convicted defendant of murder based on a jury verdict that defendant was guilty, but mentally ill, after the prosecution proved that defendant stabbed a drama coach to death in the coach's studio.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 115-4(j) (1981) was unconstitutional on its face as an ex post facto law, he was denied a fair trial by repeated prosecutorial misconduct by making prejudicial comments and repeatedly asking questions after objections were sustained, and the prosecution withheld discoverable materials. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that convicted defendant of murder and held that § 4(j) did not change the burden of proof or the elements that were required to be proven and that consequently it did not violate the prohibition against ex post facto laws in the constitution. The court further held that there was sufficient evidence to support defendant's conviction in the absence of the prosecution's comments and repeated questions and combined with the trial court's instructions to the jury to disregard them defendant was not prejudiced. The court further held that the evidence showed that the criminal information files that defendant requested did not exist and the prosecution could not produce documents that were nonexistence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that convicted defendant of murder based upon the jury's verdict that defendant was guilty, but mentally ill.

 

1186 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Lipman v. Board of Review


No. 82-2340


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


123 Ill. App. 3d 176; 462 N.E.2d 798; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 1680; 78 Ill. Dec. 679



March 30, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Arthur L. Dunne, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) issued an order that affirmed a decision of defendant Board of Review of the Department of Labor, which denied plaintiff claimant's application for antedated unemployment compensation benefits. The claimant sought further review.


OVERVIEW: The Board denied the claimant's application for antedated unemployment compensation benefits on the ground that it was untimely filed. The trial court affirmed. The claimant appealed, arguing that the Board's construction of Regulation 17F of the Division of Unemployment Insurance, Department of Labor, was unreasonable. The court reversed and remanded, holding that the Board's interpretation of Regulation 17F was clearly erroneous because it was contrary to the plain meaning of the regulation and because it did not foster the remedial purpose of the Illinois Unemployment Compensation Act (Act), which was to aid people who had become involuntarily unemployed. While the interpretation given by an administrative agency to its rules and regulations was entitled to respectful consideration, an erroneous construction by the agency was not binding. Section 1 of the Act provided that extended antedation might be allowed where the claimant failed to file or report at an earlier time due to his unawareness of his rights under the Act. The regulation did not state that extended antedation would only be allowed if the claimant's failure to file or report was due to his unawareness of the Act.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the trial court's order that affirmed the Board's denial of the claimant's application for antedated unemployment compensation benefits.

 

1187 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Lanski v. American Nat'l Bank & Trust Co.


No. 83-1402


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division


122 Ill. App. 3d 729; 462 N.E.2d 607; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 1604; 78 Ill. Dec. 488



March 19, 1984, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied April 23, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Albert Green, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, the City of Chicago, filed an action against defendants, the owners of an apartment building, seeking to remedy numerous building code violations at the apartment. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) entered judgment requiring the intervenor tenants' to move out. The tenant's intervened and moved to quash the move out order. The trial court denied the order and the tenant's appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found that the building was so dangerous that it should have been vacated and boarded up. In their motion to quash the trial court's move out order, the tenant's argued that they were necessary parties to the action and that the order deprived them of their property without due process of law. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that trial court had authority under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 24, para. 11-13, 11-15 (1983) to issue the move out order and that the order was a narrowly tailored and lawful exercise of the police power of the State. Because the move out order was a valid exercise of the police power of the State, the order did not deprive the tenants of their due process rights. The tenants were proper but not necessary parties to the city's action where that action was brought to exercise the police power of the State.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment denying the tenants' motion to quash the trial court's move out order.

 

1188 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


In re Marriage of Parks


No. 83-635


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


122 Ill. App. 3d 905; 461 N.E.2d 681; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 1631; 78 Ill. Dec. 97



March 19, 1984, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] The Name of this Case has been Corrected May 27, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of McHenry County; the Hon. Henry L. Cowlin, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent husband sought review of the decision from the Circuit Court of McHenry County (Illinois) that denied his motion to vacate a judgment for dissolution of marriage in an action commenced by petitioner wife.


OVERVIEW: Two issues were presented for review: (1) whether the judgment of dissolution of marriage was subject to attack by motion, and (2) whether the trial court's failure to make specific findings on the question of the parties' domicile rendered its judgment void for lack of subject-matter jurisdiction. On appeal, the court affirmed the decision of the trial court. The court held that it was appropriate for the trial court to enter a judgment for dissolution while reserving other issues when the court lacked in personam jurisdiction over the husband. The court found that although the judgment of dissolution was final when rendered, the husband was entitled to challenge the court's jurisdiction by way of motion. The court held that the fact that the wife had moved and was residing in Florida at the time the husband presented his motion to vacate was simply not material to the question of whether the court had subject-matter to enter jurisdiction in the first instance. The court ruled that since the trial court implicitly found that it possessed jurisdiction in the matter, specific findings on each aspect of that jurisdiction were not necessary.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court for dissolution of the marriage, holding that vacatur of that judgment was not required.

Benjamin v. Board of Election Comm'rs


No. 84-408


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


122 Ill. App. 3d 693; 462 N.E.2d 626; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 1598; 78 Ill. Dec. 507



March 19, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Eugene Wachowski, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, a candidate for public office, brought an action against respondents, The Board of Election Commissioners and an individual, seeking review of the board's decision to not put the candidate's name on an election ballot. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) affirmed the board's decision. The candidate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The candidate filed a nominating petition containing 1, 833 signatures. The individual objected to the petition on the grounds that 700 of the signatures were invalid. The board conducted a hearing and determined that 500 hundred of the signatures were invalid because the signers lived outside the ward in which the election was to be conducted. The board issued its decision to deny the candidate a place on the ballot because his nominating petition did not contain 1,379 valid signatures. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that the board's decision was not against the manifest weight of the evidence where the candidate failed to present any evidence that the invalid signatures were in fact valid. The court held that the candidate's nominating petition failed to meet the requirements of § 10-4 of the Election Code, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 46, para. 10-4 (1983). The court held that an argument that the candidate did not raise until oral argument before the court was waived.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment.

 

1190 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Fortas v. Dixon


No. 84-434


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division


122 Ill. App. 3d 697; 462 N.E.2d 615; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 1599; 78 Ill. Dec. 496



March 19, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Joseph Schneider, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff citizen brought an action in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) to review a decision of the Chicago Board of Election Commissioners that overruled certain objections the citizen had filed in relation to a nominating petition of defendant candidate. The trial court deleted additional names on the candidate's petition, and ordered her name not be printed on the primary ballot. The candidate was granted an expedited appeal.


OVERVIEW: The citizen filed timely objections to the candidate's nominating petition alleging deficiencies and improprieties, and that certain signatures were invalid because the persons who presented the sheets of the nominating petition to the signers were not the persons who signed the circulator's affidavit. The Board disallowed the citizen's challenge to certain signatures on the ground that the citizen had failed to properly specify the nature of his objections. The trial court struck all the names where there was evidence that someone other than the person signing the circulator's oath had, in fact, circulated the sheet. The court affirmed. As provided in Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 46, para. 7-10 (1981), anyone circulating a nominating petition had to execute a circulator's affidavit certifying that the signatures on that sheet of the petition were signed in his presence, and were genuine. The sheets in the instant action, that were purportedly circulated by the person signing the oath, were circulated by another and clearly evidenced a pattern of fraud, false swearing, and total disregard for the requirements of § 7-10. The trial court properly deleted the additional names.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court, reversing the Board and ordering the candidate's name not be printed, was affirmed.

 

1191 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Watkins v. Burke


No. 84-327


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division


122 Ill. App. 3d 499; 461 N.E.2d 625; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 1569; 78 Ill. Dec. 41



March 15, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Joseph Schneider, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant protestor challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) that affirmed the decision of the Chicago Board of Election Commissioners (Board) striking and dismissing certain objections he filed with respect to appellee candidate's nominating petitions for ward committeeman.


OVERVIEW: The protestor contended that names appearing on the candidate's nominating petitions were per se invalid under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 46, para. 7-10 (1981) because the signatures also appeared on the nominating petitions for the candidate from another party. The Board rejected the protestor's argument on the ground that he failed to present any evidence with respect to the order in which the petitions were signed. The circuit court affirmed this decision. The protestor sought further review, and the court affirmed. Agreeing that para. 7-10 prohibited any person from signing the nominating petitions for a candidate in the primary election of more than one political party, the court concluded that the protestor's construction of the statute did not represent the legislative intent. Instead, the court found that para. 7-10 only disqualified a voter from signing the nominating petition of a political party where the voter had previously committed himself to a different political party. Thus, the protestor was required to show which nominating petition was signed first and, since he failed to present any evidence on the order of signing, the Board correctly dismissed his objections.


OUTCOME: The circuit court's judgment was affirmed.

 

1192 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Board of Education v. Illinois State Bd. of Education


No. 83-2108


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


122 Ill. App. 3d 471; 461 N.E.2d 567; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 1566; 77 Ill. Dec. 944



March 9, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Arthur L. Dunne, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff school district sought review of the decision from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed its petition to recover the expenses of litigation, including attorney fees, pursuant to § 14.1(b) of the Illinois Administrative Procedure Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 127, para. 1014.1(b) (1981), from defendant state board, resulting from a ruling that the rules promulgated by the board were arbitrary, capricious, and illegal.


OVERVIEW: The district's noncompliance with the board's rules for eliminating and preventing racial discrimination in schools jeopardized its federal funding. The district filed suit, seeking a declaration that the rules were invalid and the trial court found in their favor, enjoining enforcement of the rules. The court and the supreme court affirmed, holding that the board had acted beyond the scope of its statutory authority in promulgating the rules. While the board's appeal was pending, § 14.1(b) was enacted, which provided for the recovery of reasonable expenses from litigation where a party had any administrative rule invalidated by a court. Thus, the district filed a petition to seek recovery of its expenses. The trial court dismissed the petition, finding that § 14.1(b) was not in effect when the rules were declared invalid. The district appealed. The court believed that § 14.1(b) was a new obligation, which was to have prospective application in the absence of legislative intent to the contrary, rather than a mere change in remedy or procedure of the type applied retrospectively. It further held that application of § 14.1(b) was unfair and would not further the legislature's goal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the district's petition to recover expenses of their litigation pursuant to § 14.1(b) of the Illinois Administrative Procedure Act.

Evink v. Pekin Ins. Co.


No. 83-137


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


122 Ill. App. 3d 246; 460 N.E.2d 1211; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 1543; 77 Ill. Dec. 647



February 29, 1984, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied April 5, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County; the Hon. John E. Sype, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, an administrator of an estate, a couple who had obtained permanent custody of the decedent shortly after her birth, and the decedent's natural mother, appealed a decision of the Circuit Court of Winnebago County (Illinois), which denied their motion to disqualify the attorney for defendants, the decedent's alleged natural father and an insurance company, and dismissed their two-count complaint for failing to state a cause of action.


OVERVIEW: The decedent was killed in an accident. The decedent's foster father petitioned to be appointed administrator and for an equitable adoption. This was opposed by the natural father with the alleged assistance of the tortfeasor and the attorney hired by the insurer. The foster father was named as administrator but the adoption was denied. The foster parents then sought to recover from the natural father and the insurer the costs of litigation, including attorney fees, which plaintiffs incurred by reason of defendants' interference in the appointment and adoption proceedings. The foster parents also sought to recover past support from the natural father. The trial court dismissed both counts. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that the claim for attorney fees and litigation expenses was properly denied because it was not related to any wrongful conduct on the part of defendants. The court rejected the claim for support because the law did not require the natural father to reimburse third persons who provided support and maintenance to his child without his knowledge or authority or promise, either express or implied, that such necessities would be paid for.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the circuit court dismissing the foster parents' complaint.

 

1194 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Hughes


No. 82-1814


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


121 Ill. App. 3d 992; 460 N.E.2d 485; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 2723; 77 Ill. Dec. 429



February 17, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Robert L. Massey, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted him of rape, Ill Rev. Stat. ch. 38 par. 11-1 (1981), and sentenced him to a prison term of 40 years. Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which denied his motion for a new trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that: (1) the rape shield statute, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, par. 115-7 (1981), was unconstitutional; (2) the trial court improperly interrogated him about the complainant's credibility, and (3) the trial court abused its discretion by denying him a new trial. The court affirmed the judgement below. The court noted that it had previously rejected constitutional challenges to the rape shield statute on the same grounds urged by defendant. The exclusion of certain evidence did not prevent defendant from challenging or attacking the complainant's credibility or veracity of otherwise utilizing cross-examination as an effective tool of impeachment, it merely denied him the opportunity to harass and humiliate the complainant and divert the court's attention to irrelevant issues. The court held that the trial court's questions were proper, as they did not indicate a bias, prejudice, or hostility against defendant; rather, the questions posed were appropriate to the court's role as the finder of fact. Finally, defendant was not entitled to new trial based on newly discovered evidence as there was no basis for believing that it would have changed the outcome of the trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgement below.

 

1195 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Davis


No. 82-730


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


121 Ill. App. 3d 916; 460 N.E.2d 471; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 1490; 77 Ill. Dec. 415



February 16, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Edward M. Fiala, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed as modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) for attempted murder and theft.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of attempted murder and theft after he shot a police officer who was questioning him. The trial judge imposed an extended sentence. On appeal, defendant asserted that the all-white jury venire did not represent a fair cross-section of the community. The court noted that the trial court's refusal to ask jurors how they were chosen for the courthouse where the trial took place precluded defendant from attempting to establish a prima facie violation of the fair-cross-section requirement. However, the omission did not mandate reversal in view of the overwhelming evidence of defendant's guilt. Defendant was improperly sentenced because a finding that the offense was brutal and heinous, which supported the extended sentence, was based on defendant's intent to kill. The trial court thus relied on conduct inherent in the offense of attempted murder as an aggravating factor. No other factors supported the imposition of an extended sentence. The victim was shot with a .22-caliber revolver in the abdomen and leg. His condition was not life threatening, and he was able to return to full-time employment the following month.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment as modified to vacate the 20-year extended term imposed, thus leaving the 30-year sentence for attempted murder.

 

1196 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Martine


Nos. 79-1406, 80-1853 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


121 Ill. App. 3d 793; 460 N.E.2d 456; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 1472; 77 Ill. Dec. 400



February 15, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Theodore M. Swain, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Vacated in part, and reversed and remanded in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted her of possession with intent to deliver more than 30 grams of cocaine, possession of more than 30 grams of cocaine, possession of cannabis, possession of methaqualone, possession of benzphetamine, and possession of lysergic acid diethylamide.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court vacated defendant's conviction for possession of cocaine because possession of cocaine was an included offense of possession of cocaine with intent to deliver. The court remanded for an evidentiary hearing on her motion to controvert the search warrant because her motion was supported with affidavits that denied each assertion in the police officer's affidavit supporting the warrant. Also, the court held that since defendant was not prejudiced by her absence from the courtroom, reversal of her conviction was not required. Despite defendant's contention that a quorum was not present at the meeting of the Dangerous Drug Commission at which the adoption of the controlled substances schedules under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, para. 1201 (1977) took place, that meeting was not void because the Dangerous Drug Commission's actions were irrelevant. Additionally, the court held that although others had access to defendant's home and often stayed there in her absence, such access was insufficient to defeat the finding of constructive possession of the controlled substances that led to her convictions.


OUTCOME: The court vacated defendant's conviction for possession of cocaine and remanded for an evidentiary hearing on her motion to controvert the search warrant.

People v. Kerker


No. 3-83-0007


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


121 Ill. App. 3d 1072; 460 N.E.2d 771; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 1507; 77 Ill. Dec. 467



February 10, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Tazewell County; the Hon. Ivan L. Yontz, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Tazewell County (Illinois) that, upon revoking his probation, ordered defendant to pay fees for his court-appointed counsel, serve additional time on probation, make restitution payments, and pay the sheriff's meal fees.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was placed on probation after pleading guilty to a burglary charge. His probation was revoked after he committed the offense of unlawful delivery of cannabis. The trial court ordered defendant to pay his appointed counsel's attorney's fees, to serve additional time on probation, to continue making restitution payments, and to pay the sheriff's meal fees. Defendant appealed, and the court vacated as to the order to pay the sheriff's meal fees and otherwise affirmed. The allowance and recovery of costs rested entirely upon statutory provisions, which were strictly construed. The assessment of costs or fees not authorized by statute was an abuse of discretion. The trial court abused that discretion here because there was not statutory authorization for payment of a sheriff's meal fees.


OUTCOME: The court vacated that part of the trial court's judgment ordering defendant to pay the sheriff's meal fees and otherwise affirmed the judgment.
