Hill Behan Lumber Co. v. Irving Federal Sav. & Loan Asso.


No. 82-2023


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division


121 Ill. App. 3d 511; 459 N.E.2d 1066; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 1435; 76 Ill. Dec. 931



January 23, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Rosemary Duschene LaPorta, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, and reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Counterplaintiff subcontractor appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), granting a motion by counterdefendant lending agencies to dismiss the subcontractor's action to foreclose a mechanic's lien on the ground that the subcontractor failed to notify them of its claim within 90 days after completion of its work as required under § 24 of the Mechanics' Liens Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 82, para. 24 (1981).


OVERVIEW: The lending agencies brought an action to foreclose on certain real property against a junior lienholder and the subcontractor. The subcontractor filed a counterclaim to foreclose a mechanic's lien. The lending agencies filed a motion to dismiss on the ground that the subcontractor failed to provided a 90-day written notice of its claim as required by § 24. The subcontractor filed a motion to file a second amended complaint. The circuit court denied the motion to amend and granted the motion to dismiss. The court affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded. The court affirmed the circuit court's finding that the subcontractor had constructive notice of the lending agencies' interest in the property and was required to give them notice of its claim. However, the court held that the circuit court erred in dismissing the complaint because the subcontractor sought leave to amend and it did not appear that after the proposed amendment no cause of action could be stated. The court remanded with instructions to allow the subcontractor to amend its complaint by adding the escrow trustee as a party and alleging that the lending agencies had notice through the escrow trustee.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment in part, reversed in part, and remanded with instructions to allow the subcontractor to file an amended complaint adding a party and alleging that the lending agencies had received notice of its claim through the additional party.

 

1199 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Wick


No. 82-511


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


121 Ill. App. 3d 94; 458 N.E.2d 1387; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 1384; 76 Ill. Dec. 587



January 19, 1984, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied February 15, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Ogle County; the Hon. John L. Moore, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed, on constitutional due process grounds, the verdict rendered by a jury of the Circuit Court of Ogle County (Illinois) that found him guilty of aggravated arson under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 20-1.1(a)(3) (1981), a Class X felony, and upon which he was sentenced to a six-year term of imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: As owner of the tavern which was damaged by fire, defendant was charged with aggravated arson when four different origin sites and the use of an accelerant were ascertained, he was the last person to leave the premises, and a fireman was injured. On appeal, defendant claimed that para. 20-1.1(a)(3) violated the due process guaranteed by Ill. Const. of 1970 art. I, § 2 as an unreasonable exercise of the State's police power in that the only apparent purpose for the statute's elimination of the need for finding an intent to defraud in knowingly setting a fire that injured a fireman was to protect the safety of firemen who might be injured in fighting the fire and that it was not reasonably designed to effect the purpose intended by the legislature. In rejecting the State's contention that the statute encompassed a legitimate and reasonable public purpose to deter people from burning buildings due to the possibility of injury, the court held that the statute was not a constitutionally reasonable means to attain the legislative goal of decreasing the risk of injury because its proscriptions and its severe penalty were directed equally to the innocent as well as to the culpable.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of conviction that was entered by the circuit court.

 

1200 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Johnson


No. 80-1783


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


121 Ill. App. 3d 358; 459 N.E.2d 1000; 1984 Ill. App. LEXIS 1418; 76 Ill. Dec. 865



January 18, 1984, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Post-conviction relief dismissed at People v. Johnson, 379 Ill. App. 3d 1074, 957 N.E.2d 588, 2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 2515, 354 Ill. Dec. 272 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2008)
Post-conviction relief denied at People v. Johnson, 2013 IL App (1st) 111544-U, 2013 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 2476 (2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. William Cousins, Jr., Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of murder, attempted murder, attempted armed robbery, and armed violence. Defendant was sentenced to concurrent terms of imprisonment of 80 years for murder, 20 years for attempted murder, and 15 years for attempted armed robbery.


OVERVIEW: Following a jury trial, defendant was found guilty of murder, attempted murder, attempted armed robbery, and armed violence. He was sentenced to concurrent terms of imprisonment of 80 years for murder, 20 years for attempted murder, and 15 years for attempted armed robbery. On appeal, the court found that the totality of the circumstances in the case demonstrated the reasonableness of defendant's arrest. The trial court did not err in denying defendant's motion to quash his arrest. The court further found that the failure of the prosecution to produce additional witnesses to establish the voluntariness of defendant's confession did not rise to the level of plain error. Finally, the court found that the trial court did not abuse its discretion by imposing an extended-term sentence of 80 years for murder. The record indicated that the trial judge imposed the extended-term sentence because of the specific facts of the case, not merely because he thought that the murder was irrational and unjustified.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order.
